# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 28

## 10,558

10,558

[B"H](#_ftn_1), 5 Tishrei, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Meir Lipshitz, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter with pleasure, and I thank you for the well-wishes and the sentiments of your heart expressed therein.

My words have already been [stated](#_ftn_2) regarding such matters in our holy Torah, in Hashem’s blessing to Avraham Avinu: "[And I will bless those who bless you](#_ftn_3)." This teaches that whoever offers a blessing is himself blessed by Hashem, the Source of all blessings, from His [full](#_ftn_4), open, holy, and expansive hand.

As we enter the new year, which comes upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours for a year that is good and sweet, in both material and spiritual matters alike. In particular, I wish you success in your responsible position, with peace and tranquility, [as the verse states](#_ftn_5): "And I will grant peace in the land, etc."

With respect and with the blessing of *chasimah v’gmar chasimah tovah*.

## 10,559

[5 Tishrei, 5733]

This [responsibility mentioned above](#_ftn_7) is not for the first time, **etc.** — and therefore there must be a clear and **signed** declaration, without any conditions — **from this person** that they will take upon themselves the responsibility to go through **and check all the material** before it is sent here.

**And as is customary** in such matters — there is no relevance to an appointment from here, nor is there any need for approval from here.

## 10,760

10,760

[B"H](#_ftn_8), 6 Tishrei, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

Following my [previous](#_ftn_9) letter for the New Year, in which I touched upon the special significance and directive of **Rosh Hashanah that falls on Shabbos**, in connection with the [calendar structure](#_ftn_11) of the current year, I wish to dwell here upon another specific point. This point distinguishes the current year—and consequently the Rosh Hashanah of this year—from most other years and Rosh Hashanahs: the fact that this year, Rosh Hashanah marks the beginning of a **Shmita year (Shevi'is)**. As mentioned in the previous letter, since Rosh [Hashanah](#_ftn_12) is the "head" (**Rosh**) of the entire year, this concept must also find expression in **all** the days of the year, including those days that are not directly connected to the mitzvos of Shmita (field work, etc., as will be explained further).

***

The [Shmita](#_ftn_13) year is, as is well known, the "Shabbos" of the seven-year cycle. Regarding labor in particular—just as Shabbos is the holy day of rest from the days of the week, so too is Shmita the year of rest from the years, with the difference that on Shabbos **all** forms of labor are forbidden, whereas in the year of Shevi'is, only those labors connected to working the land are forbidden, as the Torah states: **"And the land shall rest a Shabbos to Hashem... your field you shall not sow, and your vineyard you shall not prune"** (*Vayikra 25:2-4*).

Although in many respects the directives of the **seventh day** and the **seventh year** are similar, there is a difference in the primary ideas they emphasize:

[Shabbos emphasizes](#_ftn_14) **primarily** that Hashem is the **Creator** of the world (*"For in six days Hashem made the heavens and the earth"*); Shmita emphasizes **primarily** that Hashem is—**now** and always—the **owner** of the world. A person’s actions must demonstrate that "nothing is in his own domain, but rather everything is in the domain of the Master of all."

In the year of Shevi'is, the owner of a field or garden ceases to be its "owner," in accordance with the Torah’s instruction: **"And the rest of the land shall be for you to eat—for you, and for your manservant, and for your maidservant..."** (*Vayikra 25:6*), and as Rashi explains: **"I have not forbidden them to you for eating or for benefit, but rather that you should not conduct yourself with them as an owner; rather, all shall be equal in them."**

In other words: Shevi'is emphasizes the concept that although the Creator has given the land to man for eating and benefit, he must remember that the true owner at all times is Hashem, as the verse says: **"To Hashem belongs the earth and its fullness, the world and those who dwell therein"** (*Tehillim 24:1*). And in order to emphasize and strengthen this remembrance at all times, so that it becomes realized in daily life, Hashem designated the seventh year as a "Shabbos-like" year, when all work in the field and garden is halted for an entire year, and the owner ceases to be an "owner," becoming equal with his manservant, maidservant, etc. As the Midrash expresses it: **"His field is ownerless (hefker), his trees are ownerless, the fences are broken down, and he watches his fruits being eaten"**—and he accepts this. Thereby, a Jew bears witness that the true owner of the world is Hashem.

The concept that Hashem is the owner of the world with all its details is a thought that a Jew brings out every day of every year and expresses in practice by the fact that before he derives benefit or eats (according to Rashi's expression), he makes a *bracha*—a declaration that Hashem is **King of the world**; that He created everything, etc. However, in the year of Shmita, this matter is emphasized with the greatest sharpness, as mentioned above.

***

And this is one of the main directives of this year’s Rosh Hashanah: It is not enough to remember that Hashem is the **Creator** of the world; one must also remember the conclusion that follows from this: that Hashem is also always and perpetually the **owner** of the world, and this must find expression in one's daily conduct every day of the year.

And although [the](#_ftn_17) laws of Shevi'is are not applicable in *Chutz La'aretz*, [the](#_ftn_18) spiritual **content** and the lesson derived from it are valid in all places.

***

The concept that Hashem is the constant owner of the world and everything within it, as expressed in the year of Shevi'is, comes to fruition most clearly in the matter of **tzedakah**. Tzedakah is a [general](#_ftn_19) mitzvah that is required of every Jew; he must give from his hard-earned money to a poor person who did not toil for it, or to a Torah institution or charity organization that attends to the needs of the needy, etc. The year of Shevi'is arrives and teaches a special approach to giving tzedakah: a) He is not giving his **own** [money], but rather that which Hashem has temporarily entrusted to him, making him an agent to pass it on to the poor person; b) by sharing with others, he justifies what he keeps for himself.

Naturally, the matter of tzedakah is not limited to money, but as [the](#_ftn_20) well-known expression goes: *b'mammon, b'guf, b'chochmah (b'nafsho)* ("with money, with the body, with the soul"), tzedakah in **spirituality** is also required, which obligates every Jew to help another Jew who is "poor" in Torah and mitzvos. Regardless of how precious his time and his strengths are to him—to utilize them for his own Torah study and performance of mitzvos—he is told that he must not conduct himself in this as a total "owner." Rather, he must allot from his time and effort to disseminate Torah and mitzvos among those who are "poor" in these areas.

This is also one of the main themes and resolutions of Yom Kippur: *teshuvah, tefillah, and tzedakah*, as is also brought out in the *Haftorah* of Yom Kippur: **"Is this not the fast I have chosen... to share your bread with the hungry... when you see the naked, that you cover him"** (*Yeshayahu 58:6-7*)—which, in addition to the simple meaning of the words, *Chazal* say also refers to tzedakah in spirituality: to feed the "hungry" with spiritual nourishment, Torah, and to clothe with mitzvos the one who is "naked" of mitzvos.

And there is the Divine promise: **"Aser te'aser"** (the reading of Shemini Atzeres), as *Chazal* teach: [By](#_ftn_21) giving tithes and tzedakah, not only will the giver not lack, but on the contrary, he will receive much more, even to the point of wealth. And although mitzvos in general (and tzedakah as well) should be performed not for the sake of reward, but because Hashem, the Creator and Owner of the world, has so commanded, Hashem has nevertheless assured that it will be **"Aser te'aser,"** both in material and in spiritual matters.

With the blessing of *Chatimah v'Gmar Chatimah Tovah*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10,761

10,761

[7 Tishrei, 5733]

The inner [intent](#_ftn_22) [regarding the arrangement of the libraries] is that when people come to request a book, you should draw them into a (brief) conversation about Yiddishkeit, and so on. And if it is possible to arrange the aforementioned in such a way that there is also a clean and pleasant space for a pleasant conversation, etc. — it is understood that it is good to do so.

## 10,762

B"H, between Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yitzchak Agassi, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

With pleasure and appreciation, your letter of the 5th of Tishrei has just been received, and I thank you for your blessings. My words have already been said regarding such matters in our holy Torah, in Hashem’s blessing to Avraham Avinu: "And I will bless those who bless you" —that whoever offers a blessing is himself blessed by Hashem, the Source of all blessings, from His full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

At an auspicious time, I will mention you, your wife, and your daughter, may they live and be well, at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good in all the matters you write of in your letter. May it be His will that you share good news regarding the contents of your letter.

As we enter the new year, which comes upon us and upon all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to all that is yours: a blessing of *chasimah* and *gmar chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually, and especially for success in your general and personal affairs. And in particular, [may you merit] rest and inheritance in the ancient and eternal Jerusalem, the Holy City. 

With respect and blessing.

## 10,765

10,765

B"H, 13 Tishrei, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter and the *pidyon nefesh* request dated the 4th of Tishrei. At an auspicious time, it will be read at the *tziyun* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Since the delay in receiving Hashem’s blessing for children who are alive and enduring sometimes stems from a lack of precision and care in observing the laws and statutes of *taharas hamishpachah* (*niddah*, *hefsek taharah*, immersion in a *kosher mikveh*, etc.), and since a lack of knowledge leads to a lack of observance, you should clarify all the details regarding this with a *rav* who is a *moreh hora'ah*, with the intent to observe them from here on in as required.

With blessings for a *chag sameach*.

## 10766

10766

[B"H]( #_ftn_31), Erev Chag HaSukkos, 5733

In response to your inquiry regarding my position on the elections for the Chief Rabbinate

- and it should be prefaced that this matter also pertains to the election of rabbis in any location whatsoever, both in Eretz Yisroel and abroad -

[Consistent]( #_ftn_32) with my position at the time of the previous elections for the Chief Rabbinate, a position based on what is explained in several places, among them the [well-known responsa of the Chasam Sofer]( #_ftn_33),

I am opposed to removing a rabbi from his position upon the expiration of a contract term or the like, and this does not in any way, G-d forbid, reflect poorly on the honor of the candidates running against him, just as I wrote during the previous elections.

**M. Schneerson**

10,767

B"H, Chol Hamoed Sukkos, 5733
Brooklyn.

To the participants of the Hakafos Shniyos in Nachalat Har Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, together with all our brethren, the Children of Israel, who rejoice in the Simchas Torah wherever they may be — may they live and be well.

In this year of Shemitah and rest, at a time of double joy—the joy of the Jewish people in the Torah, and the joy of the Torah in the Jewish people—which encompasses all our people from one end to the other and unites them.

There is a special strength and content to this joy in our Holy Land, the land upon which the eyes of Hashem, your G-d (the Giver of the Torah), are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.

May it be the will that there be rest and peace in the Land and in all the dwelling places of the Children of Israel, and may the verse be fulfilled: "If you walk in My statutes and keep My mitzvos... I will be to you a G-d, and you shall be to Me a people... and I will lead you upright" (with an erect stature).

Until each and every one can say: "I have been as a wonder to many, but You are my strong refuge."

And may the prophecy be fulfilled: "You have favored, Hashem, Your land; You have restored the captivity of Yaakov," with return and tranquility, in the true and complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

Participating in your joy—which is our joy—and signing with respect and with prayer for a year of "a Shabbos to Hashem," joy in Hashem, in the study of His Torah, and in the fulfillment of His mitzvos, with tranquility and joy,

**Menachem Schneerson**

10,768

10,768

[B"H], Chol Hamoed Sukkos, 5733
Brooklyn.

To the participants in the Hakafos of Simchas Torah in Jerusalem, our holy city and the eternal inheritance of all Bnei Yisrael, together with all our brothers, the Bnei Yisrael, who rejoice in the joy of the Torah wherever they may be — may they live and be well.

In this year of Shemitah and rest, at a time when a double joy—the joy of Yisrael in the Torah and the joy of the Torah in Yisrael—encompasses our entire people from one end to the other, uniting them.

There is a special power and content to this joy in Jerusalem, the eternal capital of our eternal people, as it is written in our eternal Torah.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that there be rest and peace in the Land and in all the dwelling places of Bnei Yisrael, and may the verse be fulfilled: "If you walk in My statutes and observe My commandments... I will be to you a G-d, and you will be to Me a people, and I will lead you upright (with an erect stature)."

Until each and every one can say: "I have been as a wonder to many, but You are my strong refuge."

And may the promise be fulfilled: "You have favored, Hashem, Your land; You have returned the captivity of Yaakov," with return and tranquility, in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

Participating in your joy—which is our joy—and signing with respect and with prayer for a year of rest to Hashem, joy in Hashem, in the study of His Torah, and in the fulfillment of His mitzvos, with tranquility and joy,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10,760

B"H, 25 Tishrei, 5733

Mr. Tzvi Epstein 

[Russian], and to omit the P.S.

[Free Translation]

In response to your letter of 20 Tishrei,

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that from here on, you will be able to write only of good tidings, in a way that is good, both visibly and revealed, regarding yourself and everything you write about.

It is self-understood that adding to and beautifying one’s study of Torah and observance of mitzvos increases Hashem’s blessing in all that is needed. No matter how good one’s conduct in Torah and mitzvos may be, it is always possible to add more, for they were given by the Ribono shel Olam, who is infinite.

Enclosed are copies of my letters regarding the beginning of [the year], as their content is relevant to all the days of the coming year.

## 10,175

10,175

May it be the will of Hashem that — in accordance with the well-known statement of our Sages — you merit the revelation of the Shechinah in the third Beis Hamikdash. And in the meantime as well — with good tidings and in all matters.

It is worthwhile to arrange for a "Guest Book" to be placed there (so that whoever wishes may record their impressions, and the like).

What is the **financial** total?

I will mention [you] at the Tziyun.

## 10,751

10,751

[Beginning of 5733]

During the last few months, when I would call you on the night before Rosh Chodesh, I saw that, Baruch Hashem, there were no special problems, just the usual matters, more or less the same from month to month.

And it is my trust and hope that, especially this year, which began with Shabbos (rest), it will be **even better**. After all, the Torah is concerned with the money of Yisrael—to spend Jewish money on long-distance phone calls for no reason. Especially since, according to the Baal Shem Tov’s teaching, that **in thought** we are one with each other—we are truly **together**.

## 10,742

10,742

[B"H](#_ftn_56), Rosh Chodesh MarCheshvan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. [Chaim](#_ftn_57) Bar-Lev, may he live and be well,

Shalom u’vracha!

It was a pleasure to receive your letter of 21 Tishrei. Thank you for your blessings; [and whoever blesses is blessed](#_ftn_58) by Hashem, the Source of all blessings, [from His](#_ftn_59) full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

This is especially relevant as we have just emerged from the month of Tishrei, which begins with Rosh Hashanah. [As has been discussed](#_ftn_60) many times, it is precisely the "head" (*rosh*) of the year, similar to the physical head, through which all limbs of the body are influenced and directed. So too is it regarding all the days of the year, which are influenced by Rosh Hashanah.

May it be Hashem’s will that this be so in actual practice—both in terms of Hashem’s blessing for a good and sweet year, and in terms of the person, the channels, and the vessels required to receive Hashem’s blessings in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing to you, your wife, and your children, may they live and be well, and especially for much success in your most exalted position.

## 10,573

10,573

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Marcheshvan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Yehoshua Rabinowitz,
Mayor of Tel Aviv-Yafo

Greetings and blessings!

It is possible that this letter of mine will cause you some surprise, as until now we have not had the opportunity to meet personally or to be in contact, etc. However, since its content concerns a matter that affects many, it is my hope that you will receive my request favorably, especially since it is a matter that certainly depends on you to reach a positive resolution, and particularly because the merit of the many will assist you.

The matter concerns the Rambam Yeshivah in Hadar Yosef, Tel Aviv. As I have been informed, there is a plot of land opposite it, and for some time now, efforts have been made to place this plot at the disposal of the yeshivah. However, the formal permit for a "change of designation" is causing a delay, and now there is a suggestion to establish a community center there instead.

Although I am not privy to the details of the situation or the difficulties involved, given that this concerns the fundamental matter of public Torah study—and specifically an institution of the Sephardic community, whose youth face unique challenges, primarily problems of integration after having been uprooted from countries where they lived for hundreds of years and having ascended to Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established)—they must adapt to living conditions that are entirely different from those to which they were accustomed, etc. They are certainly worthy of special attention, and of going beyond the letter of the law and more.

For someone like yourself, who is well-versed in all these matters, elaboration is unnecessary, especially since I have been told that you have already been approached regarding this. I have come only to support their request and to add my own request, doubled and redoubled, to assist in the development of the aforementioned yeshivah in general, and specifically by transferring the requested plot to its possession, which, as they have requested, is located right next to it, on favorable terms.

With respect and blessings for good tidings regarding the above, and in all your activities for the benefit of our brethren, the Children of Israel, in the mother city in Israel, Tel Aviv-Yafo and its surroundings. Thank you in advance for the effort in this matter, and please forgive the intrusion.

## 10,577

10,577

B"H, 4th of Mar-Cheshvan, 5733

Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 27th of Tishrei, and in accordance with its content, I am replying without waiting for my turn.

In it, you write once again regarding the marriage proposal with Ms. [Name], and you elaborate at great length regarding her parents, may they be well, and you ask for my opinion.

Now, it is a simple matter that the main thing in a *shidduch* is the person being spoken of herself. And since you wrote previously that the main thing is in order, you should conclude the *shidduch* in a good and auspicious hour.

To add further strength to the above, the parents live overseas, and once the matter is decided completely in a good hour, there is room to endeavor to influence her parents through the brothers of her father, may he be well, although, of course, one cannot know the results in advance.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 1579

B"H, 4 Menachem Av, 5733

[Russian], [Free translation]

In response to your letter, in which you write regarding the behavior of your adopted son...

Generally, in such cases, the influence of friends is often more effective than the influence of relatives, especially those who raised him. Therefore, in addition to your efforts in this direction, you should find friends who will speak with him in such a way that he will not suspect that you requested them to do so.

It goes without saying that the living example of you and your husband, in the greatest measure of yiras shamayim, is of great importance in this matter.

Since the circumstances of the adoption are not clear from your letter, you should clarify with a Rav whether the evidence you received at the time regarding his Jewish origin is sufficient.

With blessings for good news.

## 10,580

10,580

[5 Cheshvan, 5733]

[In response](#_ftn_65) . . .

The first condition for a happy life is the absence of constant friction, daily disagreements, and so on.

[Therefore](#_ftn_66) — the person in question must be a keeper of Torah and mitzvos in their daily life, of their own volition (and not as a "sacrifice," doing a favor, [making a concession](#_ftn_67), or the like).

And this is in addition to the essential point (which is simple to the mind of **every** believer in Hashem and His Torah) that living according to the will of Hashem draws down the blessings of Hashem.

## 10582

10582

B”H, 15 Marcheshvan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and pious man, who engages in communal needs with energy and great accomplishments, etc., Moreinu Harav Shmuel Tuvia, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure and joy that I received your letter, in which you bring good tidings regarding the completion of the construction of the mikveh in your community with great splendor, and you also write regarding the *hidurim* (beautifications) involved in this.

While *hidur* is a significant matter in all mitzvos, it is all the more so regarding a mikveh, where there is a need to be as meticulous as possible, for the fulfillment of this mitzvah touches upon and influences those who are born, etc.—that is, for generations and generations to come.

And if this is true in all eras, it is certainly so in our generation, a "generation of orphans," and especially when there are some who refrain from speaking about this for various strange reasons—therefore, the obligation is even greater to publicize the immense necessity of the matter of *taharas hamishpachah*, etc.

There is a special possibility and merit for the city of Miami in this, for since people come there from many towns and countries during several seasons of the year, any mitzvah matter that is done there with *hidur* and appropriate publicity is not only good for the city, its permanent residents, and the visitors themselves, but it subsequently has a vast and far-reaching influence through the visitors and guests when they return to their own places.

May it be Hashem’s will that the opening be at a good and successful time, and may the mikveh fulfill its role completely—to spread the observance of the mitzvah of *taharah* in Miami and its surroundings.

May it be Hashem’s will that very soon we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy: "The Mikveh of Yisrael is Hashem," and "I will sprinkle pure water upon you, and you shall be purified" (and see the Rambam, Hilchos Mikvaos, at the end), in the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, when "the earth will be filled with the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea."

With respect and blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

I would like to note a point relevant to the day (the weekly parsha of the opening celebration—*V’eileh toldos Yitzchak*) in connection with the matter of a mikveh, from a wondrous Chazal (Baal HaTurim 26:22), that during the Greek exile, when they decreed that [the Jews] should not immerse, a miracle occurred for them and a mikveh was provided for each and every one, etc.

And from the Midrash, one may derive the halachah that a mikveh of **miraculous** water also purifies (and the debate on this topic is well-known regarding similar cases, such as the miracle oil of Chanukah and the wheat that descended in the clouds (Menachos 69b)). One cannot bring a proof from the Well of Miriam, for that is different—as the verse refers to it as "water" (similar to the Mishnah in Mikvaos 5:4).

## 10,583

10,583

[B"H], 19 MarCheshvan, 5733

## 10,584

10,584

[B"H](#_ftn_77), Motzaei Shabbos Vayeira, 20 Marcheshvan, 5733

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregation of Yeshurun, lovers and cherishers of Torah and mitzvos,

May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

It has already been noted that the calendar setting of this year’s Rosh Hashanah, which fell out on Shabbos, underscores the special directive that this year, in particular, one must infuse more "Shabbos-dikkeit" into all the days of the year, just as Rosh Hashanah is the "head" of the **entire** year.

In simple terms, how can one bring Shabbos-dikkeit into a weekday when one is occupied with mundane matters? The answer is simple: one performs the *ovdin d'chol*—the weekday activities—with a "Shabbos" purpose, and in such a way that this purpose permeates and becomes the primary focus, in thought and in feeling, of the actual deed.

This is also true regarding the matter of *parnassah gashmius* (material livelihood). When the entire toil is permeated with a Shabbos-Kodesh purpose—not merely for the sake of a livelihood, but in order to be able to educate one's children and oneself—this is as Hashem has directed in the Torah, *Toras Chaim*, meaning simple and literal directives for daily life, not just for Shabbos and Yom Tov.

This approach and way of life in practice is the ultimate goal of proper *chinuch* in general, and is one of the essential foundations of Yeshivas **Tomchei-Tmimim** in particular. For "Tamim" means to be a **complete** Yid in one's conduct and in one's aspirations, both on weekdays and on Shabbos and Yom Tov. This emphasis was implanted in the Yeshiva when it was founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Rebbe Rashab, whose birthday we mark today, 20 Marcheshvan. This same emphasis was transplanted together with Yeshivas Tomchei-Tmimim to America by his only son and successor, my father-in-law, the Rebbe; and it continues to be carried forward in that same spirit.

Now, as the annual campaign of the central Yeshivas Tomchei-Tmimim approaches, I hope that all lovers of Torah, and especially *anash*, may they live, will utilize this opportunity to bring more "Shabbos-dikkeit" into their own persons and their resources—in the sense mentioned above—in order to ensure the success of the annual campaign and enable the Yeshiva to continue its holy work of educating as many "Tmimim" students as possible, in a manner of *mosif v'holech, mosif v'or* (increasing and continuing, increasing and illuminating).

May the blessing of Hashem come upon them and their households, may they live, with all that is needed in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With honor and with a blessing for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,588

[24 MarCheshvan, 5733]

Among the suggestions for the above: do not enter into arguments **at all**, but rather steer the conversation toward a neutral and calm topic, and so on.

## 10,589

10,589

B"H, 25 Cheshvan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished bochur, a man of stature and elevated character, who seeks the good of his people and possesses noble traits, [R' Schneur Zalman] shlita,

Shalom u'Bracha!

As you approach your birthday, I hereby express my blessing for a year of health and success, for long and good days and years.

It is well known (Torah Ohr 18d) how the Alter Rebbe explains this—a [day] that is entirely "long," meaning that even its beginning is long. This resolves the question: seemingly, what is the point of the phrasing "long days and years," since days are already included in years? Rather, the meaning is that every single day of those good years is a "long day"—that is, it is filled with good content that makes the day one of great length, even to an infinite degree. As we see tangibly, sometimes in a single moment—especially a moment of great joy, [where joy] breaks through boundaries and limitations—it is an experience so full of content that it is without limit.

As is the custom among Bnei Yisrael to connect every matter to the specific time in which one finds oneself, there is a special point this year, which begins with the [fixed calendar] of **Rosh Hashanah** falling on **Shabbos**, and this year is a year of **Shabbos** [unto Hashem]. Furthermore, the Rosh Hashanah for the study of Chassidus and the ways of Chassidus, which is the day of 19 [Kislev]—the redemption of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, and the yahrtzeit of the Maggid of Mezeritch, which this year marks the 200th anniversary of his passing—also falls on **Shabbos**.

[And since] Shabbos is a matter of *taanug* ("And you shall call the [Shabbos] a *taanug*") and rest, may it be so for you and for all that is yours.

With appreciation, honor, and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,492

B"H, 25 Cheshvan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Tamar Somogyi
Greetings and blessings!

Your letter arrived with much delay, in which you write regarding a plan for a research project concerning the Chabad movement, and that you have already been in contact with Chabad individuals in Kfar Chabad, and you ask for my opinion.

Based on the style of your letter, you are surely aware of the statement of our Sages in their Mishnah that "the deed is the essential thing." This principle should also be the touchstone for the aforementioned research—that is, from the perspective of whether it will bring about a desirable and **practical** benefit, and in this case, what is good in the spirit of Chabad teachings.

It is surely known to you that there are two instructions regarding the *mashpia* (influencer) and the *mushpa* (influenced), which seemingly contradict one another, yet both are brought as practical guidance. One says: "If the teacher is like an angel of Hashem, seek Torah from his mouth," and the other says: "Accept the truth from whoever says it."

Now, whatever the resolution to this contradiction may be, experience shows that when the teacher is a living example of the Torah they teach, there is a special and great success to these instructions. My intention is simple, or more accurately, my hope is that in your private life as well, you will be a living example of daily life according to Chabad teachings. And even though, on the face of it, what is the connection to a scientific investigation of the Chabad way of life and so on—the goal, as mentioned, is the deed and the instruction regarding actual practice.

With respect and blessing,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 10,795

[Late Marcheshvan, 5733]

P.S. Regarding your writing about the private conversation with our friend shlita, etc.:

In actual practice, I stated then, at the outset and without providing any reason: a) that in my clear opinion, he should finish this term; b) that afterwards, he should not put forward his candidacy, and as mentioned—without adding any reason **at all**.

I said this so that he would not suspect me of something that is not in me, etc. Furthermore, since it is understood that for the sake of Chabad it is worthwhile for him to continue for another term—and moreover, [it was I](#_ftn_109) who suggested to him before he entered into this matter at all that (if) they were to propose that he put forward his candidacy, he should agree to it and he would succeed—it is simply understood that if I am now saying the aforementioned, I certainly have no choice in the matter.

In truth, I struggled with this a great deal—perhaps I could avoid saying the above. The statement of our Sages regarding a kettle of hot water ([Menachos at the end](#_ftn_110)) is well known—from which one can understand the magnitude of the pain caused. And in general, why should I cause him anguish several years before the matter becomes practical? Despite all this, I said the above, feeling myself compelled (to do what depends on me so that the matter should be as it ought to be, and primarily, for the benefit of the person in question).

To my regret, I saw immediately that he did not receive the words as I had hoped, and he asked me whether I was advising him as above because of, etc. Only after this did the matter of the [reason*](#_ftn_111) arise, which in truth is not relevant at all, and it is obvious that this is not the main basis of the matter for the benefit of all those involved.

[What surprised me after some time, no less than the above, is that from the circles close to him, they spread a rumor as if I had told him to put forward his candidacy and continue for another term. This is a surprise not only because it is the exact opposite of what I said, but because it is a direct and immediate cause to bring upon him disappointments **etc.** And the fact that those spreading this rumor are among those who seek his welfare, etc.—this does not change the reality and the results.]

Since I am writing the above with an open heart and will rely on your understanding as to what to convey and what to withhold, I wish to add one more point: one of the reasons I stated the two aforementioned points several years before the matter is practically relevant is so that his decision on the second point would be publicized in good time, which would increase his honor [etc.**](#_ftn_112). To my regret, in this too, my hope was not realized. May it be the will of Hashem that, in any case, both of them will now judge me favorably, and most importantly—that this matter be arranged as it ought to be, and soon, regarding the two aforementioned points.

**By the way** (for this does not relate to the substance of the matter **at all**): regarding what is said—that the reason and the concern I mentioned, that they would forgo, etc., has no basis—I wish it were so. But as the situation stands now, the concern is that they will forgo matters even more painful, both in physicality and in spirituality. May the situation change for the better—through the coming of Moshiach Tzidkeinu, immediately.

*) The saying of R. Hillel of Paritch is well known: that in explaining a maamar, one is permitted to debate even with the one who said the maamar.

**) And to distinguish, Truman (and Johnson) will prove it.

10,197

10,197

[B"H](#_ftn_114), Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the inauguration of the Chabad House in Paris,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure the news regarding the celebration of the building’s inauguration, in connection with the upcoming Chag HaGeulah, 19 Kislev.

[It is a fitting custom](#_ftn_115) to bring about a merit on a meritorious day—the liberation of our Rebbe HaZaken, the founder of the Chabad philosophy. It is well known what the Baal HaGeulah wrote in his explanation of the concept of a house and the inauguration of a house, regarding the verse, "A psalm, a song for the inauguration of the House."

A house, in its external aspect, serves as a [shield](#_ftn_116) and shelter from drought and rain, heat and cold, and so on.

Its content, "on the inside," is a life of tranquility and a permanent dwelling.

Therefore, the building (and acquisition) of a house requires the labor of man, and primarily, a great blessing from Above, as the verse states: "Hashem will build the house."

This is also why we make a feast and celebration at the inauguration of a house.

May it be His will that this be the case in this house—that it may be a permanent dwelling for all matters of Chabad and the activities of Chabad in a manner of tranquility.

These activities are founded upon the [threefold love](#_ftn_117): love of Hashem, love of Torah, and love of Israel, and are dedicated to the dissemination of all matters of Torah (both the revealed and the inner dimensions) and its mitzvos, especially among the youth, the sons and daughters of Israel.

May this house be a shield and shelter from undesirable influences from the outside—both those that are in the category of drought and strange fire, and those that are in the category of rain and turbulent waters, heat and cold.

May the blessing of Hashem, as mentioned, be drawn down upon the entire house and its activities, both in the present and in the future.

And may this house and all its affairs serve as a [model](#_ftn_118) for many.

May the Holy One, blessed be He, grant them success so that they may perform [all](#_ftn_119) the aforementioned with joy and tranquility, in a manner—[in the words of the verse](#_ftn_120)—"He redeems my soul in peace, for there are many with me."

With blessings for success in all the above and with the blessing of Chag HaGeulah,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,199

10,199

[B"H], Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Rabbi Nachum Lamm,

Shalom u’vracha!

I have just received your book, *Torah Lishmah*, along with your letter. Thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending me the fruits of your pen and time.

It is understood that this subject interests me in general, and all the more so given the discussions in several places in your book regarding matters that were at the heart of the intense polemic between the *Misnagdim* and the *Chassidim* during that era.

However, time has not permitted me to read your book with the necessary depth. Yet, in glancing through it, I noticed that it seems the highly significant fact was not mentioned—let alone emphasized—that the Alter Rebbe himself published only two books during his lifetime: the *Sefer Hilchos Talmud Torah* and the *Sefer HaTanya*. Of these two books, he published the *Hilchos Talmud Torah* three years before the *Sefer HaTanya*.

And even though the *Sefer Hilchos Talmud Torah* was first printed anonymously, the *Chassidim* certainly knew who the author was, and consequently drew the appropriate conclusion regarding the emphasis on the study of Torah. After a short time, the author became known in wider circles as well.

As for the immense value of Torah study, including the study of *Torah Lishmah*, this was highlighted with the greatest emphasis and firmness throughout the entire teachings of the Alter Rebbe.

I do not know if you possess the latest edition of the Alter Rebbe’s *Sefer Hilchos Talmud Torah*, which includes references and the like, and I have requested that it be sent to you.

Since I have heard of other books you have published, I hope you will follow the custom of many writers and authors and send your books to my library, which is for the benefit of the many. This is especially true since, based on the excerpts that have reached me, an important part of your books touches upon the problems of our generation and our era in general, and regarding the performance of *mitzvos maasiyos* in particular—and *maaseh* is the essential thing.

With respect and blessing.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

Secretary

## 10,109

[B"H], 13 Kislev, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah-scholar [Moreinu HaRav] Shmuel Elazar, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I have just received your letter dated the eve of 10 Kislev, and due to the urgency of the matter, I am responding with equal urgency.

(a) Certainly, any [gathering] that can lead to a strengthening in matters of Torah and its mitzvos, etc., is necessary, correct, and good—especially when it is connected to the teachings of Chassidus and its affairs.

(b) Since the gathering is scheduled for two weeks from now, and as it appears from your letter that there are few—at least for the time being—who are involved in preparing for it, one should not "obligate" the gathering to achieve grand results, so that there will be no disappointment, G-d forbid, etc. Therefore, it is advisable that it be called a "preparatory gathering" or something similar.

(c) It is understood and simple that if there is doubt regarding certain individuals (such as those you mention in your letter and ask about, and others like them) as to whether to invite them or not—the doubt should be resolved in the negative, meaning: do not invite them. For since this is a preparatory gathering, there is no room for resentment from someone who was not invited, but there is a concern if one *does* invite them.

(d) For the reason mentioned above, and several other reasons, one should not write that it is under my presidency, etc. [Since, in the end, there will be resentment from many who were not informed about the gathering and the preparations, etc. And as mentioned, there are other reasons not to write what was stated].

(e) On the other hand, even though you will call the gathering a "preparatory gathering," it is understood that it is **most** important that it be successful. Therefore, it is worthwhile to ensure that the participation in it is appropriate, both in quantity and in quality. And certainly, since it is [said] that "in the multitude of counselors there is salvation," you should consult with anash who understand how to ensure participation in the aforementioned manner.

(f) Although it is seemingly superfluous, because of the importance of the matter I will mention this as well: one must be careful that there be no political or partisan element in the matter, or anything of that nature.

(g) As a contribution, at least in part, toward the expenses of the gathering, I have requested that one thousand liras be given to you, but this should be done in a confidential manner, in order to avoid resentment, etc., as mentioned in section (d). And this is easy to understand.

You will surely confirm receipt of this letter, also with urgency, and thank you in advance.

With the blessing of the Chag HaGeulah and the days of Chanukah, which are illuminating and ever-increasing in light, and for success in the above, and fortunate is his portion, etc.,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,415

I read with great interest what you write regarding the emotions of your heart, etc. Regarding what you write about your sense of low self-worth, etc.—it is a well-known instruction of our holy Torah that although the trait of *anavah* is very important and one must be wary of *ga'avah*, etc., at the same time, [one must not belittle the *ma'alos*](#_ftn_169) and strengths granted by Hashem Yisbarach. Indeed, [our Sages](#_ftn_170) of blessed memory said that a single soul in Yisrael is a full world. One only needs to strengthen the connection and the channel with the Creator and Leader of the world, and this is through daily life according to the instructions of Hashem, as explained in the *Shulchan Aruch*. And since the One who commands is the Creator of man, [certainly](#_ftn_171) He has given the strength to fulfill His will and His *mitzvos*.

Regarding your letter concerning the *bochur* you are meeting with the intention of a *shidduch*, and you ask my opinion on this: If the age difference does not bother you, and secondly, if the reason the *bochur* has not married until now is also not [a concern](#_ftn_172), and thirdly—which is the most important—that both of you decide to establish your home on the foundations of Torah and *mitzvah*, may it be His will that the *shidduch* should be in a good and successful hour.

With blessings for good news in all that was mentioned and for illuminating days of Chanukah.

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary

P.S. In our office, we do not write in French, but you may continue to write in French in the future; just inform us in which language to reply to you: *Lashon HaKodesh*, Yiddish, or English.

## 178

[B"H, the days of Chanukah, 5733]
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

There are many interpretations and allusions regarding the significance of these days. In simple terms, the essence of the matter of "Chanukah" is the dedication (*chanukas*) of the Altar and the Beis Hamikdash, as explained in the *Al Hanissim* prayer: "And afterwards Your children came to the Holy of Holies of Your House, and cleared Your Sanctuary, and purified Your Temple, and kindled lights in the courtyards of Your Sanctuary."

From this, it is also understood that, in simple terms, the matter of the dedication of the Beis Hamikdash contains a primary instruction for every single Jewish man and woman, at all times and in all places.

For the purpose of all memorial days in the life of our people is to learn and to act according to the instructions of "those days" — in "this time."

Now, the essence and perfection of every Jewish home is that it be a dwelling place and a sanctuary for the *Shechinah*. And more specifically, every man and woman in Israel is a sanctuary and a dwelling place for Him, may He be blessed. As our Sages of blessed memory taught us in their interpretation of the verse, "And they shall make Me a sanctuary, and I will dwell **within them**" — within each and every one of Israel. This means that every action and *avodah* performed in connection with the sanctuary is for the purpose — its ultimate goal — of drawing down and causing the *Havayah* to dwell within each and every one of Israel.

And since the Beis Hamikdash was destroyed because of our sins, it is through *teshuvah* and good deeds, through our actions and our *avodah*—the *avodah* of every single one of Israel throughout the entire duration of the *galus*—that we build and establish the Beis Hamikdash within each and every one, and bring closer the redemption of the entire Jewish people through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*, who will build the (general) Beis Hamikdash in its place, and with even greater majesty and greater strength.

And just as everything that occurred in the days of Mattisyahu ben Yochanan *Kohen Gadol* regarding the Beis Hamikdash, so too is it (spiritually) in this time regarding the "Beis Hamikdash" within each individual: sometimes the environment and the like rise up against them "to make them forget Your Torah and to force them away from the laws of Your will."

And the precision in this is well known: "**Your Torah**" — the study of Torah, because it is, and as it is, the Torah of *Havayah*, which is incomparably higher than Torah as it is merely "your wisdom and your understanding in the eyes of the nations." "**The laws of Your will**" — the fulfillment of all the *mitzvos*, including the rational *mitzvos*, in their most exalted level, as the laws of His will, solely to do the will of the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*.

And it is the duty of every one who belongs to *Havayah* to fight, even to the point of *mesiras nefesh*, without considering at all that this is a war of the few (in quantity) against the mighty, etc. And in the end, *Havayah* fights their battle, etc., and grants them an eternal victory, and one arrives at the days of Chanukah — the dedication of one's own Beis Hamikdash — to thank and to praise His great Name.

***

Now, among the *mitzvos* of Chanukah — the recitation of the complete *Hallel* each day, the recitation of *Al Hanissim*, the reading of the Torah, the prohibition of eulogies and fasting, and the kindling of the lights — the latter is the first in time of all the other *mitzvos* of Chanukah, even though the miracle of the victory in the war preceded the miracle of the cruse of oil. It is with this that the days of Chanukah begin, for the time for kindling the Chanukah light is from the setting of the sun. Furthermore, regarding the *mitzvah* of the Chanukah light — and the custom of Israel is Torah — it is to "ascend in holiness" and increase the lights from day to day.

The emphasis on the Chanukah lights highlights a fundamental and great principle: that one must inspect even the oils found in the Sanctuary to see if the oil is pure or not. And we are not speaking of oil for eating, but of oil for kindling; and on the face of it, what difference does it make if something impure touched it for a moment?

Moreover, it was on account of the miracle of the oil that the days of Chanukah were established.

This is to say that the primary establishment of the days of Chanukah is to teach that the oil for the light (in the Beis Hamikdash — both the general and the personal) must be pure, untouched by anything impure.

The light that shines through a Jewish man and woman in their daily life is "the *mitzvah* is a candle, and the Torah is light." And with this candle and light, one must be careful that nothing impure touches it; then one will walk his path securely.

For our Sages of blessed memory informed us, "These lights shall never be nullified." This instruction applies to all times and all places, and as mentioned — regarding every Jewish home and every man and woman of Israel.

That the entire conduct of the home and the conduct of all the members of the household, and especially the education of the sons and daughters (for Chanukah is also related to the word *chinuch*—education), should be illuminated and permeated with the light of Torah, a pure light, in a manner of "increasing and going further, increasing in light," until it illuminates even the darkness that is in the entire environment, as is the instruction of the Chanukah lights, which one kindles "at the entrance of his house from the outside." And until one can justly say: "I have been as a wonder to many, but You are my strong refuge," and as it was in those days in this time, that "You stood by them in the time of their distress, You fought their battle... You performed a great salvation and deliverance."

And the fulfillment of the *mitzvos* (the nullification of "our sins" — the cause of the *galus*) and the fulfillment of the *mitzvah* of the Chanukah light in particular, brings about the fulfillment of the promise of the true and complete redemption through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu* and the building of our Beis Hamikdash.

May it be the will that this happens very soon.

With blessings for illuminating days of Chanukah, which also illuminate all the days of the entire year, increasing and going further in light,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10,619

[B"H], Days of Chanukah, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students (male)
To the students (female)
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and blessing!

During this auspicious time, may it be the will that each and every one of you be blessed with days of Chanukah that are illuminating and that will illuminate all the days of the year.

May this be reflected in all your affairs, in the well-known style of "a candle to illuminate," and especially regarding the "candle of a mitzvah and the Torah of light."

This is achieved through studying our holy Torah with diligence and fulfilling its mitzvos with *hiddur*.

As is alluded to in the mitzvah of the Chanukah candle—which we light from the time the sun sets, at the entrance of one’s home facing the outside, and to which we add candles from day to day—so too must you increase in the aforementioned candle and light from day to day. Do not be impressed by the "darkness" that is in the world, and influence with all of this even those who are still "outside."

Until, with righteousness (and with *anavah*), each one can say: "I have been as a wonder unto many, but You (Hashem, may He be blessed) are my strong refuge."

With blessings for an illuminating Chanukah and with a blessing for success in all the above,

**Menachem Schneerson**

As is the custom of Israel—and indeed, the custom of Israel is Torah—Chanukah gelt is enclosed herewith.

***

**Candle of a mitzvah and the Torah of light**: Mishlei 6:23.

**Which we light... from day to day**: Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim, 671:2.

**As a wonder... refuge**: Tehillim 71:7.

**But You (Hashem, may He be blessed) are my strong refuge**: And only through this was I "as a wonder" (as our Sages of blessed memory state in Sukkah 52b, and as explained in Tanya, Chapter 13); therefore, this is stated **with *anavah***.

**Custom of Israel**: To the extent that our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, would themselves give Chanukah gelt (to their children).

## 10,120

10,120

 In the days of Chanukah, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch,

May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

Since the annual gathering is taking place this year shortly after Chanukah, the influence of the illuminating days of Chanukah will surely be felt by all those gathered.

Chanukah recalls the renewal and purification of the Beis HaMikdash from all the impurities that had been introduced by the Greeks, as expressed in "Al HaNissim": **"And afterwards Your children came... and they cleared Your Sanctuary and purified Your Mikdash and kindled lights,"** etc.

All events in Jewish history that occurred to the Jewish people as a nation serve as practical directives and lessons for all times, both for the collective and for the individual. Likewise, what happened to the Beis HaMikdash, "in those days, at this time," has a connection to the "Beis HaMikdash" that exists in every Jewish home, as is known from the precision of the Divine words: **"And they shall make Me a Mikdash, and I will dwell among them (b’socham)."** The Ribono shel Olam desires to have a home in every Jewish home.

Chanukah reminds us that every Jewish home must be sanctified and prepared for the Divine Shechinah. It must not be defiled by foreign influences that are unworthy and in contradiction to the Jewish spirit of purity and kedushah. This is a timely and sharp reminder, for we live in an environment where these holy ideals are, unfortunately, not always held in high regard, especially in certain circles of the growing youth.

There is no better, or other, protective measure against these harmful influences—which have already claimed so many victims, may Hashem spare us—among the Jewish youth, than Torah-chinuch al taharas hakodesh to the fullest extent; a chinuch that gives our children a firm inner hold on their spiritual heritage. Therefore, the Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Tmimim Lubavitch deserves the fullest support of every man and woman who is concerned about the future of Jewish children and the growing youth, the future of the Jewish people.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that on the occasion of this annual dinner, each and every one of the participants and friends of the Lubavitcher yeshivos will renew and strengthen their support to help them continue their holy work in an ever-increasing measure, in order to fulfill the life-vital obligations that their founders, Raboseinu Nesi’einu, have placed upon them and expect from them. In this merit, Hashem Yisbarach will surely increase His blessings to each and every one, in both gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With respect and blessing for much success and for good tidings in all the above,

**Menachem Schneerson**

10,272

This is especially true in light of the fact that the *maamar* "Chalutzu" is among those *maamarim* designated specifically for purifying the atmosphere of the world, which our Nesi'im would repeat in public once every two or three years (**Hayom Yom**, 28 Tammuz, 5703).

With blessings for great success in all that is mentioned, and for good tidings in all matters,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,724

10,724

B"H, Days of Chanukah, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly individual, engaged in communal needs,
[Mr.](#_ftn_216) Moshe Ishon,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Thank you for the *pidyon nefesh* sent through our friend, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and scholarly individual engaged in communal needs, R’ Sh. Chefer, especially as it was received during the days between Yud-Tes Kislev and Chanukah.

This provides me with a good opportunity to wish you and your entire family that in all your affairs—in accordance with the lesson of the days of Chanukah and the Chanukah lights—you should be "increasing and adding" in light. Furthermore, as per the instruction of the Chanukah light [placed](#_ftn_218) "at the entrance of his house, on the outside," may you also increase in light and illumination from day to day in your activities outside your home, namely, in public affairs and in spreading the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah."

I would add and note another lesson from the fulfillment of the mitzvah of Chanukah lights: even though one fulfilled the mitzvah with absolute perfection on the previous day, one nevertheless adds to it on the following day, and is not at all deterred if he is in the minority against the majority, etc.

[It is known](#_ftn_220) that the hint brought in several sefarim regarding the statement of our Sages of blessed memory that the time for lighting the Chanukah candle is "until the feet of the Tarmodites have ceased" (*Shabbos* 21b)—*Tarmod* (תרמוד) is composed of the same letters as *moredes* (מורדת, rebellious)—meaning that one is assured that he will succeed and prevail until every aspect of rebellion, Heaven forbid, against Your Torah and the laws of Your will, is completely eradicated.

With respect and blessings for success and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

P.S. The *pidyon nefesh* will be read at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, at an auspicious time.

I also wish to thank you, as your article in the German-language newspaper came to my attention, in addition to [the one](#_ftn_221) in the Holy Tongue, in which you write about Chabad (it was a surprise to me that you write and are proficient in the German language as well). The main thing is that you utilize your talents for matters that awaken *yiras shamayim*, etc. There is no need to emphasize to you how much Chabad is interested in spreading the wellsprings outward, to the point of *u’fartzta* [spreading forth]. Therefore, I will express the great satisfaction I derive from the fact that through your aforementioned articles—which I am certain you will continue to write—you are taking an active part in this, as the content is surely directed toward the approach and teachings of Chabad. May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of us acts in these matters in a way of "increasing in holiness," as per the lesson of how the mitzvah of Chanukah lights is fulfilled, as mentioned above.

## 10,726

## 10,228

[Days of Chanukah, 5733]

In response to your question regarding the content of my previous letter: It was not my intention to write to you about theoretical matters or about people in general—at a time when there are **urgent, practical matters in your own life**. Among them: It is a **fact** that you were born to Jewish parents and they raised you, etc., and in this, they were assisted by many other Jews. **Everything** you possess (understanding, emotion, energy, etc.) was made possible **only** thanks to the aforementioned. From this follows: 

a) A principle accepted **by all: When a relative** is in **danger**, there is no time to waste—to busy oneself with philosophical matters and wander the world examining which people are the most important to help, etc. 

b) And this is also a principle as above: First and foremost, one must **repay the debt** to all those (individuals, the environment, etc.) who helped you become a person capable of helping others—and only afterwards is there room for calculating who takes precedence in receiving your help, etc.

## 10,731

[B"H], Fourth night of Chanukah, 27 Kislev, 5733

... Regarding your question—concerning study and instruction during Chanukah and its themes—specifically for those in the military, in addition to "Al HaNissim" which were given "the many into the hands of the [few], etc."—

Here are a few points on this (in brief—which will surely suffice for you, as I know you, and as it is [said], "Give to the wise and he will become yet wiser"):

Every soldier stands "[at the entrance of his **house** (the house of all the people of Bnei Yisrael wherever they may be—Eretz Yisrael) **from the outside**]"—and his role is not merely defense, but rather defense in a manner and by means of lighting the candle (his soul—"the candle of [Hashem] is the soul of man") that will illuminate the house and also the outside—[with the candle] of mitzvah and the light of Torah.

And one must not be intimidated by the fact that "the sun has set" and it is dark in the world.

On the contrary—were it not for this, they would not have recruited him, and there would be no need for an army.

This is analogous to the fact that the time for lighting the Chanukah candles is specifically [from when the sun sets].

And one should not be satisfied with the achievements of today, even if they are in the manner of **"mehadrin min hamehadrin"** (the most beautiful way),

But rather [to increase from day to day] in the candles shining at the entrance of **his house from the outside**—an increase both in the light within and in the light without.

And furthermore, to note: [Our Sages have said] that "Yehuda Maccabi performed great acts of heroism with the help of Hashem... Maccabi is an acronym for [Mi] Kamocha Ba'eilim Hashem (Who is like You among the mighty, O Hashem)."

This means that for every person in his battle—whatever battle it may be: in the battle of life, the battle to defend the holy and the spiritual, etc., and certainly regarding battle in the literal sense,

It must be written and engraved upon his banner and in his heart: **M**i **K**amocha **B**a'eilim **Y**'—and then

He will not fear anyone, for Hashem is with him.

Victory is guaranteed, for—[in the words of the verse]: "Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp to save you and to deliver your enemies before you."

There will be peace in the land, for there will be fulfilled in him [what is said] in our Torah, the Torah of truth: "And all the peoples of the earth shall see that the name of Hashem is called upon you, and they shall fear you."

And especially through precision in the fulfillment of the mitzvah of Tefillin—[as interpreted] by our Sages of blessed memory regarding this verse, as I wrote in my previous letter...

**M. Schneerson**

## 10-734

10-734

B.H., Eighth Night of Chanukah, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your inquiry regarding the matter of the custom —for the custom of Israel is Torah (Torah, from the word *hora’ah*, meaning instruction)—of giving **Chanukah-gelt** to children, and what the specific instruction is in this,

And in response to this, by way of introduction:

It is a well-known [teaching](#_ftn_258) of the Baal Shem Tov that everything a person sees or hears contains an instruction in the *avodah* of Hashem. In truth, this is self-understood and is a fundamental principle of our faith; for since a person knows that Hashem is the Creator of the world and its Guide at every moment and every second, [and I](#_ftn_259) was created only to serve my Creator—also at every moment and every second—it is understood that everything occurring around him is connected to the *avodah* of Hashem.

Regarding the instructions of [Chanukah](#_ftn_260), there are simply two aspects: a) The dedication (*chanukas*) of the Beis Hamikdash and the *mizbeach*; b) [from the word](#_ftn_261) *chinuch* (education), "Educate (*chanoch*) a youth", which includes every single Jew, [for](#_ftn_263) a Jew is a youth. This means that just as there was a clearing, purification, and dedication of the Beis Hamikdash, so too must there be in every single Jew, who is also a *mishkan* and a *mikdash* for Hashem.

It is understood that along with the *chinuch* that each person must provide for himself—[and even](#_ftn_264) though "we are all wise," etc., since a person must increase in "the mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light" from day to day—there is the *chinuch* of the sons and daughters, and this with even greater emphasis, as this obligation rests especially upon the parents. This *chinuch* must be "according to his way," meaning in a manner that is understood and accepted by the youth.

From here we come to the matter of *Chanukah-gelt*. The intention in giving it to children is to connect the instructions of Chanukah with the lesson one should learn from money, even through simple *hisbonenus*. For on one hand, money has great power; he who has much money is wealthy, even very wealthy, and he who has none is poor and destitute. On the other hand, money as it is in itself is not one of the three basic human needs—food, clothing, and shelter. Rather, it is through money that one can purchase all of a person’s needs. Furthermore, through it one can fulfill the *mitzvos* of *tzedakah*, *gemilas chasadim*, and many other *mitzvos*—which would not be the case if the money were left in a box without utilization or benefit.

One of the main points in the *chinuch* of children is to explain to them in a way that they will know and always remember that Hashem has given them "great wealth"—mighty powers in the intellect, in the *midos* of the heart, and in actual deed—but that they must utilize them to their fullest. This means utilizing the power of the intellect in the study of Torah, to the point of [toiling](#_ftn_266), for then it is certain that the promise "you have labored and found" will be fulfilled in him. The same applies to the *midos* of the heart: to love Hashem, the Torah, every Jew, and all things worthy of being loved; and to fear and flee from all things from which one must flee. Therefore, one must study with *hasmadah*, *shekidah*, and discipline to know the good and the deed that he should do. Then he is not like the situation regarding physical money—for in physical matters, one who has none is poor, but in spiritual matters, everyone can be wealthy, provided he utilizes the powers given to him, for he is guaranteed, "you have labored and found." However, in this, the choice is given to him; it depends only on him and his will, [and there](#_ftn_267) is nothing that can stand before the will.

When all this is explained to a child in appropriate terms and in words [that come](#_ftn_268) from the heart, and—most importantly—when one shows him a living example, then "Hashem illuminates the eyes of them both", so that both the one who gives the *Chanukah-gelt* and the one who receives it continue to increase in "the mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light," from strength to [strength](#_ftn_270), until it becomes a [miracle](#_ftn_271) to the many.

With respect and blessing.

## 10,335

10,335

[B"H](#_ftn_272), [Zos](#_ftn_273) Chanukah, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letters.

As we stand at the conclusion [and seal](#_ftn_274) of the days of Chanukah, may it be the will of Hashem that these lights shine in their fullness and completeness [throughout](#_ftn_275) the entire year, [in a manner](#_ftn_276) of "increasing and adding light" in both material and spiritual matters alike,

Until we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy, "[And it shall be](#_ftn_277) at eventide there shall be light," [that the night](#_ftn_278) shall shine as the day.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

I was pained, naturally, that your seat was empty at the Chabad beis medrash. May it be His will that this leads to a double measure of good in the future.

With blessings for a complete and speedy recovery and for good tidings.

**Zos Chanukah**: It should be noted that on Zos Chanukah we read extensively from the Torah; we read the entirety of the portions for all the days of the dedication of the Altar, and we read the portion of the Nesi'im. This reading is [considered] for each one **at its proper time**, and it applies to the entire Mishnah (Rashi, Megillah 31a; R' Akiva Eiger). According to the writings of the Arizal, on each day of Chanukah one should focus on one of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy, and on the fifth day, from *Notzer* until *V'nakeh*. See the Maamar of the Tzemach Tzedek, *D'h Boruch She'asah Nissim* (Brooklyn, 5711), end of section 4: "Eight [days] regarding this..." See there.

**Seal of the days of Chanukah**: Even if you were to say that the eight days of Chanukah are a single reality and not separate (Tzafnas Paneach, second edition, by the Rogatchover Gaon, p. 118)—at the very least regarding the miracle of the oil, which depends on the moment the flask of oil was found (and based on this, the question regarding the miracle on the first day is resolved; the Beis Yosef and others resolve it even if one says they are separate)—the redundancy is clarified: "A miracle was performed **with it** and they lit **from it**." The logic is understood that for a candle that has been extinguished, it is forbidden to use the candle or the oil for one's own needs for all eight days (Ria"z [in Shaarei Gan Eiden to the Rif](#_ftn_281), Shabbos, Laws of Chanukah, end of section 5). Thus, the completeness of **all** the days is specifically on Zos Chanukah.

**That these lights shine**: Their explanation in the avodah of man is found in many places, including the Chanukah maamarim of each of our Rebbes, the Nesi'im.

**Throughout the entire year**: Discussed at some length in the letter regarding the days of Chanukah of this year.

**The prophecy**: Zechariah 14:7. See Yalkut Shimoni there. Likutei Torah, Bamidbar 8:1.

**And it shall be at eventide**: The conclusion there is, "And Hashem shall be King over all the earth..." In the Zohar (Vol. I, end of Parshas Noach), it states that this follows the verse, "For then I will turn to the peoples..." and "to serve Him with one consent." See Ohr HaTorah to Zephaniah (3:9) regarding the precision of the word "**then**" (*az*)—in the same vein as mentioned above regarding Zos Chanukah.

## 10,740

10,740

B"H, 13 Teves, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students Mordechai and Nachum Zucker, may they live,

Shalom u’vracha!

It was with pleasure that I received your letters regarding Chanukah gelt. Surely, together with this, you have received an explanation of the content of the days of Chanukah and what we must learn from them—especially from the Chanukah candles, which we light [with an increase](#_ftn_290) in candle and light from day to day.

The main point in this is to know that the festival of Chanukah is not merely a remembrance of events that occurred many, many years ago; rather, it teaches us all how our conduct must be even now. For not only in those days, but also in this time, there are those who wish to ["make them forget](#_ftn_291) Your Torah and force them to stray from the laws of Your will." But a Jew does not make calculations regarding whether the opposing forces are numerous; on the contrary, he resolves with even greater strength to study the Torah—the Torah of Hashem—with persistence and diligence, and strives with all his might to fulfill the laws and mitzvos that are the will of Hashem. And then, Hashem Yisbarach helps all Jews, as it is written in "Al HaNissim": "You fought their battles, etc., You delivered the strong into the hands of the weak, and the many into the hands of the few, etc."

The same applies to the custom of [Yisrael](#_ftn_292) to give Chanukah gelt to children, which also contains many lessons and allusions, some of which are explained [in the letter enclosed](#_ftn_293) herewith. It is my hope that you will read it with attention, in a manner that will lead to actual practice in good and appropriate conduct for every single day of the year.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 10,745

10,745

B"H, 15 Teves, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from 9/12/72 (it is clear that you also know English, but naturally, it gives me more satisfaction that the main part of your letter is in our language, Lashon HaKodesh).

I was pleased to read that the shluchim extended their well-wishes in connection with the days of Chanukah. May it be the will of Hashem that the heart’s desires of the Bnei Yisrael and their wishes for one another be fulfilled completely, and even more so—[as the instruction of the mitzvah of the Chanukah candles teaches](#_ftn_299)—in a manner of "increasing and adding light." Based on the content of your letter, my hope is that this will be the case for you [in the style of our Torah](#_ftn_300), "For the mitzvah is a candle and the Torah is light"—to increase in the study and knowledge of Torah, *Torah Ohr*, and in the kindling of its lights—the mitzvos. [And there is](#_ftn_301) nothing that can stand before the will.

This is especially true since you are in a framework where you can be, [in the words of the verse](#_ftn_302), "I have been as a sign unto many"—a sign and a guide for each of your fellow soldiers, and the merit of the many will assist you.

Regarding the end of your letter concerning correspondence with religious girls overseas in order to learn about the way of life of Jewish youth, etc.: while it is certainly a good thing to know about the lifestyle of Bnei Yisrael wherever they may be—especially when there is a mutual benefit of learning from one another, [as our Sages said in their Mishnah](#_ftn_303), "Who is wise? He who learns from every person," which means that from every person one can learn something good, and it depends only on focusing on the good within that person—

Nevertheless, along with this, since you emphasize "girls," I must say, with apologies, that there is a negative point to this. It is possible that the correspondence will stir up plans and hopes beyond just learning about the order of life overseas, potentially leading to a lifelong connection—that is, a *shidduch*. Since one certainly should not make a decision on such a serious matter based on correspondence, this exchange of letters is liable to confuse the correspondents and prevent them from taking an interest in a suitable *shidduch* in their own environment, etc. Surely this matter requires no further explanation.

Since your current order of life is based on discipline and the fulfillment of [orders](#_ftn_304) without questioning them—which is the foundation of military existence—this habit prepares you (I refer to all those in the army) for perfection and *hiddur* in the acceptance of the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, which is, in its literal sense, the fulfillment of Hashem’s mitzvos. Surely this, too, requires no further explanation.

With respect and with wishes that Hashem fulfill the desires of your hearts for the good.

## 10,748

20 Teves



[Russian], [Free translation]

A very long time has passed since I received a letter from you, or indeed any news regarding the activities of the Association of Academics.

It goes without saying that what is primarily important is not that I receive letters, but rather that this long silence does not indicate insufficient activity on the part of the Association of Academics. As has been discussed many times, it is of the utmost importance—a matter of the highest priority—that there be contact with the academics arriving [from there] immediately upon their arrival, before the concerns of daily life surround them and, as is often the case, bind them and preclude the possibility of active involvement within the framework of the Association of Academics with full vigor, or even with less than full vigor.

The direct reason for this letter is the news regarding the conference of academics that took place under the initiative of Chamah. If I am to judge by the reports and the press, it was a successful conference—further proof that there is potential for extensive activity. Therefore, every unutilized day is a day of loss that cannot be recovered.

I do not like to preach or rebuke, G-d forbid, and the purpose of this letter is to remind you once again of what was discussed during the meeting with the academics in New York, regarding the necessity of broad activity, which is also very important for the academics' own material well-being.

I hope that the record of our conversation has been preserved, and there is no need to repeat it again.

May Hashem grant that you write with good news regarding all of the above, and as has been discussed frequently in recent [weeks], in a manner of "increasing and adding light."

With blessings for great success in all of the above and for good tidings.

There is no need to ask about every detail in New York; in most cases, consultation with the leadership of the Association of Academics is sufficient, and presumably, you will send the report of the meeting here afterward.
