## 10. [Untitled]

By the Grace of G-d
Rosh Chodesh Shevat, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Moshe Avnieli
Greetings and Blessings!

Our friend, Rabbi Ephraim Wolf, informed me that your wife (may she live and be well) is in need of medical treatment. I have mentioned her at the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. It is my hope that the treatment will be successful and that you will share good news. This is especially pertinent as we have entered the tenth month, in which falls the yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

Since you have been privileged to be involved in the settlement of Jerusalem, the Holy City, the Old City, it is well known how much our Sages of blessed memory praised the great merit of anyone who assists in building a home in our Holy Land, and especially in our eternal capital, Jerusalem, the Holy City. It is understood that this is a great and wondrous merit that has fallen to your lot, and you are surely doing everything within your power to ensure that these homes are fitting for Jerusalem and its essence, as explained in the words of David and his son Solomon [and their prayer], until it can be rightfully said of every house: "For... the word of Hashem shall go forth [from Jerusalem]."

With respect and blessings for success in all of the above, and for good news.

P.S. After asking for your forgiveness, I will take the liberty of offering a comment, even though, on the face of it, it may not seem appropriate to include within the letter. It is this: in general, regarding all matters of our Holy Land, a primary condition for anyone living there—and all the more so for anyone settling there—is that their aspiration, and how much better if their current state, should be in harmony with the essence of our Holy Land, which is called "the Holy Land" even by all the nations of the earth. This is especially true of Jerusalem, the Holy City.

I mean that regarding the settlement of the Old City, it is simple that there should have been no place for a distinction between those who are wealthy in material terms and those who are poor in material terms. Even if you were to say that regarding other cities in Eretz Yisrael there is no choice—since we live in a world where one must pay for building materials, labor, etc., with money, and much money at that, and the coffers are insufficient, etc.—nevertheless, seemingly there was room to exert much greater effort so that regarding the capital of our Holy Land, at the very least regarding Jerusalem, the Old City—the city where David [dwelled]—the litmus test should be solely and exclusively spiritual qualifications, without any consideration at all for the material status of the one who wishes to live there, and certainly to settle there.

It is clear that I am not coming to attack, G-d forbid, or to make accusations, G-d forbid, and it is not my way to preach morality for its own sake. Rather, it is my opinion that there is room even now to rectify the aforementioned to a significant degree by having the appropriate offices allocate special funds to assist those who are suitable to settle in Jerusalem, the Holy City, but who lack the financial means. Naturally, one should evaluate what the candidate can pay, and complete the rest from the fund as a grant.

I could have based my aforementioned suggestion on the "theory of socialism," according to which material wealth does not serve as a criterion for fulfilling a person's needs, but rather their talents, knowledge, ability, etc. But, of course, I chose to base the above specifically on our Torah, which was given to us from Sinai, for it is an [eternal] Torah and a Torah of life, given to the people of Israel, who live by the living G-d.

1076

1076

[B"H], 5 Shevat, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your writing about the [event] that has recently caused such a stir among our brethren, the Children of Israel, both in Eretz Yisrael and abroad, and your request for clarification of my position regarding the criticism of this matter—and perhaps something more than mere criticism:

It is understood that it is difficult to exhaust the subject as required in a letter. Nevertheless, I will write down a few points, and surely they will suffice for one of your stature.

(a) That our Torah—the Torah of truth and the Torah of kindness—prohibits certain children of specific marriages from entering the congregation is not a matter of punishment. For the Torah itself establishes that "a man shall be put to death for his own sin", and it states, "The fathers have eaten sour grapes, and the children’s teeth are set on edge!"

Moreover, many marriage prohibitions regarding the individuals themselves are not in the category of punishment. A case in point: the prohibition for a Kohen to marry a divorcee. This prohibition applies to a Kohen even if he is the simplest of the simple, even though she is permitted to marry a completely righteous person, provided he is not a Kohen. There are many other examples of this nature.

(b) As for the general human approach regarding a friend or an important and valuable issue—since all matters are bound up with human beings and there is no perfection in this world of ours, it is inevitable that from time to time there will be undesirable phenomena and even undesirable actions. The aforementioned approach can be taken in two ways:

1. Since the person is a friend and close associate, and the matter is important and valuable, etc.—to cover up the flaws and justify them with every possible, or even impossible, excuse, just so that the name and prestige of the person and the matter are not diminished. This often reaches the point where, out of excessive enthusiasm to protect that prestige, the person involved begins to believe himself that this is indeed the truth of the matter, even though at first he knew in his soul [that he is calling evil good and bitter sweet]. He simply felt it was his duty to defend his friend or the thing dear to him.

2. Not to distort the situation—in the terminology used above, not to call evil good and bitter sweet—but rather to strive to find the cause of the undesirable phenomenon and to endeavor as much as possible to correct that cause. Consequently, there will be no place for undesirable phenomena, even if the prestige is temporarily damaged. Furthermore, someone may come along and accuse the person who takes this approach of not being a friend, or that the matter is not dear to him, etc.

In my clear opinion, founded upon what has already occurred in such cases in previous generations, the first approach mentioned above yields an illusory reward and a great loss. For ultimately, the truth will be revealed—that evil is evil and bitter is bitter. Consequently, not only is the defense nullified, but since trust in the defender has been lost, he is no longer believed even when he defends with sound and truthful arguments.

Another point in this regard, and this is the main thing, is that the first approach precludes the effort to correct what is wrong, or at the very least weakens this effort. This is especially true when one comes with a quiet argument that the wrong must indeed be corrected, for then the ready response is: "But you yourself previously declared with a loud voice that this was a great achievement, a great salvation, and good beyond compare?" That is to say, at the price of a temporary salvation of external prestige, one diminishes the possibility of correcting what requires correction, or even precludes it entirely.

To what is this comparable? To a patient suffering from a mild illness for the time being, and the doctor tells him that he needs treatment to recover, otherwise his illness is liable to become critical. But the patient’s relatives announce and inform the whole world, including the patient himself, that he is in perfect health, and that his symptoms of illness are, on the contrary, a sign of the strengthening of his health and perfection, and that he does not need any medical treatment at all. It is understood that at first, the patient is happier with the words of those who tell him he is healthy—and indeed, perfectly healthy—than with the words of one who tells him he needs treatment. But the results of the first approach versus the second are also understood. And surely for one of your stature, there is no need to explain the analogy and its relevance to the question about which you write.

May it be the will of the Almighty that these few lines, small in quantity regarding the reaction to the matter and its implications, will suffice not only to clarify my position, but—and this is the main thing—to bring about good results for the correction of what is wrong. For ultimately, even [those] who are currently blessing themselves in their hearts, saying [otherwise], when they are made aware of their error, will admit and praise this action. Just as in the analogy of the patient and the doctor, where even if the medicine is bitter at first, the results are truly good.

With respect and blessing.

## 10,761

B"H, 5 Shevat, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Colonel Tzur and all the soldiers and officers of the Golan Heights,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

It gave me pleasure to receive your letter, in which you write about the visit of the Chabad representatives to the Golan Heights during the days of Chanukah, their activities, the impressions made, and so on.

I thank you very much for the great nachas you have caused me with this letter.

Especially as my hope is strong that the impression mentioned finds expression in actual deed as well—that is to say, not only an elevation of the soul, etc., as you write in your letter, but also an elevation of the body. By this I mean the actions of the body and its conduct in daily life, or in simpler terms—practical mitzvos. After all, our Sages of blessed memory emphasized that [the deed is the essential thing](#_ftn_340).

This is especially relevant for the soldiers of the IDF who defend our Holy Land and the people who dwell upon it, that they should succeed in this. In the words of the verse: "For Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp to save you and to deliver your enemies before you; therefore your camp shall be holy" (Devarim, Teitzei 23:15).

As has been discussed many times, and as is a rule visible tangibly everywhere, when the enemy sees the magnitude of the strength and fortitude of the defenders, it terrifies and frightens them from provoking war, "for [terror and dread shall fall upon them](#_ftn_341)."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you bring good tidings regarding all of the above, and may the prophecy soon be fulfilled: "And I will grant peace in the land, and you shall lie down and none shall make you afraid... and I will lead you upright" (Vayikra, Bechukosai 26:6-13).

With respect and blessing.

However, it is incumbent upon the recipient of the blessing to prepare the conduit and the vessel to receive the influence; and to the extent that one grows and expands that conduit and vessel, it further adds to and draws down a corresponding growth and expansion in the blessing itself.

## 10,717

B"H, 13 Shevat, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

This means to disseminate authentic Yiddishkeit in general, and the wellsprings of the words of the living G-d—the Torah of Chassidus—in particular, by being a living example of this, in addition to words that come from the heart, which enter the heart and accomplish their effect. It is well known that there is nothing that can stand before the will, and the matter depends solely on you and your will.

It is also clear that you must make an effort in an appropriate manner, but with the greatest possible energy, regarding a suitable shidduch. And surely our friends, may they live, who are in... will assist you in this to the best of their ability.

I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above, and the sooner this happens, the better.

With blessings,

## 10,777

10,777

May it be the will of Hashem that you strengthen yourselves and also [increase](#_ftn_381) in your learning and in your conduct—in accordance with the will and hopes of the Baal HaHilula,

Both regarding each individual personally and regarding your special role to be a "candle [to illuminate](#_ftn_382)" your surroundings,

As is brought and emphasized in his sichos and his letters,

And the words of the tzaddikim and their blessings are always enduring and perform their effect,

However, it is incumbent upon the recipient of the blessing to prepare the conduit and the vessel for the influence and the blessing,

And to the extent that one enlarges the conduit and the vessel and expands them—the influence and the blessing will be increased as well,

Until you [serve as a beacon](#_ftn_383) for the many.

With blessings for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

**Rosh Hashanah La'ilanos**: And see Taanis (7a): "The tree of the field..."—these are the talmidei chachamim.

**And also increase**: For one must always ascend in holiness.

**Candle to illuminate**: And behold, "Love your fellow as yourself" is a great principle of the Torah (Yerushalmi Nedarim ch. 9, halacha 4; and see Shabbos 31a; Tanya ch. 32).

**Serve as a beacon for the many**: Similar to what David, the sweet singer of Israel, said on behalf of all of Israel (Tehillim 71:7).

## 10,782

B”H, Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Yisro, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

It is with pleasure that I learned you have reached the age of thirteen, the season of Bar Mitzvah.

This is fitting for the core theme of this week’s parsha, the receiving of the Torah from Sinai, when all the people of Bnei Yisrael accepted the yoke of Torah and the yoke of mitzvos, in the sense of a "Bar Mitzvah" in every respect.

It is surely unnecessary to explain to you that when we speak of the "yoke" of Torah and its mitzvos, the meaning of this "yoke" is not, Heaven forbid, a burden or a load, but rather guidance, instruction, and a way of life through which the Jewish man fulfills his purpose in life. On the contrary, it is a matter of joy, [as our Sages of blessed memory stated](#_ftn_386), "The Holy One, blessed be He, desired to grant merit to Yisrael, therefore He gave them an abundance of Torah and mitzvos." May it be His will that you indeed accept this yoke with true joy and be a source of nachas—true Jewish nachas—to your parents and a source of pride to all your friends.

On this occasion, I will express an idea that is fundamentally relevant to every Bar Mitzvah, in connection with [the question](#_ftn_387) of why we say **Tachanun** on the day of the Bar Mitzvah. After all, we do not say Tachanun on Yom Tov, [and there is no greater Yom Tov or joy than this](#_ftn_388)—to reach the level of a Jewish man, a full member of the chosen people, with all the privileges and responsibilities that entails.

The explanation is that the Torah and mitzvos are without limit or end, as their source is in Hashem, who is Ein Sof. Therefore, there is no limit to the degree of progress and ascent in all matters of goodness and holiness in daily life, in accordance with the will of the Creator. Even if one were to say that one’s state yesterday was as required according to one’s level, the state today must be even higher, and tomorrow higher still. This is the reason we say Tachanun every weekday—to request forgiveness from Hashem, who is abundant in forgiveness, for the fact that today (and yesterday) did not fulfill the will of the Creator in a more elevated manner. This is also the reason the Bar Mitzvah says Tachanun. And it goes without saying that if, for some reason, the present (and the past) is not as it should be in its fullness, the Yetzer then tries to introduce confusion and discouragement, saying, "Did you not fail in the past? Your deeds are not acceptable before the Holy One, blessed be He, so continue as before," and so on. The response to this is the recitation of Tachanun with even greater intent, and with complete confidence [that He who is abundant](#_ftn_389) in forgiveness removes the guilt of the past, for [there is nothing](#_ftn_390) that stands before teshuvah. On the contrary, one who returns in truth becomes even more [beloved](#_ftn_391) and dear to the Makom, B”H.

It is my hope that the aforementioned idea regarding the recitation of Tachanun on the day of the Bar Mitzvah—when a Jew enters a new path of life as a complete and adult Jew—will be a lamp to your feet, to go [from strength](#_ftn_392) to strength in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of its mitzvos with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for success in all the above.

## 10727

[B"H], Tuesday, the day on which it was doubled that it is [good], 
Parshas [Im] Kesef Talveh Es Ami, 
[Shmittah Year], 5733. Brooklyn, N.Y.

The Administration of the Shomrei Shabbos Gemilas Chasadim Society
May they live and be well,

Peace and Blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter bearing good news that you are "preparing to arrange the annual Melaveh Malkah for the benefit of the Gemach" on Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Mishpatim—

And may it be the will that it be with success and good fortune.

Especially since this year is the seventh year, regarding which it is said, "A Shabbos Shabbason [shall be] for the land, a Shabbos to Hashem."

This is particularly appropriate given the unique calendar of this Shmittah year—[that Rosh Hashanah fell on Shabbos], [and likewise]—[the "Rosh] Hashanah for Chassidus," the day of the passing and Hilula of the Nasi of our generation (my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe), and more.

For [Shabbos] emphasizes the concept of Gemilas Chasadim, as our Sages of blessed memory said regarding Shabbos that the Holy One, Blessed be He, says, "Borrow upon Me and I will pay." Shabbos itself performs kindness (it has nothing of its own) for the Community of Israel. As is known in the interpretation of our Sages of blessed memory, "The sun on Shabbos is charity for the poor." This is also alluded to in the command of our Torah, the Torah of truth: "Six days you shall work and do all your labor," and a person cannot do all his labor in one week, but rather a person should view it every Shabbos as if all his labor is done (during the six days).

May the gathering resolve [to expand] the activities of the Gemach, and may you fulfill these resolutions with expansiveness and pleasure.

The activities of a Gemach are from one end to the other (both with one’s money, etc., and even for the wealthy, etc.).

And as the command to walk in His ways, among which are: "[And Your righteousness], O G-d, is until the heights, etc., and from the depths of the earth, etc."

And great is charity (and especially in its highest level—Gemilas Chasadim) in that it brings the Redemption closer, our redemption, [regarding which it is said], "In returning and rest you shall be saved."

With respect and blessing for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

Enclosed is my participation, G-d willing.

**Shmittah year**: It should be noted that the concept of Gemilas Chasadim is relevant even in Shmittah in all respects—see Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken, end of Hilchos Halvaah and the sources cited there.

**Bearing good news**: Doubled, for Heaven and for the creations (Kiddushin 40a; Rambam’s Commentary on the Mishnah, Peah 1:1)—in addition to the fact that any gathering regarding Torah and Mitzvos is a double benefit, for the participants and for the world (Sanhedrin 71a, bottom).

**Mishpatim**: See Torah Or, Beshalach (63, bottom), that the judgment and righteousness of man causes the judgment and righteousness from Above.

**Shabbos.. to Hashem**: Behar 25:4.

**Shall be for the land**: Note the reference to Torah Or at its beginning. From what is written, "And you shall be for Me a land of desire." And see Maamarei Admur HaZaken, entry "Eretz," at its beginning.

**Rosh Hashanah for Chassidus**: The well-known letter of the Rebbe (printed in "Hayom Yom" at the beginning; Introduction to Kuntres U'Maayan).

**Shabbos.. Gemilas Chasadim**: Note the reference to Zohar Chadash, Beshalach 63, bottom, and there. Likutei Levi Yitzchak there.

**Says.. pay**: Beitzah 15b, bottom. And see Or HaTorah by the Maggid, near the end (114c).

**Kindness.. nothing)**: Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 10.

**As is known in the interpretation**: Likutei Torah, discourse beginning "Vehayah Midei Chodesh." Siddur, discourse of the same name and its explanation. Ohr HaTorah by the Tzemach Tzedek, Malachi 3:20. Discourse "VeZarchah," 5699.

**Sun.. poor**: Taanis 8b, bottom.

**Six.. done**: Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken, Orach Chaim 306, end of section 21. And see also Rashi on the Torah, Yitro (20:9). Note that in Sefer Mitzvos Katan, beginning of section 80, the word **"as if"** is absent.

**In one week**: This is how it appears in the first printing of Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken. In other printings of Shulchan Aruch Admur HaZaken that I have seen, it is printed "in one week" (b'shavua achas)—and it seems to me that it should be "in one week" (b'shavua echad), and so it is in the Sefer Mitzvos Katan, Tur, etc.

**Done (during the six days)**: Based on this—the activity (spiritually) of Shabbos during the six days preceding it. See Kesser Shem Tov, discourse "Inyan HaShabbos" (59b).

**Expand.. pleasure**: See Gittin 56b. And it is said, "And you shall call the Shabbos a pleasure." And see Pri Etz Chaim, Shaar HaShabbos, chapter 21.

**Both with one’s money.. wealthy**: Sukkah 49b.

**As the command.. His ways**: Sotah 14a.

**And Your righteousness.. earth**: Tehillim 71:19-20.

**Great is charity**: Bava Basra 10a.

**Highest level**: Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah 249:6.

**In returning and rest**: See Yerushalmi Taanis, chapter 1, end of halacha 4: "Shabbos, etc., and it says 'In returning, etc.'" And in Vayikra Rabbah, beginning of chapter 9: "Israel is only redeemed in the merit of Shabbos, as it is said, 'In returning, etc.'" And see Hemshech VeKacha, at its end.

## 10,793

[B"H]( #_ftn_427), Erev Rosh Chodesh Adar I, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Editorial Board of "Kovetz Chana"
Talmud Torah Lubavitch
Paris

Shalom u'Bracha!

It is with pleasure that I acknowledge receipt of issue no. 7 (for the month of Shevat), and I thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending it to me.

Since [everything is by Divine Providence]( #_ftn_428) and the issue was received after the Shabbos of Mevarchim Chodesh Adar I, this is the appropriate place to remark upon the lesson to be learned from the concept of the leap year regarding its practical application in daily life.

[As is known]( #_ftn_429), [the concept of the leap year is]( #_ftn_430) that we count by the moon, and the lunar year is deficient compared to the solar year. We must fill this deficiency so that [the festivals fall in their proper seasons]( #_ftn_431)—Pesach in the month of spring, Sukkos at the time of the harvest, etc.—and therefore we fill the deficiency of the lunar year relative to the solar year by adding a month from time to time in a leap year. Through this, we not only fill the deficiency but even add to it.

The instruction and lesson from this are twofold: a) that it is always possible and mandatory to rectify the deficiencies of the past, and b) that this is not enough; one must also add as a "down payment" for the future.

Certainly, anyone who contemplates and makes a true accounting of their soul regarding the past will find that even if, in general, the past is satisfactory, with a little more effort it would surely have been possible to achieve more—and this is all the more true if, for whatever reason, things were not as they should have been. However, one must not despair and say, "The past is gone, it is no more, and it is a pity for what is lost," and leave it at that. Rather, one must strive to fill the deficiency, and not only that, but to add to it as a "down payment" for the future. The analogy is understood.

May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one does what is dependent upon them to [fill]( #_ftn_432) the "diminishment of the moon" so that there will be no lack in it, but rather the opposite, as mentioned above. [And our Sages of blessed memory have assured us]( #_ftn_433) that there is nothing that can stand before the will.

With blessings for success in all of the above and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1094

1094

[B"H](#_ftn_434), Motzaei Shabbos, 2nd day of Rosh Chodesh Adar Rishon,
The seventh year, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letters, etc.

We have already [discussed](#_ftn_435) several times throughout the year the unique point of this year—that its content and several of its matters are connected to the day of Shabbos:

The entire year—the seventh year—is referred to as "a Shabbos of Shabbos for the land, a Shabbos for Hashem."

Rosh Hashanah, when the events of all the days of the year are [judged](#_ftn_436) and determined, fell on Shabbos.

The [Rosh Hashanah](#_ftn_437) of Chassidus, which our holy Rebbes—may their merit protect us—bequeathed to us, and which is the very teaching of the Baal Shem Tov—19 Kislev—fell on Shabbos.

The [day](#_ftn_438) of the passing of the Nasi of our generation—my father-in-law, the Rebbe—10 Shevat—fell on Shabbos.

And being a **leap year**, the head and beginning of the [month](#_ftn_439) of intercalation falls on Shabbos.

[Now](#_ftn_440), the concept of intercalation in general is that through it, one completes what is lacking (in the number of days, relative to the solar year) from the years that have passed, and one also adds several days beyond the days of the solar year.

The concept of the day of Shabbos is rest and *taanug*, as it is written, "And you shall call the Shabbos a *taanug*," [and all](#_ftn_441) of a person’s actions and affairs on it are from a place of *taanug* and in a manner of *taanug*.

May it be Hashem’s will that the above will awaken everyone, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, until one succeeds in filling all that is lacking throughout all the days of his life, completing it and adding to it, "going and adding" in light.

And in accordance with the command to follow the attributes of the Ribono shel Olam, among which are: "[Your righteousness](#_ftn_442) is like the mighty mountains... and Your judgments are like the great deep,"

To illuminate matters of the "heights" (Torah and *mitzvos*) and matters of the "depths" (this physical and material world, lower than which there is no lower),

And to do all this from a place of true rest and *taanug*,

Until we merit, in the immediate future, the true and complete Geulah, [of which it is said](#_ftn_443): "In returning and rest you shall be saved."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,799

[18 Adar, 5733]

According to the information that has reached me regarding the manner in which nursing homes are managed—the primary profit comes from cutting back and reducing the **medical** care that the residents **require**, economizing on their **food**, on the heating of the buildings, **and the like**. I have heard this from **many people**.

Since then, I do not advise anyone who asks me to enter into this business, because apparently the **daily** trial is greater than one can bear (and they add to this the "justification" [that there is no agent for a sinful act] **and in practice**, the act is performed by someone else, etc.).

## 1070

1070

B”H, 20 Adar I, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Dr. S. Dreyfuss
11 Bustanai St., Jerusalem

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 10th of Adar I.

May Hashem fulfill your heart’s desires for the good in all the matters you write about.

And regarding the inner point, may you derive much true nachas—Jewish, Torah-true nachas—from your son, Netanel, may he live, whom you write about in your letter.

Especially since you have merited to be in [Eretz Yisrael], of which it is said, “The eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.”

With respect and blessing,

P.S. In our office, we do not write in French, which is why the response is in Lashon HaKodesh. However, you may continue to write to me in French in the future, and please let me know in which language it is more convenient for you to receive the response: Lashon HaKodesh, Yiddish, or English.

Regarding what you write concerning the conduct of your son, may he live, the chumros he is taking upon himself, and the impact this has on the relationship between you:

Generally, in any such matter, it is not appropriate to express an opinion before hearing the arguments of the other side. However, even before that hearing, I would like to note a few points that I believe are important:

(a) It is surely known to you that regarding chumros that a Jewish person takes upon himself [and practices three times or more], one must ask a Rav whether they require a formal release, whether they should be permitted, etc.

(b) It is also surely known to you the nature of our times, which are full of confusion in general, and especially regarding the worldview of the youth. Furthermore, there are no longer strong partitions separating one circle from another. Therefore, every fence and safeguard is praiseworthy, especially since one cannot know if they will last for long days. Consequently, special caution and a special approach toward the youth are required. It is not always possible for an adult, including parents (and perhaps it is even harder for parents, as they are personally involved), to accurately gauge the youth’s reaction to their approach and suggestions. Sometimes, the touching or shaking of a single "brick" can shake the entire structure of the youth’s worldview.

(c) From this, it is understood that if the matter concerns leniency in the conduct of the youth—and all the more so with excessive leniencies, to which the commandment of [“You shall surely rebuke”] applies—one is fulfilling a commandment of Hashem and His mission. This is not the case when the matter concerns chumros.

(d) The nature of the youth in our times is that they seek novelty, in a style recently accepted to the point of "rebellion against the establishment." And if this rebellion is expressed in a matter of chumrah, then even if, as you state in your letter, there are unpleasant results, etc., it is still not comparable to a situation where the expression is in the opposite direction, toward leniency, etc.

(e) When the movement is toward chumrah, even when it is against the parents' perspective, there is still a point of connection that narrows the conflict, for [“Honor”] your father and your mother is a positive commandment, and one should be stringent in that as well. This is not the case when the inclination is toward leniency.

Since you have great experience in the field of education, etc., surely these lines—few in quantity, but especially in light of the importance of the subject—will suffice.

May it be the will of Hashem, as I conclude in the letter above, that you derive much nachas from this son of yours and from all your descendants, may they live.

## 10 Adar

10 Adar

B"H, 20 Adar I, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Avraham Eden,
Major General, Commander of the Armored Corps,

Shalom u'Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the month of Shevat, and I read with pleasure that you participated in the farbrengen in Kfar Chabad and of your impressions from it.

You have surely heard the adage of the Baal Shem Tov that from everything that occurs in a person's life and in their surroundings, one must derive a lesson for the fulfillment of one's role on earth. As a man of the IDF, and especially as a commander, it is unnecessary to emphasize to you that a primary point in the army is that action is the essential thing, even to the point of kabbalas ol—without taking one's own intellect into account. When an order is given, one must first and foremost fulfill the order in actual deed, and afterwards, in one's spare time, one can seek explanation and clarification, etc.

Therefore, it is my hope that regarding what you write—that you had a special experience and a feeling of elevation—that this, too, will be translated into actual deed. And since you are a Major General and commander, this means that you have influence over many in your surroundings. Since even **one** person is an entire world, you serve, knowingly and unknowingly, as an example and a model for many. Whatever your role may be in its external aspect, internally, the goal is to bring matters to their perfection: the perfection of the person as an individual; the perfection of our nation, the Jewish people, of which the individual is a part (for the whole contains nothing other than what is in the parts); and the perfection of our Torah, which is the foundation and secret of our nation's existence. Upon this also depends—as you concluded in your letter—the security of Israel and its establishment in its land.

[As the verse states](#_ftn_468), "For Hashem your G-d walks in the midst of your camp, to save you and to deliver your enemies before you; therefore your camp shall be holy."

And according to the [statement of our Sages](#_ftn_469), the Holy One, Blessed be He, does not deal tyrannically with His creatures. It is therefore clear that together with the role with which He **grants** a person the merit to serve, He provides the strength to carry it out in the best possible way.

With respect and with blessings for success in all of the above.

10757

[B"H], 24 Adar I, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual gathering of the "Ntzivei HaYeshiva" of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal,
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the news that the annual gathering has been scheduled for the 9th of Adar II, the historic day when my father-in-law, the Rebbe, arrived in America 33 years ago.

[As] is well known, immediately upon his arrival, the Rebbe declared that he had not come for his own sake, but that Divine Providence had brought him to set foot on American soil, [in order] to make America, with the help of Hashem, a place of Torah and fear of Heaven, in the spirit of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch.

After all the years that have passed since that day, it is certainly appropriate to take stock of what has been accomplished. And surely, there is much to be satisfied with.

Yet, at the same time, when looking around at what is happening, and seeing how many Jewish children and youth are still wandering in the darkness, waiting for someone to reach out a hand and lead them from the darkness to the light of Torah and mitzvos, a distressing feeling arises: that despite all the achievements, one could have accomplished even more. And here, a flawed thought may arise: "What is past is past, it is lost. Let us at least ensure for the future that every day accomplishes its own."

However, [among] Jews, there is no such thing as "lost." And this is something we are reminded of especially by the (current) **leap year**, particularly as we find ourselves in this leap month.

[The] concept of the leap year is to **fill the deficiency** of the lunar year (the basis of our calendar) relative to the solar year, so that our Yomim Tovim fall at their proper time (Pesach in the spring, etc.). But in this, there is also the instruction that a Jew must fill in what he missed in the time that has passed.

Furthermore, just as in the case of a leap year, when an entire month is added, it does not merely fill the deficiency of the previous years, but also provides an **addition** to the account of the coming years—so too must a Jew strive not only to fill what he missed—regardless of what the reasons were and how justified they may have been—but also to add something as an "extra" for the future.

I hope, and am certain, that the response of all the participants, especially the honored Ntzivim and activists, may they live, will be especially warm this year, so that together with the Yeshiva, you can carry out in actual practice the lesson of the leap year, as mentioned above.

May you all be greeted and blessed by Hashem with great success, both in this endeavor and in general, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 5733

7 Adar II, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the activists and friends of the Bais Rivkah schools in general, and to the participants of the annual gathering in particular,

May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the news that the annual gathering is taking place this year on **Rosh Chodesh Nissan**, may it come upon us for good.

[As is known](#_ftn_505), there is a special significance to the term "Rosh" (head) in connection with Rosh Chodesh (and Rosh Hashanah). The content of this is that it is not merely the "beginning," but the "head." Just as the head concentrates within itself the vitality of the entire body and serves as the nerve center for all the body’s functions, so too is Rosh Chodesh in relation to all the days of the month (and Rosh Hashanah in relation to all the days of the year).

From this, one can understand the special importance of Rosh Chodesh Nissan, for the month of Nissan is the [month](#_ftn_506) of Geulah—the liberation of our people from the exile of Mitzrayim, which reaches its highest expression on the Yom Tov of Pesach, [zman cheiruseinu](#_ftn_507) (the time of our freedom).

[The](#_ftn_508) Geulah was twofold: Geulah in gashmius, meaning the simple liberation from physical slavery, and [Geulah in ruchnius](#_ftn_509), the liberation from spiritual enslavement, which began already in Mitzrayim (through the Korban Pesach, etc.) and reached its highest expression through Kabbalas HaTorah [miSinai](#_ftn_510).

This underscores the Jewish Torah-concept of freedom: despite living in a world where gashmius and ruchnius are viewed as two separate worlds, a Jew can be free only when they are free in both realms together—both materially and spiritually—with an emphasis on the freedom of the neshamah to conduct daily life in full harmony with the Divine Will, according to the Torah and mitzvos that He has given us. For only such a life has meaning and substance for a Jew.

This concept must be implanted in our children from their earliest youth through a Torah-true chinuch in Torah-true educational institutions. However, it is understood that the home also has a vital place in the chinuch of children. This brings out the special importance of the Bais Rivkah educational institution, where Jewish daughters are prepared to occupy their central place in the Jewish home as the **akeres habayis**, upon whom the entire conduct of the home, and the very foundation of the Jewish home, is dependent to a very great extent.

It is therefore my request and firm hope that all the activists and friends of these institutions of chinuch habanos al taharas hakodesh will do everything in their power to ensure that this annual undertaking and all the activities of Bais Rivkah throughout the entire year should be met with great success. May this merit stand by all the activists, friends, and supporters to receive the blessings of the Ribono shel Olam for themselves and their families, in everything they need, in gashmius and ruchnius alike.

With honor and with a blessing for success and good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,761

B"H, 12 Adar II, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. and Mrs. Nosson Dovid and Devorah Rabinowitz, may they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 28th of Adar I, and I thank you for the good news that you passed the examination successfully. May it be His will that you continue to bring only good tidings in the future.

This is especially relevant as we are in the month of Adar [in which we are commanded to increase in joy](#_ftn_517). Since [Hashem](#_ftn_518) does not deal harshly with His creatures, He surely provides and arranges good matters for us to rejoice in. This is particularly true in this year, a leap year, in which we have two months of Adar—meaning that the "increase in joy" must also be doubled. Furthermore, since the commandment comes [from Hashem, the G-d of truth](#_ftn_519), it refers to true joy, without any distracting elements.

[As we stand](#_ftn_520) before the eve of Purim, which is the Yom Tov of the month of Adar, it is superfluous to emphasize that one of the points of Purim is the matter of drawing hearts closer together, which is one of the reasons for the mitzvah of sending gifts to one another, [as explained in the reasons for the mitzvos](#_ftn_521). There is nothing that draws the hearts of the Jewish people closer to one another and to their Father in Heaven like Torah and mitzvos. If throughout the entire year we are obligated to spread and establish Yiddishkeit, then how much more so during these days. And surely, for one such as you, further elaboration is unnecessary.

May it be His will that you carry out the above with joy and with an increase in Torah and its mitzvos, in accordance with [the words of](#_ftn_522) the Megillah: "The Jews had light, and gladness, and joy, and honor," [and our Sages of blessed memory expounded](#_ftn_523) that "light" refers to Torah, and so on.

With respect and with a blessing for a happy and illuminating Purim.

## 10,726

B"H, 16 Adar II, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the graduating class of "Beis Rivkah"
Brooklyn, N.Y.

May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

In response to your notification regarding the completion of your studies, may it be at a propitious and successful time for even higher advancement in your learning and conduct, as is fitting for daughters of Yisrael who carry with pride the title—daughters of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah, who built the house of Yisrael.

Since we have just come from the days of Purim and the reading of the Megillah, one of the matters that are "remembered and performed"—that those days are remembered so that they may be performed also at this time —as emphasized in the Megillah of Esther, is: **"There is one people"** (not only then and there, but in every place and time, even though they are) **"scattered and dispersed among the peoples"** (and their unity is expressed in that) **"their laws are different from every people"** (the interpretation of "their laws" in the plural—their customs, habits, and conduct in daily life). This applies to all sons and daughters of Yisrael in general.

[And as discussed at the Purim farbrengen] regarding the women and daughters of Yisrael in particular, even though **"the word of Mordechai Esther performed,"** and her entire conduct was according to the instructions of Mordechai, the head of the generation, nevertheless [the Megillah was named specifically after her alone], **Megillah of Esther**. This emphasizes once again that **action is the essential thing**, and the performance was indeed carried out by Esther. This also brings out the explanation of the matter that Esther requested, ["Write me down for the generations"] —which, of course, was not intended for her own honor, but so that the women and daughters of Yisrael in all generations would learn from her and act likewise, in a manner of mesiras nefesh, just as she sacrificed herself for her people and for everything holy to her people.

May Hashem grant that each and every one of you [will go from strength to strength] in actual deed, in all matters of Yiddishkeit, and may Hashem bless each and every one of you and fulfill the requests of your hearts for the good.

With blessings for success and for good tidings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,727

B"H, 16 Adar II, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Aaron Cohen,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Your letter of 8 Adar II has reached me, as have your previous ones. Many thanks for your attentiveness in bringing the events and occurrences you write about to my attention. I am certain you will continue to do so in the future, and I thank you in advance.

Regarding the substance of the matter, it is difficult to express a true opinion, because with every single issue, those involved immediately strike a deal and launch a campaign, etc., to the point of complete shamelessness. For example, regarding the matters you write about, those who actually set the line of action are not ashamed to say openly that it is necessary to enter into a deal with them: if they want them to concede on the issue of [the draft of yeshiva students](#_ftn_538), then they will concede to them on the issue of [“Who is a Jew”](#_ftn_539). This is a disgrace the likes of which did not exist even in the conduct of the four or five individuals mentioned, even though they have already prepared the basis to forcefully deny it in the well-known phrasing, “it never happened,” [in the style](#_ftn_540) of our Sages, of the one who claims: (a) I did not borrow, (b) I borrowed and repaid, (c) I was the lender and the loan must be paid to me.

Similarly, at first they announced that the Law of Return in all its details was a wonderful religious achievement, and afterwards they announced that there was never a [decision by the Chief Rabbinate](#_ftn_541) on this, etc., etc., leading up to the latest declaration here—specifically on the front page of the press—that the decision regarding the draft of yeshiva students was never accepted. And no one opens their mouth or chirps. And, of course, they continue to stand at the forefront of all activities, and primarily, this includes the distribution of funds, positions, and honors, etc.

As I have said several times, perhaps the merit to be found in them is that one sees their aforementioned conduct regarding every issue on the agenda is always in one direction, which is liable to cause, Heaven forbid, the destruction of the people of Israel, the Torah of Israel, and the Land of Israel. Yet, their position remains firm, and they are the ones who stand at the head and set the line. And all those who say they will not concede and will not agree, etc.—when it comes down to it, they beg them to give them a share of the honors, etc., and promise them their place at the top of the list for the Knesset elections and the institutions. They will even declare them, with full mouth, to be the responsible leaders and the true guides who guard our religion, etc., etc. There is no need to elaborate on this appalling matter.

And since we stand between a miracle and a miracle, between the miracle of Purim and the miracle of the holiday of Pesach, may it be the will of Hashem that we, too, merit to see actual miracles in all the aforementioned matters, even though we are still the servants of Achashverosh (Megillah 14a).

With respect and blessing that, finally, you will begin to share good news.

## 10737

B"H, 26 Adar II, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the soldiers of Unit 1331
May Hashem protect them and grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letter dated 17 Adar II written on your behalf, and I offer many thanks for your thoughtfulness in informing me of the receipt of the [Mishloach Manos]() for the festival of Purim.

It is my hope that, being members of our people, the Jewish people—who are called in the holy Torah a "[wise]() and understanding nation"—you have certainly also contemplated the inner dimension of this mitzvah of sending portions to one another. As explained [in the words]() of our Sages of blessed memory, one of the reasons for this mitzvah is to emphasize that even though our people are ["scattered]() and dispersed among the nations," they are nonetheless **one people**, united in love and brotherhood **one to another**. This is not merely a matter of abstract thought or feeling, but must be expressed in actual deed. This is why [the precision of this mitzvah]() dictates that one does not fulfill the obligation by sending words of blessing, or even words of Torah and wisdom, but specifically by sending actual portions of food to be enjoyed [immediately]() as an actual meal. Furthermore, a "manah" (portion) implies a fine portion, worthy of being served to a guest.

[And another point regarding this:]() as emphasized in the Megillah, even a gentile like Haman the Wicked recognized the reality of the truth: that there **is** one people (even though they are) scattered and dispersed among the nations (and their unity and uniqueness are expressed in the fact that) "their laws are different from every people." The term "laws" (das) here does not refer to religion and faith of the heart, but simply to customs, manners, and the way of life in day-to-day, practical action. Even Esther, when she sought to annul the decree, did not deny this, for it is indeed the truth.

Surely, the men of the IDF who stand on the borders and guard all the children of Israel dwelling in Eretz Yisrael do not require extra emphasis regarding the uniqueness and destiny of our people. It is this that has stood for us and for our fathers in every generation against all who rise up against us.

May it be the will of Hashem that you merit to protect not only the physical borders of Eretz Yisrael, but also the spiritual borders of Eretz Yisrael—which is called the Holy Land even by all the nations of the world. For this holiness, which stems from our holy Torah and its mitzvos, is the secret and the existence of the Jewish people.

And may you accomplish all of the above—also [in the language of the Megillah]()—with light, joy, gladness, and honor.

And since we are approaching the festival of Pesach, the time of our freedom, may each and every one of you be blessed with a kosher and joyous Pesach and true freedom. May we soon merit the fulfillment of [the promise](), "And I will grant peace in the land," and as the [verse continues](), "And I will be to you a G-d, and you shall be to Me a people... and I will lead you upright."

With respect and blessing for a kosher and joyous Pesach,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10741

10741

[B"H], Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem protect them and grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

The month of Nissan and its central point, Chag HaPesach, have a special connection and bond with their Rosh Chodesh—Rosh Chodesh Nissan. This is also indicated in the introduction to the month of Nissan and to Chag HaPesach: **Parshas HaChodesh**, which is read in the Torah on the Shabbos before Rosh Chodesh Nissan (or on Shabbos Rosh Chodesh Nissan).

The entire passage is called "Parshas HaChodesh," even though "HaChodesh" is merely the beginning of its second verse—and the content of the passage is entirely about the Korban Pesach, Chag HaPesach, and their laws.

From this, it is understood that the content of this verse is not merely an introduction to the subject of Pesach, but rather that it has a special connection to it.

The question arises: What is the connection between "This month shall be for you... it is the first of the months of the year"—beginning the counting of the months of the year from the month of Nissan—and the matters of Pesach? Furthermore, if every detail in the Torah has a deep content, then surely, regarding a matter connected to Pesach (and Yetziyas Mitzrayim)—which are a "great foundation and strong pillar of our Torah and our faith"—the content must have a far-reaching, general significance.

***

Among Jews, there are—according to the Torah—two general systems in the annual calendar: a) Beginning from the first of Tishrei—from Rosh Hashanah; b) Beginning from "This month"—from Nissan—which is the first of all the months.

The counting beginning from the month of Tishrei is understandable: This is the time of the creation of the world, and it is in accordance with the way of the world (nature), as Hashem established it: "Seed and harvest, etc." (plowing and) **sowing**, and the time for this is the month of Tishrei. Only later, in Nissan, does the first **harvest** of barley begin, and subsequently (at the time of Shavuos) the harvest of wheat, and so on.

The counting among Jews, beginning from the month of Nissan, emphasizes the **miraculous**—*lemalah miderech hateva* (above the way of nature)—conduct of the life of a Jew. This is explained right there on the spot by connecting the matter of Nissan as the "first of the months" with the matter of Pesach, for Pesach and Yetziyas Mitzrayim were "miracles and wonders," entirely above the way of nature.

Both modes of conduct exist. And the instruction of Parshas HaChodesh—that **Nissan** is the first of **all** the months—is that a Jew must know the truth: that even when, with his eyes, he sees only natural conduct, if he looks deeper, he will understand and perceive that, in truth, everything is directed by *Hashgacha Pratis* and in a miraculous manner. This is so to the extent that even a natural thing, such as harvesting barley and wheat, etc., is not the result of "my power and the might of my hand"—of plowing and sowing half a year earlier—but rather "the blessing of Hashem, it makes rich."

And as it was for all Jews **without exception** upon leaving Mitzrayim—they had the *manna* daily, and also later, upon entering the settled land in Eretz Yisrael, the beginning was in Nissan, and they received ready-made fields and gardens for harvesting, etc.

***

Superficially, it might appear that the above contradicts the order of "man is born to toil"—since, after all, the essence is not human toil, but Divine blessing.

However, besides the fact that this is also a directive from Hashem in the Torah, "one does not rely on a miracle," it has already been explained in a previous letter that **amal** (toil) has different levels and stages, similar to how the *avodah* on weekdays is different from the *avodah* on the day of Shabbos, when the toil must be in spiritual matters. In general, even regarding toil in the simple sense—that one plows and sows at the time of plowing and sowing, etc.—the **toil** of the person is merely to create the *levushim* (garments) and vessels according to the way of nature, but he must know and remember that the blessing comes from Hashem.

***

There were times when Jews clearly saw open miracles, such as the miracles that occurred daily in the Beis HaMikdash. But even in these days of *galus*, when the world is enveloped in darkness and miracles are not seen with the physical eye, this is only, as our Sages of blessed memory say, "The one to whom a miracle happens does not recognize his miracle." Yet every person, and especially a Jew, when he reflects on what has happened to him over a certain period, will perceive the *Hashgacha Pratis*—to the point of a miraculous mode of conduct.

***

And this is the *hora'ah klalis* (main instruction) of "This month shall be for you the first of the months": While Jews stand on the eve of "Yetziyas Mitzrayim" and the beginning of a new "life," both for the collective and for the individual, Hashem gave us a new order—to count the months of the year specifically from Nissan. The instruction of the Torah of **truth**, which is the Torah of life (the Torah of daily life), which is the true perception and Jewish concept of conduct in the world, is: to always see the *Hashgacha Pratis* and the *lemalah miderech hateva* conduct, even when it is concealed in "natural" garments.

***

This was also indicated by Dovid HaMelech in several of the Psalms, which he said as the "sweet singer of Israel"—for and in the name of all Jews in all generations; also in the Psalm: "In You, Hashem, I have taken refuge" ("In You, G-d, I protect myself"—not only at certain times, but always, every day, and therefore) "I shall **never** be shamed."

And this leads to a conduct where one sees clearly that it is a miraculous conduct, to the point that all those things that could hinder life as it should be in general, and Torah and *mitzvos* in particular, are not only nullified, but **v'nahapoch hu**—they are turned around, so that they even assist in the good and facilitate the proper life, as the conclusion of that Psalm:

"Also my tongue, **all day long**, shall speak of Your righteousness, for those who sought my harm have been shamed and confounded."

All those people and things that previously were not only unfavorable, but sought to do evil, not only become powerless and nullified, but they are ashamed of their **previous** attitude.

***

May it be the will that the month of Nissan, the month of *Geulah*, should bring to everyone a liberation and freedom from all things that are *metzarim* and *Mitzrayim* (causing distress, G-d forbid, or limiting), and may it be the proper preparation for the festival of Chag HaMatzos, the time of our freedom.

With respect and with the blessing of a kosher and happy Chag HaPesach,

**Menachem Schneerson**

10 Tishrei 5732

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Chabad girls participating in the "Mishloach Manos" project,
May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the "Mishloach Manos" project in which you participated.

Certainly, there is no need to explain to you the greatness of this mitzvah. Although it is one of the specific mitzvos of Purim, its content and essence—the matter of **"Love your fellow as yourself,"** as emphasized in the phrasing, "sending portions, one to **another**" —is relevant throughout the entire year.

In particular, as has been discussed many times, the women and girls had an important part in the miracle of Purim, to the extent that it is emphasized that the Megillah is not named after Mordechai, nor even after Mordechai and Esther together, but specifically after Esther alone.

And since our Sages, of blessed memory, said, "Connect one redemption to another," which is highlighted especially in this leap year where Purim falls in the Adar adjacent to Nissan,

May it be Hashem’s will that your aforementioned activity, along with the rest of the mitzvos of Purim, serve as a preparation for the time of our liberation, including liberation from all matters that cause confusion in both material and spiritual affairs. May Hashem grant you success to go from strength to strength and from mitzvah to mitzvah.

With blessings for a kosher and happy Pesach.

Enclosed is a copy of a general letter which will surely be of benefit to you, "and action is the primary thing."

## 10th of Nissan, 5733

10th of Nissan, 5733

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received the volumes of Likutei Sichos on the weekly parsha in good time and with pleasure.

May it be the will of Hashem that these words accomplish their intended effect, in accordance with the words of our Sages that "the deed is the essential thing"—meaning that there should be an increase in strength and beauty in the performance of mitzvos in actual practice in daily life.

Certainly, for people like you, it is superfluous to elaborate on the magnitude of the merit of one who [performs and causes others to perform](#_ftn_623) all matters of our Torah—Torah of life—and its mitzvos, [regarding which it is said](#_ftn_624) "and he shall live by them."

The interpretation in Chassidus (brought in [Kuntres Limud HaChassidus](#_ftn_625), p. 20) regarding the sugya of "two holding onto a tallis" is well known:

**Two holding onto a tallis**: The *tallis* represents an *ohr makif* (encompassing light), which is the spark of goodness found within a physical object. When two people come and perform a mitzvah with that physical object, they thereby clarify the spark of goodness that was captured and held in captivity within that physicality. They—the ones performing the mitzvah—redeem the spark from its captivity and extract it from exile. Furthermore, the body and essence of that physical object itself is refined from its materiality, because through it and by means of it, the supernal intent in the creation of a physical world is fulfilled.

Now, when the souls that performed the mitzvah in this world arrive in the World of Truth, both of them hold onto the *tallis*, which is the [King’s covering](#_ftn_627)—the spark that was in the physical object, which has been refined and elevated by those who performed the mitzvah.

This is the meaning of "two holding onto a tallis": one says, "I found it," meaning that through his *avodah* he clarified that spark; and the other says, "I found it," meaning that through his toil and labor he acted and caused that physical object to be refined and become a vessel for *Elokus*. Since each of them claims, "It is all mine," this serves as a lesson in how the *avodah* of clarification and refinement should be conducted in such a way that each person receives his reward according to the nature of his *avodah*.

May this be a reflection of the blessings of these days—to carry out all that has been mentioned in a manner of freedom from all matters that cause distraction,

Especially in accordance with what our Sages said in their Mishnah: "There is no free man except one who engages in Torah."

With blessings for a kosher and joyous Pesach and for good tidings in all that has been mentioned.

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Nissan, 5733

With respect and holiday blessings.

This means that your past achievements have increased your energy, your desire, and your activities in accordance with this statement of our Sages, and the merit of the many assists you.

It is certainly unnecessary to emphasize that the news regarding the assistance and help, etc., provided to the activities of the Anash of Chabad in Rechovot has caused me special satisfaction, and surely in this matter as well, you will conduct yourself according to the aforementioned statement of our Sages.

## 10 Nissan 5747

[2 Nissan, 5773]

[To the Secretariat]:

Show this to the administration and members of the Kollel, may they live—[here]—and ask them:

a) Is there **anything** here similar to the above, or better than it—given that it was founded here many years ago?

b) If there is—why have they not informed me of the good news?

c) If not—is there anyone who has the heart for it?

d) If there is—what has been done to rectify the situation? (My intention is not for excuses that someone else needs to do it).

e) If not—perhaps the time has already come (more than the three years required for *chazakah*) to "finish" the Kollel—even in their opinion (for if among those who are supposed to have their souls yearn for Torah there is nothing like the above—then the Kollel serves only as a justification for waste and wasting time—the opposite of [what is written]: **Man is born to toil**).

(The response [is to be given] before 11 Nissan).

## 10 Nissan, 5733

[10 Nissan, 5733]

## 10 Teves 5751

11 Nissan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

Following up on my previous letter, and in order to clarify the point brought out therein—that the true Jewish concept of *Hashgacha Pratis* is, quite simply: every day and in every detail; and that *hanhagah nissis* (miraculous conduct) is not limited to open miracles, but rather that in daily life there is also *hanhagah nissis*, only that **the beneficiary of a miracle does not recognize his miracle**—it is worthwhile to add a few points and also to bring out the lesson from all this, in addition to knowing the Jewish *hashkafas olam* (worldview), also regarding *maaseh b’fo’al* (actual deed), for *maaseh hu ha’ikar* (the deed is the essential thing).

***

*Hanhagah nissis* can exist in two ways: (a) open miracles, manifest miracles, like the miracles associated with *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, meaning miracles that are **entirely above the order of nature** and in complete opposition to nature; (b) miracles like the miracle of *Purim*, which were "clothed" in natural garments.

The miracles of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*—beginning with the signs and wonders in Egypt, up to the liberation of the **entire** nation, young and old, sons and daughters, after hundreds of years of enslavement in a land from which not even one slave could escape, and furthermore, a redemption *b’yad ramah* (with a high hand) and *b’rechush gadol* (with great wealth)—these are events that everyone, without exception, saw clearly and distinctly as open miracles.

Different was the miracle of *Purim*. Although in that case, too, there were miracles, to the point of *v’nahapoch hu*—a complete reversal, until *layehudim haysah orah v’simcha v’sason v’yikar* (the Jews had light, gladness, joy, and honor)—the miracle of *Purim* was "clothed" in the garments of nature: Esther becomes queen, Mordechai sits at the king’s gate and saves the king from an assassination attempt, Esther intercedes with the king to annul the decree, etc., as all these details are recounted in the *Megillah*. Yet, even each event individually, and especially their **convergence** *bayamim hahem bazman hazeh*, was a miracle, as we say many times: *nissim v’purkan v’gevuros v’teshuos v’niflaos*.

***

Also in **natural conduct** there are two ways: (a) conduct that on the "outside" is **entirely natural**, (b) conduct in which *Hashgacha Pratis* is clearly visible.

An example of the first case is the matter of **zera v’katzir** (sowing and reaping): sowing and later reaping is an **entirely natural** thing, to the extent that in order to see the Divine *Hashgacha* in this as well, one must contemplate deeply how *Hashgacha Pratis* brings together different phenomena—winds, rains, and sunshine—each at the proper time, etc.

The second case, of open *Hashgacha Pratis*, or as the world calls it: success, luck, a windfall, etc.—terms that do not say what it **is**, they only state the negation, that this is **not** the achievement of the person’s intellect or his toil—*Toras Emes* tells the truth: that this is through *Hashgacha Pratis* and the blessing of Hashem in *banai, chayei, u’mezoni* (children, life, and sustenance):

True, extraordinary *nachas* from children, constant good health, extraordinary success in *parnassah*, etc.

***

And this is the point that was emphasized in the previous letter as a lesson from *Hachodesh hazeh lachem*: through the fact that the Torah established a counting for Jews such that **all** months begin from the month of *Nissan*, the month whose content and essence is *ki vo yatzas mimitzrayim* through open miracles from the *Ribono shel Olam*, the Torah teaches us that this is how it is—the *Ribono shel Olam’s* conduct—all months of the year. Whether one sees open miracles, whether one sees miracles in natural garments, whether one sees *Hashgacha Pratis*, or whether one sees only nature—a Jew must know and remember that the *Ribono shel Olam* is the *Bashefer* of the world and the sole and absolute *baal-habayis* of the world, and He leads the entire world in all its details and sub-details, and *al achas kamah v’kamah*—this *olam katan* (small world) which is man, every person individually, in **all** the particulars of his daily life.

According to this, it is **self-evident** that every detail of his life, no matter how "small" it may be, contains an instruction—and it must be done according to the instruction—from the One who is "supervising" that specific detail—and nothing can change it, for it "counts" from *Nissan*—open miracles of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*.

***

In continuation also of what was brought in the previous letter, that Dovid Hamelech, in the name of every Jew, pointed out in *Tehillim* the matter of **constant** *Hashgacha Pratis*, and therefore: *B’cha Hashem chasisi al evosha* (In You, Hashem, I have taken refuge, let me not be ashamed—and both things)—*l’olam* (forever), and this brings about that *leshoni kol hayom tehgeh tzidkasecha* (my tongue, too, will speak of Your righteousness **all day long**) (and one sees *Hashgacha Pratis* openly)—*ki voshu ki chafru mevakshei ra’asi* (for ashamed and confounded were those who sought my evil),

The continuation immediately thereafter—in connection with *hanhagah nissis*—is: *Lishlomo Elokim mishpatecha lamelech tein v’tzidkasecha l’ven melech* (To Shlomo, G-d, give Your judgments to the king, and Your righteousness to the king’s son)—the conduct that existed in the times of King Shlomo: *yadin amcha b’tzedek* etc. (he will judge Your people with righteousness—as is known regarding the judgments of Shlomo—in a supernatural way) and thus his entire reign in general—was entirely above nature, such that without any wars: *v’yired etc. ad afsei aretz* (he will rule... to the ends of the earth), until—*kol goyim ya’avduhu* (all nations will serve him).

And the *mizmor* is also an indication, according to how our Sages explain, of the times and conduct of Melech Hamoshiach, when nature **will** be elevated to the level of *l’ma’alah miderech hateva*. Until, instead of the order of **zera v’katzir**, first sowing and then reaping, and only then performing a series of labors like threshing, grinding, kneading, and baking, until it becomes *v’lechem levav enosh yisa’ad* (bread that strengthens the heart of man), there will be *yehi pisas bar ba’aretz* (there will be an abundance of grain in the land), which—in connection with the interpretation regarding *Moshiach*—means according to our Sages that *Eretz Yisroel tozi gluskos v’chilei milas*—that in the times of *Moshiach*, the earth of *Eretz Yisroel* will bring forth ready-made rolls and silk garments—

The conduct in the world will be so miraculous that even compared to the miracles of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* it will be a miracle, and as the verse is interpreted: *kimiy tzeischa me’eretz Mitzrayim ar’enu niflaos*—even compared to the miracles of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* these will be "wonders"—wonders upon wonders.

***

*Y’hei ratzon* that just as in order to hasten the coming of *Moshiach*, it is through *Hayom im b’kolo tishma’u*, conducting oneself in accordance with the message of the *Ribono shel Olam*,

Which is also **hinted** at in the beginning of the *mizmor*: *Mishpatecha lamelech tein v’tzidkasecha l’ven melech*, for every Jew is likened to a king and to a king’s son,

May everyone, man and woman, carry out in daily life the *mishpatim* and *tzedakah* as the *Ribono shel Olam* demands, and *hayom*, from today on, and this will hasten and bring the *Geulah Amitis v’Hashleimah* through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu*, and it will be fulfilled, as he says at the conclusion of the *mizmor* that

... *Elokei Yisroel* (who is) *oseh niflaos levado* ... (there will be) *v’yimalei chvodo es kol ha’aretz* (and the whole world will be filled with His glory) *Amen v’Amen*.

With respect and blessing for a *Pesach* *kasher v’sameach* and for the fulfillment of the promise very soon: *kimiy tzeischa me’eretz Mitzrayim ar’enu niflaos*,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10 Nissan, 5733

10 Nissan, 5733
B"H, 11 Nissan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Peace and blessing!

In anticipation of the Festival of Matzos, the time of our freedom, which is approaching us and all of Israel for good, I hereby express my blessing for a kosher and joyous holiday and for true freedom—freedom from material worries and spiritual worries—from everything that hinders the avodah of Hashem with joy and a glad heart.

And may this freedom and joy be drawn into all the days of the entire year.

Especially since the avodah of Hashem, as we are commanded in our Torah, the Torah of life, encompasses all of a person’s affairs throughout the entire day and night, as it is [stated], "In all your ways, know Him."

With appreciation, honor, and holiday blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

P.S. Your letter was received, and thank you, thank you, etc. However, at the same time, I was surprised (a surprise mixed with pain) by the "spirit" in it and in your recent conversations, etc.,

The reason for which, apparently, is that since in a few weeks the [period] of your position will conclude, you feel it should already be noticeable now, etc.—

And besides the fact that this is neither correct nor good, after asking for **much** forgiveness—since your goal is **certainly** that your business [dealings], etc., should be conducted with integrity—based on this, every single day carries the **full** responsibility of your position, just as on the **first** day, a decade ago. And along with this, there is the full provision of strength to fulfill the position, and along with this, the full merit that comes with fulfilling the position.

Therefore, there is no place at all for such a state of mind or anything similar. One could elaborate at length on this, but you certainly do not need it at all. Furthermore, I am wary of the style of "moralizers," and therefore I will suffice with their conclusion, and most importantly—with the conclusion of the period of Galus, speedily in our days:

[And a redeemer shall come to Zion], and let us say Amen,

And may the [prophecy] be fulfilled: "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders."

## 10,753

11 Nissan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, Torah scholar, and Chassid,
Rabbi Mordechai, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Regarding your note on the *Likutei* for Parshas Ki Sisa—that since a person cannot **prohibit** something that is not [his], Aharon did not transgress the prohibition of idolatry with the gold of the calf because he did not acquire it—this is not the case. For even before it was fashioned into an idol, and even at the very beginning of its making, one transgresses the prohibition of "You shall not make for yourself a graven image," as explained [in the Rambam], etc.

The incident of the calf took place before the Oral Torah was taught to the Bnei Yisrael. They were obligated only by what was explicitly stated in the Ten Commandments: 1) **making** [an idol], 2) [an idol itself]. And even if you were to say that they had learned and fulfilled the four hundred chapters of idolatry that Avraham Avinu taught Yaakov (Zohar Vol. III, 165a), the fulfillment of this stringency **on their own** does not override the preservation of life (*pikuach nefesh*) for Aharon [after he saw the killing of Chur (cited in Rashi)].

This is unlike the principle that a person cannot prohibit something that is not his. Many of the discussions in the *Likutei*—**which are logical deductions** (and one should note the Tosafos in Shevuos 22b, end of side b)—must also hold true before the Oral Torah was taught. That is why they were included in the *Likutei*.

Based on the above, the well-known [question] regarding the matters of the *Chafetz Chaim* is answered simply: How did the Yisraelim perform circumcision at [night] (Shemos Rabbah 19:8)?

The answer is that the law that circumcision must be performed during the day was introduced only after the Giving of the Torah (Tosafos, s.v. *Mar*, Yevamos 72b). And even if you were to say that they observed this as well before the Torah was given, they would not have nullified the eating of the Pesach offering—which is forbidden to an uncircumcised person—because of this stringency.

Enclosed is the discussion of the student [may he live] in the *Likutei* regarding the above, which I hope will be of interest to you.

## 10 Tishrei 5759

## 10 Tishrei [sic]

B"H, Erev Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Iyar, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner for the educational institution "Oholei Torah,"
Hashem should keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

On various occasions, the special importance of the current year as a **Shmittah year** has been emphasized. And although the mitzvos connected with the Shmittah of lands are not practiced in the Diaspora, nevertheless, like other mitzvos that are not practiced in the present time, they exist here in a spiritual sense even in the present time and in the Diaspora, for all matters of the eternal Torah are above time and place. And since they exist, this means that their content must also be expressed in *maaseh b'poel* (actual deed), for **action is the essential thing**.

The content of Shmittah is that although a Jew has a field that belongs to him—and belongs to him according to Torah, which says that it is his and obligates him in *terumos* and *maaseros*, etc.—at the same time, the Ribono shel Olam says, "**For the earth is Mine**." A Jew must recognize that the true Master is the Ribono shel Olam, and this recognition is not merely a thought, but must be expressed in action, by leaving the field free and unworked for the **entire** year of Shmittah, so that even the produce of that year does not belong to the owner of the field, but is *hefker* (ownerless) for everyone, even for the animals of the field. And like all mitzvos, which must be performed with joy, he fulfills the mitzvah of Shmittah with joy, knowing the preciousness of a mitzvah, and there is no greater happiness than to fulfill the will of the Ribono shel Olam.

And regarding Shmittah, the Ribono shel Olam promised a **supernatural** reward also in material matters, that the harvest of the field in the sixth year will be threefold, for three full years.

One of the lessons from this, in all times and in all places, is that a Jew must know that although Torah says he should work in matters of livelihood according to the way of nature ("Six days you shall work and do all your labor"), when it comes to Yiddishkeit, to matters of Torah and mitzvos, then he is entirely removed from nature and stands not only under *hashgacha pratis* (Divine Providence), but also under a miraculous conduct.

And just as Shmittah is not a matter for "special" days of the year, but for a **whole year**, so too is Yiddishkeit in its fullest measure—not for exceptional days, like Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur and Shabbos, etc., but it must be observed the entire year and every day of the year, the weekdays, Shabbos, Yom Tov, etc.; and not, Heaven forbid, as a burden and a toil, but with the cheerfulness and *simcha shel mitzvah* (joy of the mitzvah).

This approach to Torah and mitzvos must, self-evidently, be implanted in Jewish children from their earliest youth, and this is the task of the educational institution **Oholei Torah**: to educate Jewish children in Torah, fear of Heaven, and *simcha shel mitzvah*—in accordance with the aforementioned, and it is successful in this.

It is to be hoped that the participants in the gathering, and in general the activists and friends of this highly important educational institution, will respond generously and give the institution their fullest support, in accordance with the supernatural content of the current Shmittah year. And the Ribono shel Olam will surely bless each and every one, *midah k'neged midah* (measure for measure), with a supernatural abundance in everything one needs, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With respect and blessing for success,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10756

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5733
