## 10757

[B"H]( #_ftn_717), 5 Iyar, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yitzchak Weil
Sdeh Eliyahu (Emek Beit Shean)

Greetings and blessings!

The acknowledgment of your [letter]( #_ftn_718) was delayed due to the doubts I had—and still have—as to whether any benefit would come of this, or the opposite. Nevertheless, for several reasons, I have decided to write, at the very least, briefly, since the matter at hand is fundamental. I will preface this by saying that you are not required to acknowledge receipt of this letter, and it goes without saying that you need not reply to it—neither out of courtesy nor for any other reason—since, apparently, that would be against your conscience.

The point of the response to all the sections of your letter can be explained [by way of a parable]( #_ftn_719): Imagine a person who has a very close relative who is not in good health, yet he deludes himself by saying that he is perfectly healthy. Furthermore, [in the language of the prophet]( #_ftn_720), he calls darkness light, claiming that the symptoms of his relative’s illness are, on the contrary, signs of health, and therefore he encourages them, and so on. There are two possible approaches here: (a) In order to maintain the relationship, one could say to him, "You are right, well done, continue on your path," or at the very least, avoid any response, leaving whatever happens to this sick relative to our Father in Heaven. (b) Since there is no chance the illness will be cured as long as the sick person persists in his aforementioned decision—and, on the contrary, tries to ensure that everyone around him is in a similar state, especially since the illness is contagious—then one must not consider whether it pleases the sick person or not. Instead, one must begin by quietly explaining the situation to him and pointing out his error, and if that does not help—and certainly if the situation worsens—to speak with him more openly.

The decision between these two approaches is provided in our Torah, the Torah of life, [as it is stated]( #_ftn_721), "You shall surely rebuke your neighbor," etc.—a positive commandment from the Torah. This is all the more true when the matter concerns fundamental issues, etc., [and as is explained in the Poskim]( #_ftn_722), distance does not separate the children of Israel from one another, [and in the words of our Sages, of blessed memory]( #_ftn_723), "All the children of Israel are responsible for one another." Moreover, this is also a directive in the Torah: that **every** person who has the ability to protest and does not protest, etc. (Shabbos 55a; **see there**).

To my great regret, no response was heard from you or your colleagues when you called darkness light and labeled matters that destroy religion as a "religious achievement," when you denied "with full force" that there exists a [psak din]( #_ftn_724) that was accepted unanimously, even though it was publicized, etc., and when you took charity funds belonging to the children of Israel for the benefit of the children of Israel in Eretz Yisrael and invested them in the establishment of non-Jews—among them known enemies of Israel—in the Holy Land, using various strange excuses and pretexts.

It is not my intention to accuse anyone, as that is not my concern; rather, it is a faint hope that, in the end, you will realize the truth of what has been caused by your silence and the silence of your colleagues. Naturally, whatever you say among yourselves where no one hears has no effect. May it be His will that this happens soon.

As mentioned, you are under no obligation to reply to my letter at all, for this is a matter between you and your conscience, as the current expression goes, or in the language of our Sages, of blessed memory, between you and the Ribono shel Olam.

With blessings.

## 10758

B"H, 7 Iyar, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter containing a request for a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh* dated 27 Nissan. At an opportune time, it will be read at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding the relationship between you that you write about: since it sometimes stems from a lack of **precision** and the necessary caution in observing the laws of *taharas hamishpachah*, and since a lack of knowledge (due to forgetfulness) leads to a deficiency in observance, you must study all the details of these laws once again.

All of this should be within the context of daily conduct according to Torah and *mitzvos*.

In matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, no matter how good the situation may be, there is always room to add, for they are connected to Hashem, Who is infinite.

With blessings.

Regarding what you wrote about the ailment that occurred, *l'o aleinu*, and the state of mind, etc.: since its entire "reality" exists only in the world of thought and "rumination," the more you divert your mind from all of this, the easier it will be for you; it will weaken this "reality" until it is nullified.

To hasten this and facilitate the diversion of your mind, it is advisable that you be occupied for at least a few hours a week outside the walls of your home, in a matter that requires being involved with people, etc.

Have the *mezuzos* checked.

Regarding the suggestion of visiting here: it is not advisable, for several reasons, including: a) The constant worry about how the children, *shiy*, are doing, etc., does not help to reduce tension or provide peace of mind. b) The same applies to "wandering about" when not at home, especially during the holidays, etc. c) The great merit of *Eretz Yisrael*—to increase peace of mind and body. And more.

## 10759

[B"H], 8 Iyar, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Noach and his wife, Mrs. Paula Moses
Ramat Gan

Shalom u’Bracha!

For some time now, I have intended to write to you following your visit here and our conversation, in addition to the news I have received in the interim regarding your health, etc. However, I was waiting for some matter that would serve as a pretext for writing to you. That reason presented itself yesterday, and therefore I am hastening my letter, as in my opinion, it is for the benefit of the many.

I am referring to what we discussed regarding a matter that I believe is a great necessity: that in the newspaper which you own, through Divine Providence, at least one page or more should be dedicated each week to the topics of the weekly Parsha and the mitzvos whose time is in that week, with the addition of practical halachic guidance on these matters—for ultimately, [action] is the essential thing. As we discussed at length then, since a significant portion of the newspaper’s readers are observant of Torah and mitzvos, and surely the newspaper’s intention is to provide for their needs as well, it is proper that the events of the week presented to the readers should reflect not only the political, economic, and similar spheres, but also the religious sphere—naturally, within the appropriate framework, as it is not the role of a newspaper at all to be a Shulchan Aruch or to issue halachic rulings, which belongs to a Rav who is a teacher of Torah.

I do not see a need to repeat what we discussed at length then, especially since the impression I was left with is that you do not need convincing on this from anyone else, considering "the rock from which you were hewn," your family background, your ancestors, etc. And as I recall, I also mentioned that although I am not an expert in the management of newspapers and the profits therein, etc., I am certain that through this, the number of readers will increase, and perhaps even the number of advertisers, etc.—although it is my hope that in your opinion, this factor is secondary to the main point: the role of a newspaper that wishes to satisfy the demands of a diverse and maximal audience, and especially according to the [statement of our Sages, of blessed memory], that all of Israel are believers, the children of believers.

And precisely in recent years, all of the above has even greater validity, since there is a growing demand among the youth—the so-called "secular" youth—everywhere, and especially in the Holy Land, to know what true Judaism is, the heritage of our fathers, the values of Judaism, etc., after having been educated without any knowledge of this, neither in school nor at home. And although it is simple that it is not the role of a newspaper to be a substitute for school, the point is to inform them about what is happening in this area and to satisfy the curiosity of many of the readers, etc.

The reason mentioned above that led me to mention all of the foregoing is that I received yesterday the advertisement/leaflet attached hereto, which in several points corresponds to the proposal I made during our conversation. This leaflet is further proof that the time has already arrived in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, for the printing of such a page. And all the more so in your newspaper, where, according to reports, you are the owners and can set the tone as you wish; this must be a (significant) part of the newspaper itself, and not an advertisement from the outside.

It is understood that there are several points to add to a page of this nature, in addition to what is printed in the attached leaflet, and in several points, there are also changes, etc. However, I am not entering into the details of this, but rather into the essence of the matter; and then, surely, you will find many true experts in the field of our true religion regarding the particulars.

I will permit myself to add one more general point, prefaced by the fact that if our entire Torah is called "Toras Emes" (the Torah of Truth), then this is all the more so regarding the terms in the Torah that relate to practical halacha. One of these terms is the concept of *devarim betelim* (idle words), regarding which our Torah’s *mussar* literature is extremely stringent, warning one to guard against them, etc., and there are also practical halachic rulings regarding this. The [precision] is that it is not referring to forbidden or repulsive things, but rather to things whose only negative point is that they are *devarim betelim*—that is, things that were spoken for a specific purpose, and when that purpose is not realized, the words become *betelim* (void). In our case, my intention was surely only for the good, and not, G-d forbid, to interfere in a business that is not my own, but rather for the sake of many of your readers, whose welfare you surely seek. And now, it is entirely in your hands to ensure that these words of mine will not fall into the category of *devarim betelim*.

Since in everything there is surely a good part, even though the matter has been delayed, in such a case every single day is important. From this, too, good can grow, [in the style] of the well-known saying, "The jealousy of scribes increases wisdom"—that if my proposal is accepted now, you will increase in your newspaper many times over in both quantity and quality, and the note appearing at the bottom of the page, "Please preserve the sanctity of the page," etc., will be justified in the fullest sense of the word.

In the course of time, I had news that your health had improved, and may it be His will that this, too, will continue to increase.

With respect and with blessings for good news in general, and regarding the aforementioned in particular.

## 10763

[B"H], Lag B'Omer, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 18th Annual Convention
of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and Peace!

On this auspicious day of Lag B'Omer, I send my greetings and blessing to all participants in the convention. May it be His will that it be successful to the fullest measure.

It has been emphasized many times that in all the significant historical events immortalized in our calendar, Jewish women have played a decisive role. This is also true regarding Lag B'Omer.

Lag B'Omer, as is known, reminds us of the episode involving the students of Rabbi Akiva, especially those who survived the plague—may we be spared—and who, together with their Rebbe, revived and secured the continuity of the **Torah Shebaal Peh**. Among them was the Tanna Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai (Rashbi), the author of the **Zohar**, whose Hillula is on Lag B'Omer. Along with his contribution to **Nigleh D'Torah**, it is thanks to him that the continuity of **Pnimius HaTorah**, the Torah of Kabbalah, was also secured.

And these students of Rabbi Akiva—our Sages of blessed memory tell us—saved the Torah at that time (Yevamos 62b).

In what does the role of the Jewish woman consist at this critical moment in the history of our people?

Our Sages of blessed memory brought this out clearly in the narrative regarding Rabbi Akiva. The Gemara relates in detail how the ascent of Rabbi Akiva, from the state of an ignorant shepherd to the level of the greatest Tanna of his generation, was due to a woman—his loyal and courageous wife, Rachel. And Rabbi Akiva himself publicly confirmed this before the masses, saying to his students, **"Mine and yours are hers"**—"Everything that I have learned, and that you have learned, is thanks to her" (Kesuvos 63a).

This means that the entire edifice of the Torah Shebaal Peh, which is the foundation and existence of the Jewish people, is actually owed to a Jewish woman!

Since this story, with all its details, has been told and immortalized in the Gemara, it is a clear and distinct directive for all Jewish women in all generations.

The practical lesson from this is that every Jewish woman receives from the Ribono shel Olam tremendously great powers, with far-reaching possibilities, not only for herself and for her husband and children, but also for the entire Jewish people.

Referring to the main theme of this year's convention: **"He shall turn the heart of the fathers to the children, and the heart of the children to their fathers"**—or, as the expression is used now, to create a bridge between the young and old generations—it is clear, and also understandable, that the woman occupies a very important place in this. Especially since in the matter of **kiruv halevavos** (drawing hearts closer), which is in the realm of **regesh** (emotion), the woman has been gifted with a very great measure of sensitivity and understanding—not to mention that in the chinuch and character-building of children, from their earliest youth, the woman and mother, the **akeres habayis**, has a very great and essential influence.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that in the spirit of the aforementioned theme of the convention, and primarily through the increased activities that will grow from it—together with the activities of **all** Jews, men and women, young and old—we should soon merit the realization of the aforementioned prophecy, which begins with the words: **"Remember the Torah of Moshe My servant"**—in a way that this remembrance is expressed in daily life and actual conduct; which will bring closer the continuation of the prophecy: **"Behold, I am sending you Eliyahu HaNavi"**—the herald of the Geulah Amisita VeShleima through Mashiach Tzidkeinu; at which time the conclusion will be fulfilled: **"And he shall turn the heart of the fathers to the children, and the heart of the children to their fathers."**

Then, the prophecy of Dovid HaMelech, the sweet singer of Israel, will also be fulfilled: **"And His glory shall fill the whole earth, Amen and Amen"**—through the fact that the glory of Hashem will first penetrate and fill the hearts of all children and all parents, all sons and daughters of the people of Israel.

With blessings for success in both spiritual and material matters, and for good tidings regarding all the above,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10,757

B”H, 20 Iyar, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Shabbetai Rosen, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

It was a pleasant surprise to receive your letter of 30 Nissan, after the long hiatus since our meeting, and even more so because of the content of your letter, in which you write about a Mivtza Mezuzah program, similar to Mivtza Tefillin, etc. This gives me strong hope that to the extent of his ability, you are active in spreading Yiddishkeit and its values, and in a way that highlights one of the primary points of the mitzvah of mezuzah—publicity. After all, the place for a mezuzah is on the entrance of one’s home, facing outward, the opposite of the well-known slogan, “Be a Jew in your home and a man in the street.” The results of that slogan did not take long to manifest—both at the time, tearing the soul apart, and after a period of time, when the home itself became like the "street."

Naturally, I will reflect once again [on the program for the aforementioned Mivtza](#_ftn_752) that you raised in your letter.

I write “once again” because several years ago, when an attempt was made to do this, they encountered specific difficulties. In this Mivtza, one must visit the homeowner in his home, and the mezuzah and everything necessary for affixing it must be ready at hand. Furthermore, one usually needs to convince the members of the household as well; it is not enough to convince the head of the family—none of which applies to Mivtza Tefillin. For this reason, they only endeavored to affix mezuzos in special cases.

Nevertheless, and especially according to the teachings of Chassidus, which state that [every matter is by Divine Providence](#_ftn_753), and having received your letter prompting this matter, it is certainly an instruction that I must reflect upon this matter once again.

It is not clear from your letter whether you are continuing in the same [position](#_ftn_754) and field in which you were engaged while you were in New York. If so, you naturally have a great interest in what is permitted to be disclosed, and if that is the case, the more detail, the better—and my thanks are extended to you in advance.

With respect and with blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 10780

[20 Iyar, 5733]

In accordance with his age, it is appropriate that he take an interest in a shidduch.

Regarding eating and diet—it is not so much about what one eats (provided it is **kosher as required**), but rather the **intent** behind the eating: whether it is merely to satisfy a craving or hunger, or in order to be healthy and, consequently, to perform good deeds, etc.

See also Shulchan Aruch, Orach Chaim 231.

The normal life of **each and every one** of the Children of Israel is **only** when it is according to Torah and mitzvos (Shulchan Aruch).

If one diminishes this or changes it, it is [like] a fish that has jumped from the sea or river onto dry land—even during the moments that it is alive, it is merely twitching and convulsing, not living a normal life.

I will mention this at the tziyun.

## 10-Tevet 5782

22 Iyar, 5773
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the G-d-fearing, man of action, engaged in communal needs,
Mr. Yirmiyahu, known as Prof. Branover,
Shalom u’Bracha!

[Russian]

[Free translation]

Since it is much easier to write in Lashon HaKodesh here in the secretariat than in Russian, and taking into account that you know Lashon HaKodesh, I am continuing to write in Lashon HaKodesh. However, I emphasize that in the future, you should continue to write in Russian for the same reason—that for the time being, at least, it is easier for you to write in Russian than in Lashon HaKodesh.

I acknowledge receipt of your letter from Rosh Chodesh Iyar, along with the booklet "Min HaMa'amakim." Many thanks.

And after asking your forgiveness, it is a pity that you titled it "Min HaMa'amakim," rather than the standard scriptural phrasing **MiMa'amakim** (and I believe I saw somewhere that it was initially titled "MiMa'amakim"). It is even more of a pity because people will surely link the change to the Latin translation "De Profundis," which consists of two separate words. That is to say, not only did you not choose the scriptural phrasing, but it is as if you are giving precedence to Latin over, l’havdil, Lashon HaKodesh. And even from a scientific perspective, "De Profundis" is merely a translation of the original "MiMa'amakim." Even if, on the face of it, this is a small matter and what difference does it make, nevertheless, one cannot always evaluate what is small and what is not so small, or even great and important.

It is understood that I know one does not complain about the past, but my intention is to correct this for the future, when a second edition is printed.

Incidentally, I have just received the "Intercom" booklet (Iyar) from the organization of Charedi academics here, which contains this article in English.

Regarding the content of your letter, many thanks for the good news concerning several activities of the organization of academics in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. May it be His will that the statement of our Sages, "He who has one hundred wants two hundred; he who has two hundred wants four hundred," be fulfilled immediately in you and all those participating with you in these activities. For if this is true in material matters, it is all the more so in spiritual matters, and especially in the dissemination of authentic Yiddishkeit, our Torah and its mitzvos, which are our life and the length of our days.

In my opinion, as we have spoken several times, great alacrity is required here, at least regarding the registration and initial correspondence with all those who have the hope of eventually joining the organization of academics. My intention is that even though for some of them it is possible that there is not yet a clear plan on how to **influence** them, etc., it is imperative that in close proximity to the arrival of academics to our Holy Land, they be notified that this organization of academics exists, its address, and propaganda material—at least in very brief form—along with an invitation to register as a simple member without any prior commitment, as we discussed here. The benefit of this is understood and simple, as it forms a connection and informs all the olim that there is a religious organization that they can join as members, etc., etc.

Continuing with the above regarding matters that have priority and are time-sensitive, this also applies to matters connected with the upcoming festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah. This is the most appropriate time to arouse [the public] regarding the matter of setting fixed times for Torah study and to speak regarding the preciousness of the Torah and its importance, and how it is a Torah and instruction even regarding practical action in daily life in these days and in every place, and especially in our Holy Land. And even if there is not enough time to do all that is required before the festival of Shavuos, there is still room to complete it in the days following, with the introduction that we have just come from the time of the giving of our Torah, and therefore we are raising the matter, etc.

Following what I told you regarding the payment of a secretary’s salary for an entire year—though of course you must notify us here from time to time of the payment dates and the amount, etc.—in addition to this, in connection with the Torah campaign mentioned above, an additional sum of $500 has been allocated from here, and they will provide it to you when you have need of it. You should consult among yourselves how to use this sum, whether through shluchim or propaganda matters such as leaflets, circular letters, and the like.

Regarding your writing about whom to include in the work of the organization of academics, it is understood that you must decide this on the spot after speaking with the candidates, etc.

Certainly, in our land as well, during the summer months, students (even those taking summer courses) have more time at their disposal than during the academic season, and this also applies to students among the new olim. Therefore, perhaps it is worth looking into how to utilize this for the goals and programs of the organization of academics.

Regarding your writing, continuing our discussion about establishing a city in Eretz Yisrael whose entire life would be based on Torah and mitzvos, and you write an explanation that it would be a city of academics: one must be careful even in speaking about this, so as not to instill fear and dread in certain offices that it is the intention of the organization or the intention of Chabad to build and establish such a city, for then they might not want to help at all, as they would be most opposed to a religious city of this type. As we see that even regarding the city of Bnei Brak, they are looking for various ways and stratagems to change, Heaven forbid, the conduct that has existed there until now.

In addition to the above, it seems to me that in general, Eretz Yisrael is not yet prepared for such an academic city, since concentrating academics in one city where they would be the majority of the residents could lead to several frictions among them and sharp differences of opinion regarding the management of the city, etc., since all are academics and all are wise, etc. And likewise, regarding influencing their surroundings, it will succeed more when they live together with students and simple people, for then a living example of religious academics makes a strong impression on them, which is not the case with a living example of one academic regarding another academic. And there are other details that are not in favor of a plan for an academic city for the aforementioned purpose.

You do not mention the state of your health or that of your family, and my hope is that everything is in order.

And approaching the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send to you, your family, and all those who accompany you, my blessing in the traditional phrasing for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

With a blessing for success and good tidings.

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to a scientist, and my hope is that its content will also interest you. And it is understood that you have permission to use it in a way that will bring benefit.

## 10785

27 Iyar

Mr. Yitzchak

[Russian], [Free Translation]

## 10 Teves 5733

[Late Iyar, 5733]

To the members of the Kollel, may they live:

During my visit to the Kollel today, I saw a paradox: there is good material here that could succeed as a Kollel, and in a wonderful way at that, provided it takes on the proper form...

Since it is accepted that a member of a Kollel should be a mature individual, a person of substance, who stands by his own convictions when he decides that his soul desires Torah—and consequently, in everything related to this, he will act with the **necessary** vigor and does not require prodding, supervision, or someone standing over him to "nudge" him, etc.—

Therefore, if there are such individuals among you, you should certainly gather **immediately** and choose from among yourselves, and inform me who will be responsible from this point forward for the order of studies, punctuality, cleanliness, etc., **in accordance with the command** of our Sages: "Adorn yourself before Him." And it is understood that you have the authority to institute fines, etc.

If there are no such individuals, I am not coming with complaints, Heaven forbid, [and just as one receives reward, etc.], and the resolution of this doubt—**whichever way it may be**—should be sent as soon as possible.

## 10,790

[Late Iyar, 5733]

The **interpretation** of the news you wrote that you received (that the aforementioned has become engaged) — in my opinion, it is clear:

1) Since there was still a bit of doubt in her mind—whether the aforementioned’s relationship with her was deep, at least to the extent that he would want to adapt to her character, to compromise at least in matters **most** essential to her, to show that he is not entirely enslaved to his own views, etc.—

The aforementioned news has completely nullified any such doubt.

2) Since, according to the custom in a **very** limited circle, even when the breaking of a shidduch is good and necessary—nonetheless, **when possible**, one tries to wait until the other side has become engaged—

This, too, was granted to her from Above.

*

According to our Torah of truth—a person, even the greatest of Bnei Yisrael, is "close to himself"—and as a necessary result of this, when he sees that he is not being pressed a second and third time after he has said "no," he becomes disappointed, or even embittered, **etc.**,

And to such an extent that sometimes he does not want to acknowledge the reality:

1) That this is proof that even the request the first time was not "with all your heart."

2) That something which is not suitable (and more than that)—the knowledge that it was cancelled, etc.—is truly for the best in a way that is visible and revealed. And one must offer thanks to Hashem for this.

*

I will mention it at the Tziyun, bli neder, that you should be blessed with all this (in the accepted phrasing), that you should receive the Torah with joy and inwardness, and that you should become engaged soon with your basherter, with peace of mind and with joy.

## 10757

By the Grace of G-d
Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Chaim [Grade] 
Greetings and Blessings,

It has been quite some time since I have heard from you directly, though I have inquired and received regards about you through mutual friends. Furthermore, when one wishes to receive a greeting from someone gifted with a literary talent, one of the ways is to look at what has recently been published from his pen. Yet, that does not compare to a direct and personal greeting.

Therefore, I was especially pleased that a letter from your wife arrived at the secretariat, which gives me the opportunity to write these lines to you, and also to ask you to convey to your wife my thanks for the greeting and for creating this opportunity for me.

I will begin with a comment regarding an expression in your wife’s letter and react to it; presumably, you will also convey this to your wife with additional explanation if necessary, although as I understand it, she does not require it. I am referring to what your wife writes, that you are "a modern Jew with a *Misnagdish*-Lithuanian tradition."

My position on this is that the very word "*Misnaged*" is a matter of negation—a negative attitude toward something. From this, it is understood that when one sees that a mistake has been made in calculation and the matter is actually entirely positive, a fundamental change is not required; rather, the opposition is nullified of its own accord and automatically. What is required is to have the inner strength to express this publicly: that despite having been raised in an upbringing and environment where a prejudice against this matter prevailed, once one perceives the truth, one accepts it.

From our meetings at Chassidic *farbrengens*, from what I have heard about you, and also from your correspondence and literary works, there is no doubt in my mind that despite the so-called *Misnagdish* tradition, the warmth with which your writing is imbued is in complete harmony with a Chassidic feeling. I believe that you feel this yourself, and what is even more relevant, that your readers feel it too, seeing that in your description of a "*Misnaged*," you smuggle in feelings that were drawn from Chassidic sources.

In the same vein, I take a position regarding the beginning of the aforementioned expression—"modern Jew." For the concept of a "modern" Jew, which was created by the so-called "*Haskalah*," has long since gone out of style. On the contrary, the more truly "modern" a Jew is today, the further he is from that modernity which created a rift between the "Jew in his tent" and the "person in his public life," and which waged war against the "Jew in his tent" to the point that it turned the Jew into a servant and follower of the "person"—read: a *goy*, *lehavdil*. Today’s Jew is, specifically, a proud Jew, and is becoming ever closer to the "old-new" Torah. Although it was given approximately 3,500 years ago, it is still new and fresh, according to the expression of our Sages [of blessed memory] : "In your eyes, they should be as new every day." This is seen especially among Jews who were subjected to the Communist regime for over a jubilee of years and remained Jews, and emerged from there as Jews—which, unfortunately, is not the case with those who held on to various "isms."

A similar tendency is seen even in the field of science, which, precisely in modern times, has taken a new turn in the direction of seeking ever more unity in the entire world—exactly the opposite of 100 years ago, when science held that the world was divided into various separate fields, etc. Furthermore, modern archaeology has also confirmed the accuracy of the narrative of the *Tanach*, in contrast to the so-called *Maskilim* and adherents of "Jewish Science" that grew out of Germany—the same country that produced German "culture," including Hitler and his heirs, may their names be blotted out.

Presumably, this letter is longer than you anticipated. I think, however, that perhaps it is actually too short relative to the matters of its content.

I will conclude with the traditional wish of many generations in connection with *Chag HaShavuos*, the time of the giving of our Torah, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for the good—to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness, together with your wife, *tichyeh*, for long and good days and years.

With respect and blessing,

P.S. I take the liberty of writing the following, and it is self-evident why this comes on a separate page, and that is:

Knowing your relationship with our friend President Shazar, *shlita*, and knowing that you took an active part in making his visit to me easier, despite those who did not want to allow it,

I take the liberty of making the suggestion that you strengthen your connection with our friend, especially in these days of deeper experience for him due to the change in his official [status], etc. And presumably, you will also arouse others who are under your influence to do so.

Since you are closely acquainted with his state of mind, you will certainly find the appropriate way for this, [and words] that come from the heart enter the heart and accomplish their effect. It is certainly not necessary to elaborate on this for you.

Because of this point, this letter is being sent "Special Delivery."

## 10798

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished R' Nissim Ben-Chaim
Rechov HaYehudim, Beit HaKeranot, Apt. 6
Old City, Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established,

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter, in which you write that, with the help of Hashem, you have merited to be among the first of the congregants of the [Tzemach Tzedek Synagogue](#_ftn_798) in the Old City to move in and reside in the Jewish Quarter of the Old City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established. May it be His will that this be in a good and auspicious hour.

Since you daven in this synagogue, which is named after my revered father-in-law, the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, and [a name](#_ftn_799) is a significant matter—for it is the inheritance of the Tzemach Tzedek for generations, in a physical sense, and all the more so in a spiritual sense—when one davens in this synagogue, which includes the courtyard and all that pertains to it, one is in the domain of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek. He was a leader and a *moreh tzedek* (righteous teacher) for his generation and for all the generations that followed him, especially through his halachic rulings, which instruct and illuminate the earth and those who dwell upon it to this very day.

My hope is strong that you will do everything within your power, with a "righteous accounting" that is in accordance with the will of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek—both in your day-to-day conduct and in the deeds and activities to support all the affairs of the synagogue, both physically and spiritually. From you, all those who merit to settle in Jerusalem, the walled city, may it be rebuilt and established, will see and do likewise, knowing with certainty the teaching of [our Sages](#_ftn_800), of blessed memory, that the name Jerusalem (*Yerushalayim*) indicates *yirah-shalem*—a complete fear of Hashem. The Holy One, blessed be He, assists everyone, especially in Jerusalem, our holy city.

With blessings for a successful settling in, both physically and spiritually, and in anticipation of the time of the giving of our Torah—in the traditional style of the Rebbe’s house—to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

## 10,799

[B"H,](javascript:void(0)) the days of limitation leading up to Zeman Matan Toraseinu, 5733

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Aharon [HaKohen,](javascript:void(0)) 
Reines St. 5, Kiryat Moshe
Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of the 27th of Iyar, in which you write regarding your dilemma concerning the promises made to you regarding the list of candidates for the Knesset elections and the change that has occurred in this regard in the present,

It is understood that you must stand firm that they fulfill the promise, especially since the matter concerns a party that champions and declares itself to be a [religious party.](javascript:void(0)) 

However, if you will forgive me, we have seen a deterioration in recent times in the strength of the conscience of those who determine matters within the party. In the style known today, one says one thing and the next day says the opposite, and in the common parlance, "vehemently denies" that he ever said otherwise. This is true even regarding a matter that is not only [destined to be revealed](javascript:void(0)) in the future, but is already well-known from the past.

As one example: regarding the well-known letter of [psak din](javascript:void(0)) from the Chief Rabbinate concerning the amendment of the "Who is a Jew" law, they vehemently denied (a) that such a letter exists, (b) after that—that they received such a letter, (c) they then admitted that they did receive such a letter, but that it was not a psak din but merely a temporary instruction, and so on and so forth. All those who set the policy gave their stamp of approval to this conduct, and each one strives to publicize and declare that everything mentioned is a "religious achievement."

I must admit my own error in having expected that the younger generation would keep their own promises—that is to say, that what they said, they would actually do. Then came the bitter surprise that they voted against the Halacha. And not only that, but they strove with all their might that specifically one of their own, and one of their leaders, should inherit the place of [the one](javascript:void(0)) who was removed from his position because of his vote in favor of [the word](javascript:void(0)) of Hashem, which is Halacha. And from this, too, they made a "religious achievement" to protect the education of the children of Israel, etc., etc.—the very same explanation used for the "law" of Who is a Jew, the Law of Return, etc.

The relevance of these lines to the content of your letter is not only because when a person feels a deep, internal pain, he cries out and screams without considering whether it will help, for sorrow is not subject to calculation, etc. Rather, it has a direct connection to the content of your letter, for the gates of excuses and pretexts have not been locked. Surely, the one they wish to place in the position promised to you will also find that it is a "religious achievement" for the salvation of the religion of Moshe and Israel, and for the salvation of the Torah of Israel and the Land of Israel.

Therefore, regarding the practical side: if you have the backing of physical and material power—control over financial funds, the distribution of positions, or the like—so that you can stand your ground if they do not wish to fulfill the promise, then there is a chance that the promise will be kept. This is not the case if your claim is based solely on the argument that when one makes a promise, one must stand by one's word and commitment.

It is not worthwhile to dwell at length on this painful and distressing matter, especially when it is done in our Holy Land and they cloak these matters in the guise of fear of Heaven, etc., as written above.

To conclude with a positive note: as we stand on the eve of the time of the giving of our Torah, the Torah of Truth, eventually [Truth](javascript:void(0)) will sprout from the earth—the known land, the land, our Holy Land—and the [word](javascript:void(0)) of our G-d (the word of Hashem, which is Halacha) will stand forever, regarding all the Halachos, including the Halacha of "Who is a Jew" and what constitutes true Judaism, etc.

I wish you—in the style customary in the Rebbe’s house—to receive the Torah with joy and with inwardness.

With respect and blessing for good tidings.

## 10,802

10,802

B"H, Erev Shavuos, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. ...

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter of the 9th of Iyar was received with pleasure, albeit with some delay.

I was especially pleased to read about the progress in returning to the source, in the style inherent to the essence of every Jew, [as our Sages of blessed memory state](#_ftn_812), "Yisrael are believers, the children of believers." Indeed, one of the foundations of the Jewish faith is [that the deed](#_ftn_813) is the essential thing. This is also emphasized in the giving of the Torah, in the content of the Ten Commandments, which are entirely about action—with the exception of the first statement, which establishes the foundation for the fulfillment of all the actions. Even in this, there is a most practical point, as we have seen in our generation, the generation of Hitler and his successors. All those who based the commandments of "Do not murder" and "Do not steal," etc., on philosophical systems and moral theories founded merely on human intellect, not only failed to uphold these commandments, but actually turned the concepts of murder and theft into a philosophical and moral system, and so on and so forth, to a degree beyond all imagination.

Based on the statement of [our Sages of blessed memory](#_ftn_814) that "one mitzvah leads to another," I am certain that the mitzvos you are fulfilling and writing about will surely, most surely, lead to further mitzvos. As an [eshes chayil](#_ftn_815) and [the foundation](#_ftn_816) of the home, the entire household will conduct itself and progress in the aforementioned direction, and [the merit of your ancestors](#_ftn_817) will assist you.

With respect and blessings—in the style customary in our family, and also in the Slonim family—for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for good tidings in all the aforementioned matters.

10,803

12 Sivan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all those involved in *chinuch* on the path of *kedushah* in particular,
And to all those involved who cherish Torah and *mitzvos* in general,
May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

As we stand on the day of the *siyum* and conclusion of the *tashlumin* days of the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, and in continuation of what was discussed and emphasized at the *farbrengens* of the festival, as well as those preceding and following it—based on the teaching of our Sages that it was only (and immediately) when the Jewish people said, "Our children will be our guarantors (that we will keep the Torah)" that the Holy One, Blessed be He, gave the Torah to the Jewish people—I take the liberty to add a matter that is timely. It is a holy obligation upon every single person who has the ability to act, and a great merit, to do everything within their power to ensure that every Jewish boy and girl is educated with an education of *taharas hakodesh*—both during the hours dedicated to study and during the other hours of the day and night (and, in fact, even more so).

Although this obligation and this merit are relevant throughout the entire year, they are most potent during the days of the time of the giving of our Torah and the days adjacent to them—days that serve as a remembrance of those days in the first year of the exodus from the land of Egypt, when this guarantee was first given.

I would also like to point out the unique opportunities available during these months in many countries—in Eretz Yisrael and abroad—where studies in many schools are suspended (or at least the hours of study are reduced) for many weeks.

Consequently, a large number of teachers, guides, and educators are freed from their regular work, and they will surely cooperate with great desire in the establishing and spreading of *chinuch* on the path of *kedushah*.

Furthermore, it is possible—and therefore mandatory—to bring thousands and tens of thousands of students into appropriate summer camps, in a manner where they will be in a **unified** atmosphere, saturated with genuine Yiddishkeit for a significant period of time.

This is in contrast to the rest of the year, when it is impossible to avoid some contradiction between the atmosphere of the school, the home, the street, and so on.

This is a unique opportunity, the value and influence of which are of the utmost importance. Therefore, every effort and exertion in this regard is worthwhile, and in all of this, the promise will surely be fulfilled: "You have labored and you have found."

May it be the will of Hashem that every one of the educators, those involved in *chinuch*, and anyone who has the ability to act—both personally and by activating all those over whom they have influence—should do all that has been mentioned. May they establish camps upon camps of Jewish boys and girls, of whom all who see them will recognize that they are the seed blessed by Hashem, students of His Torah—the Torah of truth and the Torah of life—and observers of His *mitzvos*.

Until we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy: "I will pour out My spirit upon all flesh, and your sons and daughters will prophesy," and (as stated before that): "And you shall praise the name of Hashem your G-d, Who has dealt wondrously with you," with the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, who will rule from sea to sea (in Eretz Yisrael and abroad) and from the river to the ends of the earth.

With respect and blessing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 1070

1070

[B"H, 17th of the Third Month, 5733] 

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, Montreal, on the occasion of the *Siyum*

May Hashem grant them life,

Peace and Blessing!

In anticipation of the *Siyum*, I send my blessing to the graduating students, and indeed to all students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim wherever they may be, *shlita*. May they go from strength to strength in their Torah study with increased diligence and application, studying with the intent to act and to fulfill the *mitzvos* with beauty and joy.

As has been emphasized many times, the significance of this *Siyum* is not as the world interprets it, but rather as preparation and an ascent to a higher level—or, in the well-known expression, **"we ascend in matters of holiness."**

Since the date of this *Siyum* falls at the conclusion of the third month—the month in which the Torah was given to the "third" people, by the "third" [Moshe], on the third day—this is the place to stir once again, in continuation of what was discussed at the *farbrengen* and reiterated in the letter of the day of the *Siyum* and the conclusion of the *tashlumin* days of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah.

It is a sacred obligation and a great privilege for each and every one—and all the more so for the students and alumni of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim—to do what is within their power. First and foremost, this is to be done through a living example and through words that come from the heart, so that every Jewish boy and girl will be educated with an education of *taharas hakodesh*. This is especially true during the summer months, when there are unique opportunities to accomplish and achieve great and hidden things in this regard.

Happy is the portion of all those who bring the hearts of Jewish children closer to their Father in Heaven—a true *kiruv* through actual deeds, by studying Torah and fulfilling *mitzvos* every day, as is known from the teaching of our Sages in their explanation of the *Mishnah*, "Two are holding onto a *tallis*," etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that the following be fulfilled in them, and in all those who will be educated with an education of *taharas hakodesh* through their influence, and in general: "A person who sanctifies himself a little below is sanctified much from above." As has been discussed many times, however much a person sanctifies himself below, it is but "a little" in comparison to above. And the attribute of goodness is abundant, such that from above they sanctify him "much," even in relation to the level of Above.

Until we merit the fulfillment of the prophecy that knowledge, wisdom, and truth will increase, as it is said: "For the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem," and "they shall no longer teach each man his brother and each man his neighbor, for they shall all know Me, from the smallest to the greatest."

With blessings for great success and for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,807

10,807

[B"H](#_ftn_850), 17 Sivan, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the graduating students and all participants in the first graduation ceremony of Beis Chana - Chabad in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established soon,

May Hashem grant you life,

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the news regarding the first graduation—an important and heart-warming event in its own right, in addition to the special *nachas ruach* it causes me, given that the institution is named after my mother, my teacher, the Rabbanit, of blessed memory.

May it be the will of Hashem that the following be fulfilled in the students in general, and the graduates in particular: "I have been as a wonder unto many" —both regarding diligence and perseverance in studies, and regarding their purpose: conduct that is appropriate in daily life, and in a manner of *mosif v'holech* (ever-increasing). As has been discussed many times, a "completion" (siyum) applies to matters that are not essential, but there is no such thing as a "completion" or a break, *chas v'shalom*, in matters of our Torah, which is our life, and in conduct according to its *mitzvos*, of which it is said: "Which a man shall do and live by them."

From this it is also understood that the summer season, which is called the "vacation season," applies only to secular studies and matters of permission (*reshus*), but this is not the case regarding holy studies and all matters of goodness and holiness. For every Jewish man and woman, as a preface to the Giving of the Torah, was commanded: "And you shall be unto Me a kingdom of priests and a holy nation". And although this is phrased as a command, it is also a promise.

Moving from one subject to a related one: since we are currently in the month of the Giving of the Torah, Jewish women and girls have an important and primary share in this aforementioned command and promise, as our Sages of blessed memory explain the verse stated as a preface to this: "Thus shall you say to the House of Jacob"—these are the women (first, and afterwards) "and tell the Children of Israel"—these are the men.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that all the graduates, and through them their families, and all the participants in this celebration, and through them those who will be influenced by them, be permeated with the spirit of the Torah, which is eternal. It is eternal not only in the sense that it will not be replaced, but that it is in its full strength in every place, at every time, every day, and every hour, regarding every Jewish son and daughter, throughout the entire duration of a person's life on earth, in thought, speech, and action—and action is the essential thing.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings in all the aforementioned,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,811

[20 Sivan, 5733]

[It is well known](#_ftn_867) the **halachic ruling** that "a single judge cannot judge alone, except for One (Hashem)," and this is especially true in an educational institution, [which requires](#_ftn_869) an administration and practical oversight. And as for the fact that such-and-such individuals act to the contrary—the damage they cause thereby to the institutions (and to themselves) makes the fulfillment of the aforementioned ruling even more imperative. And this is easy to understand. And it is a mitzvah to publicize this ruling of the Mishnah.

## 10,717

10,717

[B"H], Erev Rosh Chodesh Tammuz, 5733
Brooklyn.

To the Editorial Board of "Bitaon Chabad,"
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following a hiatus of quite some time, on the 28th of Sivan, a portion of the material [for the Bitaon] was received, with the request that it be proofread here and that we notify them, etc., with the intention of publishing it... by the 12th of Tammuz!

Before I respond to this, I wish to clarify the following, and by way of introduction: "Bitaon Chabad" must be as consistent as possible with its name. Consequently, the responsibility is understood (as is the privilege—which should **increase** the level of attention even more, **etc.**). It is also obvious that one must primarily be wary of those who seek a pretext [to criticize], rather than those who teach merit.

It is also obvious that the responsibility is **many times greater** regarding anything brought within it in the name of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im.

Given how obvious this is, I will not elaborate, especially since this has been written about previously, and faithful promises were made, **etc., etc.**

**And among the many** matters that, on the face of it at least, contradict the aforementioned—I will address the most severe one, and may it be Hashem’s will that they explain the matter and the difficulties be resolved.

There is printed therein [a story] "that occurred with the Alter Rebbe" ("naturally" without indicating any source) that he ruled the meat was kosher, and afterwards... at the request of the Shach, he retracted... **and declared it treif**, and because of this, **the entire city** did not eat meat that Shabbos (I do not have the text before me now—but this is the content **in essence**)—**and nothing more**, without any addition or note regarding this at all from the editorial board!

The wonder of the matter is—even if we were talking about a novice [student] **of a single day**, how can they print such a thing without any "note, at least by way of possibility"? And if they did not pay attention to the above at all—after the stumbling block that occurred in a similar vein in the past (though not **actual theft**) and the promise, etc.—why would there be any change in this in the future?

With blessings for good tidings, finally,

**M. Schneerson**

10,826

10,826

B"H, 12 Tammuz, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of "Gan Yisrael,"
May Hashem keep them alive.

Greetings and Blessings!

Transcribed herewith is the text of the blessing which the Rebbe shlita was gracious enough to send to the Gan Yisrael camps in connection with their opening this year.

Secretary

B"H, Days of Redemption, Tammuz 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To "Gan Yisrael," 
May Hashem keep them alive.

Greetings and Blessings!

May the opening of "Gan Yisrael" and the entire duration of their stay there be with success in all matters. This is especially true since this year is the seventh year, which is a Shabbos unto Hashem, and is auspicious for an increase in Torah and mitzvos, and for drawing down "shuvah v'nachas" —true pleasure—in matters of both body and soul together. It is also the centennial year of the histalkus-hillula of the Maggid, the Light of the World, and [a time] to hasten the fulfillment of the prophecy in our parsha: "A staff shall arise from Yisrael"—this is Melech HaMoshiach—who shall have dominion from sea to sea and from the river to the ends of the earth, and "Yisrael shall perform valiantly."

With blessings for the Festival of Redemption,

**Menachem Schneerson**

**Gan Yisrael**: Literally (producing fruits appropriate **for Yisrael**) and as implied—its cultivation (through the fruits, one makes a **dwelling** and a permanent home **for Yisrael**—and see the maamar "Basi L'Gani" (5710) by the Baal HaGeulah).

**The Seventh**: And all sevenths are beloved (Vayikra Rabbah 29:11).

**Auspicious for an increase**: Sforno (Behar 25:4).

**Increase in Torah**: See Berachos (35b): "Is it possible that a person plows... and [still] studies Torah...?"

**And mitzvos**: (Through the increase in) study, which leads to (an increase in) action.

**True pleasure**: See the Reshimot of the Tzemach Tzedek to Tehillim (92:1 and in the supplements there).

**Body and soul**: In spirituality, these are: mitzvos (the limbs, his bones) and Torah (the blood—which is the soul—his life force)—see Tanya, Chapter 23 (and the glosses of the Tzemach Tzedek there); Likutei Torah, Bamidbar 13a.

**Light of the World**: Introduction of the sons of the Alter Rebbe to his Shulchan Aruch.

**This is Melech HaMoshiach**: Rambam, Hilchos Melachim, beginning of Chapter 11.

**Dominion... earth**: Tehillim 72:8.

**Yisrael shall perform valiantly**: See Zohar, end of this week's parsha.

10,829

10,829

Motzaei Shabbos, 15 Tammuz, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

Following the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz—on which the Ribono shel Olam redeemed not only the Nasi, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, but also "all who cherish our holy Torah, who observe the mitzvos, and all who are called by the name of Yisrael"—

And as we stand at the conclusion and seal of the forty days of the giving of our Torah, which the Ribono shel Olam gave to Yisrael only (and immediately) when they said, "Our children will be our guarantors (that we will fulfill the Torah),"

I come once again to reiterate what has been discussed many times regarding the immense importance, the absolute necessity, and the great privilege of doing everything possible in the education of every single son and daughter of Yisrael on the foundation of purity and holiness, with ever-increasing strength and intensity, beginning with the education of the very youngest.

This is, of course, also understood from the verse: "From the mouths of babes and sucklings You have established strength (and 'strength' refers only to Torah)... to silence the enemy and the avenger"—as the Baal HaSimcha elaborated in his maamar, "And the Yehudim accepted what they had begun to do" (at the time of the giving of the Torah).

There is also a special connection here to the days of "Bein HaMetzarim" that are approaching, in the style of our Sages: "The cure precedes the affliction," for this is the way to silence the enemy and the avenger.

This is in addition to the fact that, at all times, the world exists only because of the breath of children studying Torah.

It is understood that education in mitzvos (in addition to the aforementioned study of Torah) is also essential and vital, and it impacts the entire life of the student, as it is written: "Educate a youth according to his way, and even when he grows old, he will not depart from it."

This includes—and is primarily focused on—education in the giving of tzedakah and acts of loving-kindness.

In the words of the verse: "For I have known him (an expression of affection; and why have I known him? Because he commands) his children and his household... to perform tzedakah and justice."

Nevertheless, there is a special connection to "Bein HaMetzarim," as it is explicitly stated: "Tzion shall be redeemed through justice (the study of Torah) and those who return to her through tzedakah."

May it be the will of Hashem that every man and woman does everything in their power regarding the above, and through this, hasten the fulfillment of the promise that these days will be transformed into joy and gladness, in our true and complete redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, of whom it is said: "Give Your judgments to the King, and Your righteousness to the King’s son."

Then the verse will be fulfilled: "There shall be no needy person among you, for Hashem will surely bless you," and "No longer will one teach his neighbor... for all of them will know Me, from the smallest to the greatest," and "The earth will be filled (from sea to sea and from the river to the ends of the earth) with the knowledge of Hashem."

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

The report regarding the publication of the above has just been received. It is surely still in its early stages—for the saying will be fulfilled in them and in those who receive the publication: "He who has one hundred, wants two hundred," etc.

***

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above.

It is certain that the mission regarding the above has been conveyed to him, and he will act with the **necessary** alacrity and with expansion, from sea (Atlantic) to sea (Pacific) and from the river (Hudson) to the ends of the earth.

***

The letter from some time ago and the enclosure have been received. Regarding Rashi at the beginning of Parshas Vayeshev: "The Ribono shel Olam sought..."—one should not corrupt all the seforim; and "we have not seen" is not proof.

Regarding the Likkutei Sichos—it must be in a manner, language, and explanation that is more understandable to the listeners, and there is no room at all for the nuances he writes.

The Pidyon Nefesh mentioned in the letter will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite.

***

Regarding his question as to how the spies could say "for it is stronger than us" (that they lacked faith)—it is similar to "Woe is me that I have sworn" (Bava Basra 74a).

***

The letters have been received. In response to his writing: 1) Their traveling here for Tishrei, etc.—is not relevant at all. 2) That he should study wrestling, etc., for the arena, etc.—is preposterous. It is distressing even to entertain such a thought.

***

The travel of the avreich... to here—I have already written, **and so it is decided**—regarding the lack of proper supervision here and the abundance of trials, etc., which is why there is no room for the aforementioned idea. This is in addition to the prohibition against leaving for abroad. And this is understood.

***

The place of study (education) for your daughter...—it is simple that it must be in a Chabad institution (and likewise for all children of Anash. **And this is understood**).

***

...The distress over the dormancy of the organization of the descendants is understood, and it is understood that through excuses **and the like**, nothing will be accomplished...

If the booklet (in a **well-organized** and beautiful publication) is received here before Chai Elul, I will participate in the publication costs, G-d willing, at 95 percent.

***

With the blessing that, finally, they will bring into reality, with energy and alacrity, that which has been granted from Above and with a generous eye, etc.—and the matter depends only on a true desire, *aliba d'nafsha*. And this is understood.

## 10830

10830

[B"H](#_ftn_940), 15 Tammuz, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To each and every one of the students, boys and girls, who have not yet reached the age of mitzvos — who are staying at summer camps and day camps, in every place:

May Hashem protect them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It is my strong hope that you are utilizing these summer days to recharge and strengthen your health — the health of the body together with the health of the neshamah, for they are bound to one another. And since the health of the neshamah is bound up with Torah, for it is [our life and the length of our days](#_ftn_941), and with its mitzvos — of which it is [said](#_ftn_942), "and he shall live by them" — you are surely exerting yourselves in the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos as much as is required. And surely the promise will be fulfilled: [“You have labored and you have found.”](#_ftn_943)

In particular, I wish to emphasize a point in connection with the days of "Bein HaMetzarim" that are approaching —

For you are surely aware of the nature and content of these days,

And the point is: that you should turn your attention to the special privilege that the children of Yisrael possess, a privilege that concerns the entire nation of Bnei Yisrael, according to the words of Dovid Hamelech, peace be upon him: **"Out of the mouths of babes and sucklings You have founded strength, to silence the enemy and the avenger"** — to silence even that enemy who brought us to "Bein HaMetzarim" and continues to take vengeance upon our people to this very day. The way to defeat and silence him is through "strength" (*oz*), which is [our holy Torah](#_ftn_945), which is called *oz*, and which is studied and comes forth from the mouths of babes, etc. So great is their power that, [as our Sages](#_ftn_946) of blessed memory have informed us, the world exists only for the sake of the breath of the children in the schoolhouse—a breath that is without sin—meaning, the children of Yisrael who have not yet reached the age of mitzvos.

And in continuation of the above, one must pay special attention to the words of our prophet, the vision of Yeshayah [ben](#_ftn_947) Amotz: **"Tzion shall be redeemed through justice, and those who return to her through tzedakah."** One of the interpretations of ["justice" (*mishpat*)](#_ftn_949) here is — Torah. This means that through the study of Torah and the fulfillment of its mitzvos, [and in particular](#_ftn_950) the mitzvah of tzedakah, we hasten the Geulah. The matter of tzedakah is, similar to what was said at the beginning of the letter, tzedakah for the body and tzedakah for the neshamah: Tzedakah for the body is as it sounds—giving tzedakah to the poor, or setting aside money for a tzedakah box. And tzedakah for the neshamah is to strive to have your friends and acquaintances increase in matters of Torah and mitzvos, by each and every one of you being a living example, and speaking to them about this [with words](#_ftn_951) that come from the heart.

Since my desire is great and it will be a great pleasure for me to be a partner with you in this, it is my request to give each and every one of you a coin in the currency of the country where you are located — my participation in the aforementioned act of tzedakah.

May Hashem Yisbarach bless and grant success to each and every one of you in all that has been said, and in particular in increasing your Torah study and the mitzvah of tzedakah, in a manner of "ever-increasing." Thus, even when you return from the camps to your homes and in the coming school year, may we all be blessed, you will increase in strength and health in both body and neshamah alike, and you will go [from strength](#_ftn_952) to strength in the study of Torah with persistence and diligence, and the study will lead [to the](#_ftn_953) action of fulfilling the mitzvos with beauty — and all of this with joy and a glad heart.

And very soon, may we all, together with all of Yisrael, merit that these days be transformed into joy and gladness,

In our true and complete Geulah through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, and "he shall have dominion from sea to [sea](#_ftn_955), and from the river to the ends of the earth," and "the glory of Hashem shall fill the entire earth."

With blessings for success and good tidings in all the above,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10,831

[Summer 5733]

## 10,836

10,836

B"H, 19 Tammuz, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration and the campers of Camp "Pardes Chana,"
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

I have received with pleasure the souvenir of your handiwork from Camp "Pardes Chana," and I thank you very much for your thoughtfulness.

Enclosed herewith is a general letter pertaining to each of the campers who has not yet reached the age of mitzvos, as well as a letter to the administration to do that which is incumbent upon them.

It is well known in the teachings of Chassidus regarding the Mishnah, "Two are holding onto a garment; one says, 'I found it,' and the other says, 'I found it,'" etc., that the inner lesson to be learned from this is that anyone who helps another—whether great or small—in matters of Torah and mitzvos, acquires a portion in that mitzvah and can claim before Hashem, "I found it." Furthermore, our Sages of blessed memory have already stated that one who causes another to perform a mitzvah is greater than the one who performs it himself.

And if these words apply at all times and in every season, how much more so during these days regarding which it is said, "Zion shall be redeemed with justice, and those who return to it with tzedakah," as is explained in the aforementioned letter.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.
