10,847

26 Tammuz, 5733
Brooklyn

To the Honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, etc.,
R' Shimon [Moshe]
Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your letter dated 13 Iyar, along with your seforim, *Mas'as HaMelech*: 1) [On the Rambam], 2) Novellae [on the Torah].

Many thanks for your thoughtfulness in sending them to me. I trust you will continue to do so in the future, and I thank you in advance.

Because of the fondness of the matter—and especially since the beginning of the sefer is [on this week’s parsha]—I have at least leafed through its pages, even though time does not permit the study it deserves.

In accordance with the Sages’ statement: "Do I not know that it is well... whereas through one who 'raises a difficulty... the matter is clarified of itself'" (*Bava Metzia* 84a), I will note a few comments nonetheless:

At the beginning of the sefer (on [the Rambam]) – 1, 1. Regarding not taking... exile.

I have long surmised that the enumeration of the mitzvos preceding the body of the laws in the Rambam is by the Rambam himself—and I was happy to see at the end of the Rambam in the Shulsinger edition (5707) a facsimile of the Rambam’s manuscript at the beginning of *Hilchos She'elah U'Pikadon*—**in his own handwriting**: "Two positive mitzvos: 1) the law of..."

What you wrote at the end of the second negative mitzvah, "Rather, he shall be put to death," and did not write in the fourth negative mitzvah, "Rather, he shall be exiled" (in your sefer 2, 1), is as written [in our parsha].

The reason can be explained simply: it comes to teach us that they may not take a ransom even after they have fulfilled the positive mitzvah of exiling the unintentional murderer—to return to dwell in his city. According to Rashi on the Torah, **this is** the negative mitzvah. According to the Rambam (beginning of chapter 5), who writes "in order to dwell in his city" and omits the end of the verse "to return to dwell, etc." (which is the foundation of Rashi’s explanation), it implies that he interprets the negative mitzvah as including both aspects equally.

Whether ransom ([in the case of a goring ox that killed], etc., and from this we know regarding all ransoms that it is one concept) is also one of the essentials of the obligation, or whether it comes **in place of** the death penalty—and the practical difference arises when the ox is exempt from the death penalty (see *Bava Kamma* 43a and there; *Tzafnas Paneach*, *Hilchos Terumos*—copied in the sefer *Tzafnas Paneach, Klalei HaTorah VeHaMitzvos* by Rabbi Kasher).

On the face of it: the death penalty at the hands of Heaven is incurred immediately, whereas the ransom is imposed upon him later. It is stated in the language "If a ransom is imposed" (even though it does not depend on this). The death of the ox and the death of the owner [are compared to one another]. It could be said that regarding ransom, you have nothing but the innovation explicitly stated in the verse*; the very content of the word "ransom"—from all this it is implied that the ransom comes **in place of** [the death penalty].

For the sake of sharpness, it could be said that it depends [on a dispute]: 1) Is it the value of the damager (if so, it could be said it is in place of his death at the hands of Heaven) or the value of the damaged party? 2) Is there a ransom for unintentional [killing] or not (*Bava Kamma* ibid.)? And the ruling of the Rambam is known: the value of the damaged party, and there is a ransom for unintentional [killing] (*Hilchos Nizkei Mamon*, beginning of chapter 11; ibid., chapter 10, law 13).

At the end of the aforementioned sefer: When it is impossible to return to one’s study afterward—does a mitzvah that cannot be performed by others override Torah study? See *Hilchos Talmud Torah* by the Alter Rebbe, chapter 4, section 4, regarding Torah study [for the many] (specifically)*.

**Regarding the novellae on the Torah** (104a), in the explanation of the Sages: "If the matter is as clear to you **as your sister**, who is forbidden to you, say it" (*Sanhedrin* 7b). Specifically your sister [etc.]. See *Margolios HaYam* (by Rabbi Margolios, ibid.) for several more explanations. In my humble opinion, several of them are difficult, because: 1) There are others like them [in many] prohibitions (including the explanation that since we derive a law from this, it proves that it is clear. And regarding this very point, that we do not punish based on a logical inference, he brought [in his sefer] [the Mechilta] that we also derive this from the digging of a pit). 2) Since he adds "who is forbidden to you," and from this it is not stated concisely "as the prohibition of your sister," it implies that there must be the clarity of: a) that she is your sister (as the explanation of [the Ritva]), and b) that a sister is forbidden.

However, it is not stated here whether the practical difference is [something] forbidden by law or by verse, and the like.

Likewise, one should be precise regarding his language here, "clear" (unlike *Kiddushin* 30a and *Sifrei Devarim* 6:7. And see *Torah Temimah* there). And note [the Sages who preceded] "clear... like the morning," for morning is also [from the word *bikkru* (sought/clarified)], etc.

Therefore, it seems to me, and along the lines of the *Chiddushei Aggados* (Maharal): "Clear" (from the word *berirah*—choice/clarification—between one logic and another, and both are strong, specifically). And specifically regarding the prohibition of his sister, the verse "clarifies" and rejects the strongest logic: the marriage of a man and a woman must be in the likeness of [your creation in Gan Eden of old], which "she was taken [from man]," and therefore, the priority is specifically for the marriage of his sister, who is [half] **his flesh**.

However, the example is complete when she is his sister from (the mother and) the father, and in this, there must be a clarification.

And here is another logic along the lines of the above: that the world was created in such a way that it was necessary for there to be the marriage of his sister (*Yerushalmi Yevamos*, chapter 11, halacha 1) or the marriage of his mother (Chava).

Likewise, regarding his mother—she is (a fetus) the thigh of his mother, except that he was separated afterward [and like bone] of the bones of Adam HaRishon.

But it is not entirely the same as a sister—for in practice, the existence of the world was through the marriage of a sister; a sister is half his flesh, like Adam and Chava, whereas with a mother, it is the opposite.

And note also Rashi in *Yevamos* (62b) and *Sanhedrin* (103b): "Is there any pleasure for you," etc.

And according to the above, it will be understood that there is room to say also "clear as his mother"—and like the *She'iltos* on *Mishpatim* (brought in [Margolios HaYam] there).

And note *Berachos* (58a): "He who has relations with his mother, etc., his sister, etc."

I will not elaborate further*.

See *Sefer HaMitzvos* by the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek, the mitzvos of forbidden relations—wondrous words.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

*) It could be said the opposite: since the deaths are compared to one another, it is impossible to say that the death of the owner is different, for a ransom is applicable [to it], and it must be that the ransom is a matter [in its own right].

*) [Note for later]: And regarding prayer, see *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe, *Orach Chaim*, end of section 106.

*) [Note for later]: It is difficult to understand the above from *Hilchos Talmud Torah* of the Alter Rebbe, chapter 2, section 3.

10848

10848

[B"H]( #_ftn_1018), Erev Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Menachem Av, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To each and every one of the students, boys and girls, who have not yet reached the age of Mitzvos — who are staying at day camps and summer camps, in every place,

May Hashem protect them and may they live,

Peace and Blessing!

Following [the letter]( #_ftn_1019) of the 15th of Tammuz, and as we stand before Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av and the first nine days of this month,

In which the unique aspect of the entire three weeks of *Bein HaMetzarim* is [emphasized]( #_ftn_1020) to the greatest degree —

[For because]( #_ftn_1021) of our sins we were exiled from our land and our Beis HaMikdash was destroyed,

From which it is also understood [that through]( #_ftn_1022) Teshuvah for our sins, and through the study of Torah and the fulfillment of its Mitzvos, our true and complete redemption will come immediately through Moshiach Tzidkeinu —

I come once again to remind and emphasize the special privilege in all of this that the children of Yisrael possess.

This is also understood from the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, right at the beginning of the Midrash [Eicha]( #_ftn_1023) — regarding the greatness of Yerushalayim, which was "great among the nations" (because it was "great") in its ideas — in wisdom. They bring examples of this, and within it are **seven** stories regarding the wisdom of a young boy and a young girl, and another young boy, etc., and two stories regarding the wisdom of students of the school,

Even though in the Midrash, as in all parts of the Torah, there is nothing superfluous, Heaven forbid, and every story, matter, and even a single word is precise to the ultimate degree and holy.

[They also]( #_ftn_1024) relate that there were in Yerushalayim four hundred schools for the study of [Mikra]( #_ftn_1025), four hundred schools for the study of Mishnah, and four hundred schools for the study of Talmud.

The intent of these stories is that each and every one of the children of the House of Yisrael should do everything within their power to be like them — through diligence and perseverance in the study of Torah, [and that the study]( #_ftn_1026) should lead to action and conduct according to the Torah in daily life,

And especially in these days — which remind us of the destruction and its cause (our sins) — to increase in Torah and its Mitzvos, and especially in Tzedakah, including also on the day of Tisha B'Av (regarding the things that are [permitted]( #_ftn_1027) to be studied on this day).

May it be the will that very soon we shall all merit, together with the entire Jewish people, the fulfillment of the promise of [Hashem]( #_ftn_1028) Elokim, the G-d of Yisrael, who alone performs wonders: [Tzion]( #_ftn_1029) shall be redeemed through justice (Torah) and those who return to her through Tzedakah,

[And these days]( #_ftn_1030) shall be transformed into gladness and joy.

With blessings for good tidings,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10,853

[B"H], Rosh Chodesh Menachem-Av, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Tenth Annual Convention of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad in our Holy Land, may it be built and established speedily in our days,
May Hashem grant them life,

Blessing and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received the news that the Tenth Annual Convention will take place at the end of the month of Menachem-Av. May it be the will of Hashem that it be at a propitious and successful time.

Any gathering of Jews with the goal of encouraging one another in matters of Torah and mitzvos—especially when illuminated and permeated with the light and vitality of Chassidus—is a great thing. This is all the more so when gathering for this purpose in our Holy Land, the land upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always fixed, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year.

Beyond the unique quality of the place, the time itself is also particularly auspicious and appropriate for matters that strengthen the trait of love—Ahavas Yisrael. The opposite of this was the cause and reason for the events of this period of "Bein HaMetzarim." As our Sages of blessed memory have taught, by rectifying and nullifying the cause, one nullifies the effect and hastens the fulfillment of the promise that these days will be transformed into joy and gladness.

As has been discussed many times, the women and daughters of Israel have a special merit and a special role in every good thing that has happened to our people. This begins with the Giving of the Torah, when we became a nation, which was given to the women first. As is well known, the interpretation of our Sages of blessed memory is: "Thus shall you say to the House of Yaakov"—these are the women (first, and then)—"and tell the Children of Israel"—these are the men. Likewise, regarding the contributions for the Mishkan, the women preceded the men, as it is stated: "And the men came upon the women." Similarly, regarding the affection for Eretz Yisrael, as our Sages of blessed memory stated: "The strength of women is greater than the strength of men..." (Sifrei, Pinchas 27:1). And so too regarding the end of this bitter exile, as it is said in the Midrash that it will be similar to the Exodus from Egypt, for it was in the merit of the righteous women of that generation that our forefathers were redeemed from Egypt. So too will it be in our true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

I would also like to note an additional point regarding this convention: since there will be participants from several countries and lands, including—and foremost—those who have recently arrived from that country, the good resolutions made with the appropriate vigor and their implementation will have an influence and benefit not only in our Holy Land, but will spread to the ends of the earth.

With blessings for great success and for good tidings in all the above,

**M. Schneerson**

## 10,850

10,850

## 10,859

B”H, 11 Menachem Av, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter (undated), in which you write that you cannot define yourself as a Jew, even though you were born to a Jewish mother, and you conclude with three questions:

(a) How can a person be considered as belonging to a religion when they say they do not believe in the existence of Hashem?

(b) In your opinion, Judaism lacks the element of choice, since a child born to a Jewish mother is automatically Jewish.

(c) How does a person remove themselves from the framework of the Jewish religion?

You requested a prompt response.

The answer to all three questions is one, and by way of introduction:

The Jewish religion differs from other religions in a fundamental respect: it is not based only on thought and speech, but rather on actual deed, and it encompasses the entire life of a Jew from the first moment of birth (or the conversion of a non-Jew, conversion according to Halacha) until the final moment of their life in this world.

The foundation and reason for this is that the Jewish religion is not something added to the person’s essence and being; rather, it *is* the very essence of the person.

Based on what has been said, the answer to all your questions is understood.

One who is born a human, or an animal, or a plant—it is impossible for them to change this. Any declaration on their part that they are not a human, or not an animal, or not a plant will be of no avail, even if they continue to claim that they deny their own existence or the existence of the human species, etc. It is clear that free choice is not applicable here, for free choice was given to man regarding his **conduct** in deed, speech, and thought, but not to change his own essence and being.

One more point to add to the above: even though free choice was given to man regarding his conduct and way of life, as mentioned, since his essence is in a specific, fixed, and absolute state, it is understood and simple that the more he strives to align his conduct with his essence, the greater his peace of mind, happiness in life, and tranquility of soul will be—upon which the tranquility of the body also depends. However, the Creator of man desired that man should have free choice in this (as mentioned, regarding conduct) in order that he bring his talent and potential from potential into action, to show that he is not mistaken regarding his nature and his essence, and that he is not impressed by the obstacles and trials he sometimes encounters on this path—the purpose of which is also so that he may show that he is a wise and discerning person. And furthermore, and this is also essential: that he is not ashamed of those who mock him.

I understand that there are those who would debate all of the above, but the intent of my letter is not for pilpul. On the other hand, it is my duty and also my privilege to state the truth as I see it, without any doubt in the matter.

May it be the will that you utilize your time, your ability, and all your potential to align your daily conduct with your soul, which is, in the well-known [expression](#_ftn_1061), "literally a part of Hashem from above." And our Sages, of blessed [memory](#_ftn_1062), have already said: "There is nothing that can stand before the will."

With blessings for good tidings regarding all of the above.

10872

10872

[B"H], 15th of Av, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letters...

As we stand on the day regarding which it is said, "**From this point on, one who adds, adds** — one who adds nights to the days to engage in Torah will add life to his life,"

And the study of Torah (and in particular, the engagement in Torah) and the addition to it, is what leads to action, to the fulfillment of the mitzvos and an increase therein, including an increase in quality — *hiddur* (beautification) in the fulfillment of the mitzvos.

This is also the theme of the current time, as we have entered the "Seven Weeks of Consolation" following the tragedy of "because of our sins we were exiled from our land, etc.," and an increase in nullifying the cause (our sins) adds to the nullification of the effect (our exile).

This is also emphasized by the fact that Chazal connect this day and its theme (adding to Torah study at night) with the theme of Tisha B'Av — by providing a *siman* (sign) for the matter (and a *siman* in Torah is itself Torah and instruction): *Kumi* until *Shichvi* — meaning, from the time of saying *Kumi Roni* at night (in Megillas Eichah) on Tisha B'Av, until the time of saying *Shichvi* until the morning (in Megillas Ruth) on Shavuos, one must engage in *Kumi Roni Balailah* — to increase in Torah study at night.

And the connection between Tisha B'Av and the 15th of Av is emphasized not only in a *siman* (for all generations), but also in the establishment of the 15th of Av as a Yom Tov for the first time. This occurred in the fortieth year of the generation of the desert, when they saw the moon in its fullness on the 15th of Av — they knew that the decree of "the men of the desert shall die" (which was decreed during the first weeping of Tisha B'Av) had been annulled, and they established it as a Yom Tov, as recounted in the Midrash.

The aforementioned (that "from this point on — one adds") is also hinted at by the fact that Yisroel count by the moon, one of the reasons for which is that the history of Yisroel consists of ascents and descents, like the moon, and they are destined to be renewed like it. And when the moon stands in its fullness on the 15th of the month, its light is at its peak and perfection. And this is especially true on the 15th of Av — which comes after the miraculous descent of Tisha B'Av —

Which is why there were no days as festive for Yisroel as the 15th of Av and Yom Kippur —

This hints at and emphasizes the fullness and perfection of the life of every individual among Yisroel through Torah, which is light, and the mitzvah, which is a candle, brought about by Torah.

And *l'fum tza'ara* (of Tisha B'Av) *agra* — a miraculous addition and ascent.

May it be Hashem's will that on this day of the 15th of Av and "from this point on" — and especially in this year, the seventh year, a *Shabbos* to Hashem, and a preparation for the year and theme of *Hakhel* (assembling the people, the men, the women, and the children, etc., so that they may hear, etc., all the words of this Torah) — every one of us, within all of Yisroel, will be aroused to add to our Torah and mitzvos, both regarding ourselves and in influencing others.

And through adding light in the darkness of the night and the exile (which is called night) — for even a little light pushes away much darkness, and how much more so an addition of light, light in its fullness —

We will merit, very soon, the fulfillment of the prophecy: "He has set an end to darkness," and "the night shall shine like the day,"

In our true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, from darkness to a great light.

With respect and blessing,

**M. Schneerson**

***

I hereby acknowledge receipt of the letters and the report, and thank you.

With respect and blessings for great success in the establishment of the institution and its expansion in both quantity and quality, very soon.

## 10,873

15 Menachem Av, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yosef K. Landis

Shalom u’Bracha!

I thank you for your thoughtfulness in sending me the journal "Yidish" under your esteemed editorship, which I naturally found interesting to look through. I hope that you will also send the subsequent issues.

I trust you will not take it amiss that I begin this letter with the observation that while the content is generally more important than the "vessel"—in this case, the language—it is certainly true that language carries a special significance and impact. Therefore, even if for various reasons the journal is published in English, there ought to have been at least a brief summary of the articles in Yiddish, as is the practice in many journals.

In continuation of the above, I would also like to express the wish that the content of the journal "Yidish" should be permeated with the spirit of authentic Yiddishkeit, and truth, after all, precludes compromise.

It is, of course, known to me that there is a fear in certain circles of not stating the full truth so as not to alienate, or, as they put it, "not to drive people away." Yet, precisely in recent years, one sees that the youth are not afraid of the truth, provided they have the feeling that one is telling them things as they are and that one is committed to the truth. And certainly, as in the case of any book or journal, one is highly interested in attracting the youth.

With respect and wishes to hear good news regarding all of the above.

## 10,774

10,774

B”H, after the fifteenth of Av, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter was received, and may the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the requests of your heart for the good.

As we have just passed the day which, according to the words of our Sages, of blessed memory, holds special significance for the daughters of Yisrael—particularly regarding preparation for family life, the conduct of the home, and so on—as our Sages recount in their Mishnah: that on the fifteenth of Av, “the daughters of Yisrael would go out and dance in the vineyards, and what would they say? ... ‘A woman who fears [יראת](#_ftn_1114) Hashem, she shall be praised’” (end of Maseches Taanis, see there at length).

Just as with every single matter in the Torah, there is a general lesson here for every daughter of Yisrael and for all generations. This, of course, applies to every one of the women of Yisrael who are married and mothers of daughters: to strive as much as possible in one’s own chinuch, and in the chinuch of one’s daughters, upon the foundation of taharas hakodesh and yiras Hashem.

[The goal is] for every daughter of Yisrael to be worthy of the title [“Akeres HaBayis”](#_ftn_1115), which is a privilege and responsibility without compare. And the foundation and essence of this is: **A woman who fears Hashem, she shall be praised.**

And as with all matters in the Torah, which is called **Toras Chesed and Toras Chaim**—a [lesson](#_ftn_1116) for life, for day-to-day life—this draws down the kindnesses of Hashem in this matter, and in general, in all that is needed.

Furthermore, and this too is essential: since the Torah is Toras Chesed, it is also understood that everything it demands and every responsibility it places upon us, including what has been mentioned, is [preceded](#_ftn_1117) by the granting of the strength and fortitude to carry out the mission and responsibility in practice, in their entirety, and with joy. [And there](#_ftn_1118) is nothing that can stand before the will.

May it be His will that you share good news regarding all that has been mentioned, including good tidings regarding the contents of your letter.

With blessings for success and for good news.

## 10880

B"H, Motzaei Shabbos, 20 Menachem Av, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Oholei Torah 
who are studying the shechita of large cattle (gasos),
May Hashem keep them alive,

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter requesting a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh*, and at an auspicious time, your names will be mentioned at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for the good.

It is surely known to you what is brought in the *poskim*, and especially from our Rebbes, the *Nesi'im*, who were *poskim* in both the *nigleh* of Torah (as we see from the *Shulchan Aruch* of the Alter Rebbe and the *Shu"t* of the Tzemach Tzedek) and *poskim* in the *nistar* of Torah: that a *shochet* must be exceedingly G-d-fearing. And since responsibility is placed upon one from Above, this itself is proof that the strength to carry it out has been granted; it is understood that the magnitude of the merit corresponds to the magnitude of the responsibility.

May it be the will of Hashem that the statement "He does not slaughter (*shachat*) except by drawing (*mashach*)" be fulfilled in each and every one of you, including according to the interpretation in *Toras HaChassidus* — to draw the *nefesh habehamis* and elevate it, until the verse, "The spirit of man is that which ascends upward," applies to it. This is as the concept of *meshichah* (drawing) is explained in *maamarei d'ach* on the verse, "Draw me (*moshcheni*), we will run after You," and see also *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, page 37d.

We are now approaching the month of Elul, the month of mercy.

With blessings for constant ascent in the study of Torah and the performance of its *mitzvos* with *hiddur*, and for good tidings in all the aforementioned.

## 10,886

10,891

[B"H], days of the month of Elul, the month of mercy, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students—both male and female—who participated in the Tzedakah campaign,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom and blessing!

I was pleased to learn [that they fulfilled] my request to act as shluchim for a mitzvah by distributing my Tzedakah, and that they connected this with the study of Torah, adding Tzedakah of their own.

And although in any matter of a mitzvah that a Jew performs, there is no place for thanks from flesh and blood—for the very fulfillment of the mitzvah and the carrying out of the will of Hashem Yisbarach is the greatest reward and true happiness, [as our Sages of blessed memory stated]: "The reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself"—

Yet, there is a place to express thanks for the fulfillment of the mission, and for this I express my great thanks to each and every one of them.

On this occasion, since we have entered the month of Elul, this is the place to mention once again the special quality of the days of this month, the month of mercy, which serves as preparation for Rosh Hashanah and for the entire new year that is approaching us for good, according to the [well-known explanation] of the Alter Rebbe:

It is analogous to a king who, before arriving in the city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to go out to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone, etc. Afterward, when he arrives at his royal palace, no one may enter except by permission, and even then, only the elite of the people and the select few.

This is the concept of all the days of the month of Elul, when the King of kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, declares and makes known that He is present "in the field," and each and every one can approach Him, without any conditions, difficulties, or special efforts, etc.

Seemingly, one might ask: what is this matter of approaching the King in the field, since [He has no bodily form] and is not a body, Heaven forbid, [as the verse states]: "For you saw no image, etc."?

The Alter Rebbe continues to explain that this matter of approaching is connected to tefillah.

For tefillah in general, and specifically during these days, is in the manner [that it is said]: **"May Hashem shine His face upon you,"** face to face; the one who prays stands before the face of the King, as in the aforementioned analogy.

And he adds that in order for this to have actual existence and hold, one must engage in matters of Torah, Tzedakah, and kindness.

May it be the will that each and every one of you goes [from strength to strength] in all matters of goodness and holiness, Torah and mitzvos, and that you be a source of pride, glory, and true nachas to your parents, teachers, and educators—may they live—and that you utilize the auspicious days of this month to their fullest, and be blessed with a good inscription and sealing for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

With the blessing of a good inscription and sealing,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 18 Elul

18 Elul, 5733
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,
Peace and blessing!

In this time of preparation for Rosh Hashanah—

The day when Adam HaRishon was created, through which the entire creation was completed and perfected;

The day that is the beginning and the "head" of the entire year, which means that Rosh Hashanah teaches, provides guidance, and sets the direction for all the days of the year—

I wish to dwell here on one lesson and instruction: the central place that man occupies as the "crown" of the entire creation, and that the perfection of the entire creation depends upon him, as mentioned above.

***

Rosh Hashanah teaches and reminds everyone of the immense *kochos* that have been placed within him—*kochos* that give him the possibility not only to bring himself to the fullest perfection, but also to influence, lead, and—if necessary—transform the world around him.

Along with this comes the tremendous responsibility not to underestimate the *kochos* that one has been given, and to utilize them to the fullest extent regarding oneself and regarding the world around one.

The very fact that Rosh Hashanah, the day of judgment for the entire creation, was established not on the first day of creation when **everything** was created *me'ayin l'yesh*, but rather on the day when man was created, proves that the judgment of the entire creation depends upon him.

From this, it is understood that he has been given the *kochos* to influence and lead the creation.

All of this is clearly brought out and further emphasized by our Sages, of blessed memory, in their narrative (which is a part of Torah—an instruction) regarding the first man, Adam HaRishon, on the first Rosh Hashanah, the day of his creation: As soon as Adam HaRishon was created, he looked around and contemplated the creation, and recognized that this is *ma'aseh Hashem*—the creation of the Ribono shel Olam. Immediately thereafter, he called out (and accomplished in all created beings), "Come, let us go, you and I... and crown as King over us the One who created us." This means that immediately upon his creation, man was given the immense *koach* to elevate himself and the entire creation to the highest level of perfection—to connect with the Creator through the recognition that the Ribono shel Olam is the **Creator** and the *Melech HaOlam*, the King of the world; a recognition that expresses itself immediately in a fundamental and concrete way.

And as explained in many places in our Torah—according to the creation of Adam HaRishon and the details therein—so too is it with every Jew.

***

From the above follows a highly important point, which is actually self-evident but must be emphasized, especially in these times: that the aforementioned awareness in general, and the subsequent fulfillment of it regarding the great *zechus* and responsibility, is not a "private" matter that concerns the individual alone. For, as stated, the task of **every** individual is not only to elevate himself to the necessary height, but also to elevate his entire surroundings, until the perfection of the entire creation is realized—the very reason for which he was created and given immense *kochos*.

And regarding the excuse that influencing and accomplishing in one's surroundings can be done by others, and that utilizing his *kochos* is only his own private matter—Torah tells us that Adam HaRishon was created *yechidi* (as a single individual) in order to teach that everyone is like Adam HaRishon, a single individual who is the entire world.

From this, it is also understood that just as Adam HaRishon had no one to whom to delegate his mission to accomplish in the world—the "Come, let us crown as King over us the One who created us"—so too regarding everyone in his mission.

And when one arrives at the recognition of this responsibility and *zechus*, all the obstacles and difficulties one encounters on the way become insignificant and small. For when one considers how far-reaching every action of every individual is—not only for himself, but for the entire *klal*, up to the final goal of the entire creation—what weight do all difficulties have in comparison to that!

***

Like many other matters in Torah, which are issued in very concise language, the above is also brought out in a few words in the *Torah Shebichtav*, together with a brief explanation in the *Torah Sheba'al Peh*.

Immediately upon the first verse in the Torah, which includes within it the entire creation: **"In the beginning, Hashem created the heavens and the earth"**—"In the beginning, the Ribono shel Olam created the heaven (including all heavenly beings) and the earth (including all earthly beings)"—the *Torah Sheba'al Peh* explains that the first word, **Bereishis**, contains the indication: **"For the sake of the Torah, which is called *reishis* (beginning), and for the sake of Israel, who are called *reishis*."** This means to say that the entire world was created, and is constantly being renewed, enlivened, and perfected, through a Jew conducting himself according to the Torah.

***

This is, as mentioned above, one of the fundamental instructions of Rosh Hashanah as the "head" of the entire year—in the sense of leading all the days of the year just as the head leads all the limbs of the body—that a Jew must be permeated every day with the consciousness that his every **ma'aseh** (deed), and even **dibbur** (speech), and even **machshavah** (thought), concerns not only himself and his immediate environment, but also the entire scope of the world, up to the highest worlds. At the same time, he must also remember that as a **"branch of My planting, the work of My hands,"** he receives the fullest possibility to fulfill his task as it was given to Adam HaRishon, **"the handiwork of the Holy One, blessed be He"** (whom G-d formed with His own hands, *kivayachol*)—the task to bring himself and the world around him to the ultimate level of their perfection,

And he receives the possibility, as the Ribono shel Olam gives in general, and specifically on this day and in this time when **"G-d saw all that He had made, and behold, it was very good"**—from His full, open, holy, and generous hand.

With the blessing of *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year,

**Menachem Schneerson**

## 10891

[B"H](http://www.chabad.org/1221), after the Shabbos of Chai Elul, the Year of Seven, 5733.
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed organizers of kosher education in every place,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby present my earnest request and proposal:

In connection with these days of favor and mercy, and based on the words of Chazal regarding the immense importance of the *hevel* of children—for whose sake the world exists—I propose that on one of the days of Selichos (if possible, on the first day), you gather boys and girls who are under Bar/Bas Mitzvah age. Please endeavor **energetically** to ensure the number of participants is as large as possible.

Explain to them—according to their level of understanding—that this is the (beginning of the) week of Rosh Hashanah, a time of appropriate preparation for Rosh Hashanah. (At that time, everyone accepts upon themselves the kingship of Hashem for the entire year, to observe His mitzvos, etc., and Hashem blesses all of Bnei Yisrael with a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.)

Especially since this is a time of *segulah*, as explained by the Alter Rebbe: during these days, the Holy One, Blessed be He, is, as it were, like a king who is in the field, at which time anyone who wishes to greet Him is permitted to do so, and He receives everyone with a welcoming countenance.

Therefore, I request that everyone participating in this gathering say together, with *chayus*:

*Torah tzivah lanu Moshe, morashah kehillas Yaakov.*
*Shema Yisrael Hashem Elokeinu Hashem Echad.*
*Baruch shem kvod malchuso l'olam va'ed.*
*Avinu Malkeinu, Avinu Atah. Avinu Malkeinu, ein lanu melech elah Atah. Avinu Malkeinu, rachem aleinu. Avinu Malkeinu, chaneinu va'aneinu, ki ein banu ma'asim; aseh imanu tzedakah vachesed l'ma'an shimcha hagadol, v'hoshi'einu.*

Afterward, let each of the organizers explain to their class (or have one person explain aloud to everyone):

The Baal Shem Tov said: Every Yid comes into this material world with a specific *shlichus* of *Torah Ohr*—Torah light—and with this *shlichus* of Torah and mitzvos, he goes about and travels, whether in his own city or wherever and for whatever occasion he travels.

And we wish for each one that they fulfill this *shlichus* in its proper time and with success; and that they be blessed with a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

My request is twofold: that afterward, you give each child two coins. One is a **gift** from me—with the suggestion (but **not** as a condition) that they give it to *tzedakah*; and the second—with my request that they entrust it to you, as my *shluchim*, for *tzedakah*.

With respect and with great and heartfelt thanks for the above, and with a blessing for success in the above, and for good tidings in this, and with a blessing for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

It is good and proper to also do all of the above on one of the days of Aseres Yemei Teshuvah, except that instead of the concept of the "King in the field," explain to them that regarding these days it is said: "Seek Hashem when He is found, call upon Him when He is near," as explained by the Alter Rebbe, that this is like the analogy of the light drawing near to the spark—the *nefesh elokis* that is within each and every one of Bnei Yisrael.

And I believe [we also spoke] then that he should do everything that depends on him to become a focal point to which all those visiting Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established—will turn, without any formalities or office protocol, etc. He should influence them in necessary and good matters, especially those pertaining to the holiness of [the Land]—upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year—and the holiness of the people, who are a holy [nation] in the land, and a [nation] that is one in the land. This is according to the [explanation] of our *Rabbeinu HaZaken* that they draw down "One" (and holiness) even into mundane matters. All of this is founded upon the holiness of the Torah, which is the Torah of truth, which rejects all matters of compromise. In all of this, it is forbidden to evaluate one’s strengths as less than what they are in truth, as per the words of [my father-in-law, the Rebbe]: Just as one must know one’s own shortcomings, one must also know one’s own strengths.

May it be the will of Hashem that very soon I will hear good news regarding the above as well.

## 10,934

10,934

[5733]

In order to succeed in any endeavor, one must have self-respect, and there must also be a sense of respect from the people upon whom that success depends—those who need to assist in the matter. This is all the more true in the world of business, where a person’s character is of the utmost importance.

**Everyone** knows that he is **in the middle** of his studies toward receiving a PhD.

If, **Heaven forbid**, he were to abandon these studies now, it would be interpreted by **many** people (who will also say this to his father-in-law, *sh’y*, and to his wife, *t’y*, etc.) as an indication that he lacks the drive to persevere in a matter that requires effort—that he is someone who starts things but does not finish them. He would not be ashamed that everyone would know this, because he lacks self-respect; and since he found a "convenient excuse"—to enter his father-in-law’s business—he abandoned everything just to be rid of the aforementioned effort, **and so on**. Therefore, it is **imperative** that he continue his studies until he receives the PhD. **Afterward**—if he wishes to enter his father-in-law’s business—he can **then** discuss the matter with his father-in-law.

As for coming here to speak with me about this in person now:

1) It would be of no use, as my opinion is clear, as stated above.

2) There is a risk of harm—for it is better that he decide this for himself, as stated above, rather than people saying that he wanted to quit in the middle, but that **I** pressured him not to do so. And this is clear.

## 10,940

## 10,950

10,950

## 10,951

The doctor has surely told her that **many, many** people are in a similar state to the one she describes (where they feel that they have done something without proper care, that their hands are not clean, and therefore they must wash them again, etc.).

If one makes an effort to pay **no attention at all** to these thoughts—**not** to fight them, but rather to **divert one's mind** from them as much as possible—they weaken over time until they pass completely. When the urge to wash her hands arises, for example: she should **not** make an issue of it. Rather, she should either tell herself that there is no substance to this urge, or she should wash her hands and **immediately** busy herself with something that has no connection to any of this.

Among the reasons for the aforementioned state is a general weakness in health; strengthening it will also help alleviate the situation.

Yes, to **hasten** the correction, consult a friendly doctor and follow his instructions.

Check the mezuzos.

The names, and I will mention them at the holy gravesite.

10,952

[5733]

Regarding the worries you write about – you should **divert** your attention from all of this **as much as possible**; that is, do not even "fight against them," but rather pay them no mind – **as much as possible**.

However, you should organize your daily life precisely according to the **Shulchan Aruch**.

You must have a **fixed** and orderly job (work), and in your free time (at least part of it), establish fixed times for Torah study with a *chavrusa*.

Give *tzedakah* **bli neder** every weekday morning (a few coins).

Establish your residence in **Eretz Yisrael** [it would be best – in a religious *kibbutz*, if possible].

Have your *tefillin* and *mezuzos* checked.

I will mention you at the *tziyun*.

## 10,953

10,953

[5733]

One should exert effort in matters of parnassah by observing Shabbos and Yom Tov **literally**, and by utilizing the knowledge (at least to some extent) and acquaintances one possesses—or at the very least, one of these.

## 10,954

10,954

[5733]

(1) Since he is a student (who is affiliated) with a yeshiva, he must study the tractate of the yeshiva—at least for a portion of his study time.

(2) Regarding his participation in the invention business: If those involved in this and the inventors are reliable (they understand such commerce, at least some of them are also investing their own money, they are not "dreiers" [hustlers/con artists], and the like), he may also participate. However, the magnitude of the wonder... [the conclusion is missing]

## 10,955

10,955

[5733]

Regarding [what you wrote](#_ftn_1300) – it requires further study whether he can protect his product with a patent,

And without such protection – whether he can withstand the competition from those who are already engaged in this, and whose business and livelihood have been in this field **for some time**.

And he should make his decision in accordance with the clarification **of this** (in addition to the above).

## 10,950

10,950

[5733]

Please make known and inform me how much money is needed for this – **and an estimate** of when they will be able to repay it – and there is room to say that it might be possible to arrange a loan for them based on this, or a portion of it.

## 10,957

10,957

[5733]

Regarding:

1) A partnership — if this is not a one-time matter but for a duration of time, there is room for this, provided that they get along with one another and have trust in one another.

2) Selling the property — only if you will immediately invest the money in something that is better than real estate; if there is doubt, it is not advisable.

3) Royalties — renew your efforts in this. If it depends on difficulties, it is not worth the effort to return the file to Switzerland, and you should continue in England.

4) A shidduch for your daughter, may she live — it is not advisable to make the location of their residence after the wedding a condition (and it is appropriate to leave this to the chosson), and you should show interest both abroad and in Eretz Yisrael.

I will mention this at the Tziyun for the aforementioned.

## 10,958

[1973]

You should request that the details of her position be **written down** (so that there will be no disagreements about this later). And if you **verify** that this does not constitute an encroachment on anyone else’s territory, you should accept the offer, and may it be with *siyata d’shmaya* (heavenly assistance) and *hatzlacha* (success).

Regarding her daughter ... *tichyeh* — you must make an effort concerning a suitable *shidduch* in an appropriate manner.

I will mention it at the *tziyun*.

## 10,860

[5733]

As long as there is no assurance of a better livelihood, one should not leave the one that already exists.

As is evident from the above, it is difficult for him to succeed in negotiating with his employer for a salary increase on his own; perhaps he should attempt to do so through appropriate intermediaries.

I will mention this at the Tziyun.

## 10,862

10,862

[5733]

**Simply** — through **hisbonenus**, and as you are accustomed (according to what you wrote) **in all** of your affairs [with a full heart](#_ftn_1305) and also with [intensity](#_ftn_1306) — regarding the matter of hashgacha pratis by Hashem, **Who** directs the world at every moment (it is only that He desired that a person **should do** what is dependent upon him through the way of nature, **and not** that he should worry in his thoughts). If so, **the entire** foundation for any worry whatsoever, or [strain](#_ftn_1307), or the like, is nullified.

## 10,863

10,863

[5733]

At the beginning of our acquaintance, you were **extremely** worried about: 1) A *shidduch* for your daughter, may she live; 2) How to rescue your brother and his family, may they live, from Romania; 3) Whether you would be able to support yourself without needing help from others, *chas v’shalom*.

Since all of these are fundamental matters, **etc.**,

And in all of them—things were arranged (and whatever is lacking in the completeness of the above—it is possible that it will be filled),

So how can you say that you have no basis for *bitachon*?!

Regarding your questions:

a) It is good (and also for your health) that you continue to work.

b) You should conduct yourself according to your doctor’s instructions.

I will mention you at the *tziyun* regarding the above.

## 10,970

10,970

[5733]

Hashem helps everyone to perform [teshuvah](#_ftn_1326), and the matter depends **only on the will** of the person.

I will mention [you] at the holy gravesite.
